میں ایک نفیس نظم لکھی ہے اس میں وہ مسائل نہیں لیے جو قابل اعتراض تھے اور حمودی کی نظم پر میں نے چند مسائل کا اضافہ کیا ہے۔ ( اس نظم میں مسائل کی مجموعی تعداد میں ہے ) یہ نظم میں نے اپنے حاشیہ ردالمختار باب النفقۃ ج ۲ ص ۷۲۶ میں ذکر کی ہے۔
اعتراض و جواب: علامہ ابن نجیم رحمہ اللہ البحر الرائق، کتاب القضاء ج ۲ ص ۲۶۹ میں تحریر فرماتے ہیں: ۶ " پس اگر کوئی شبہ کرے کہ مشائخ کے لیے مقلد ہوتے ہوئے یہ کیسے جائز ہو گیا کہ وہ امام اعظم کے علاوہ دوسرے کے قول پر فتوی دیں؟ تو میں کہوں گا کہ یہ اشکال خود مجھے عرصہ تک رہا ہے میری سمجھ میں اس کا کچھ جواب نہیں آتا تھا مگر اب اکابر کے کلام سے ایک جواب میری سمجھ میں آیا ہے اور وہ یہ ہے کہ علماء نے ہمارے ائمہ سے یہ بات نقل کی ہے کہ کسی کے لیے جائز نہیں کہ ہمارے قول پر فتوی دے جب تک وہ یہ نہ جان لے کہ ہم نے کہاں سے بات کہی ہے ۔ اور فتاوی سراجیہ (۹۷) میں تو یہاں تک منقول ہے کہ عصام بن یوسف (۱۰۰) جو امام اعظم کے خلاف فتویٰ دیتے تھے تو اس کا سبب یہی تھا وہ بکثرت امام صاحب کے قول کے خلاف فتویٰ دیتے تھے کیونکہ ان کے علم میں امام صاحب کے اقوال کی دلیل نہیں ہوتی تھی اور دوسروں کے اقوال کی دلیل ان کے لیے واضح ہوتی تھی اس لیے وہ دوسروں کے قول پر فتوی دیتے تھے۔" جواب کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ حنفی کے لیے امام ابو حنیفہ رحمہ اللہ کے قول پر فتوی دینا ضروری ہے مگر شرط یہ ہے کہ اس کو امام صاحب کے قول کی دلیل معلوم ہو ورنہ دوسرے کے قول کو اختیار کرے گا پس جو مشائخ امام صاحب کے علاوہ دوسرے کے قول پر فتوی دیتے تھے تو اس کی وجہ یہ ہوتی تھی کہ ان کو امام صاحب کے قول کی دلیل معلوم نہیں ہوتی تھی ۔ کیا فتویٰ دینے کے لیے مفتی بہ قول کی دلیل معلوم ہونا ضروری ہے؟ پس میں (ابن نجیم ) کہتا ہوں کہ یہ شرط اکابر کے زمانہ میں تھی۔ اب ہمارے زمانہ میں فتویٰ دینے کے لیے صرف مسئلہ کا اچھی طرح محفوظ ہونا کافی ہے جیسا کہ قنیہ وغیرہ میں ہے۔ میہ صاحب بحر علامہ ابن نجیم رحمہ اللہ کی عبارت ہے ۱۲

پس امام صاحب کے قول پر فتونی دینا نہ صرف جائز ہے بلکہ واجب ہے اگر چہ ہمیں معلوم نہ ہو که امام صاحب نے وہ بات کہاں سے فرمائی ہے۔ بناء علی هاذا حادی قدی میں جس قول کو صحیح قرار دیا ہے یعنی قوت دلیل کے معتبر ہونے کا قول تو وہ اسی شرط پر مبنی ہے مگر اب علماء نے طے کر دیا ہے کہ امام اعظم کے قول پر فتویٰ دیا جائے گا ( دلیل جاننے کی شرط ختم کر دی ہے ) تو اس سے یہ نتیجہ نکلتا ہے کہ ہمارے ذمہ امام صاحب کے قول پر فتوی دینا واجب ہے۔ اگر چہ مشائخ نے امام صاحب کے قول کے خلاف فتونی دیا ہو ۔ کیونکہ ان حضرات نے امام صاحب کے قول کے خلاف فتوئی اس لیے دیا تھا کہ ان کے حق میں امام اعظم کے قول پر فتوی دینے کی شرط مفقود تھی اور وہ شرط امام صاحب کے قول کی دلیل سے واقف ہونا تھی رہے ہم تو امام صاحب کے قول پر فتوی دیں گے اگر چہ ہمیں ان کے قول کی دلیل معلوم نہ ہو ۔ ( کیونکہ دلیل جاننے کی شرط ہمارے لیے باقی نہیں رہی) اور محقق ابن الہمام رحمہ اللہ نے متعدد مواقع میں مشائخ پر جہاں انہوں نے صاحبین کے قول پر فتوی دیا ہے یہ کہ کر رد کیا ہے کہ امام صاحب کے قول سے عدول صرف دلیل کی کمزوری کی صورت میں کیا جا سکتا ہے ( علامہ کی اس بات کا صاف مطلب یہ ہے کہ ہر جگہ امام صاحب کے قول پر فتویٰ دینا ضروری ہے اور اگر کوئی شبہ کرے کہ علامہ نے تو دلیل کا بھی اعتبار کیا ہے کہ جب امام صاحب کی دلیل قوی ہو تو اس پر فتوی دینا ضروری ہے دلیل ضعیف ہو تو اس سے عدول کیا جا سکتا ہے اس صورت میں امام صاحب کے قول پر فتویٰ دینا ضروری نہیں ہے تو ابن نجیم اس کا جواب دیتے ہیں) لیکن علامہ ابن الہمام دلیل میں غور و فکر کرنے کی اہلیت رکھتے تھے (اس لیے ان کے حق میں دلیل کا اعتبار ہے ) اور جو لوگ دلیل میں غور و فکر کرنے کی اہلیت نہیں رکھتے ان کے ذمہ امام صاحب کے قول پر فتویٰ دینا لازم ہے۔
اہلبیت نظر :
اور یہاں اہمیت کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ آدمی فقہ کو خوب جانتا ہو فقہاء کے اقوال کے درمیان
امتیاز کر سکتا ہو اور اس میں بعض اقوال کو بعض پر ترجیح دینے کی پوری صلاحیت ہو ۔
حادی کی بات سے صاحب بحر کے مدعی پر اعتراض وارد ہو سکتا تھا اس لیے وہ اس عبارت کا جواب دے
رہے ہیں ۔ ۱۲
Commentary on the section of the Mufti: A fine poem has been written; it does not include those issues that were objectionable, and I have added several issues to Hamudi's poem. (The total number of issues in this poem is such.) I have mentioned this poem in my gloss on Radd al-Muhtar, chapter of Nafaqah, vol. 2, p. 726.
Objection and answer: Allamah Ibn Nujaym (may Allah have mercy on him) writes in al-Bahr al-Raiq, Kitab al-Qada, vol. 2, p. 269: "If someone doubts how it became permissible for the mashayikh, while being muqallids, to give fatwa based on the saying of someone other than Imam A'zam? Then I say: This difficulty persisted with me for a long time; I could not find any answer to it in my understanding. But now, from the words of the elders, an answer has come to my understanding, and it is this: The scholars have narrated from our Imams that no one is permitted to give fatwa on our saying until he knows from where we have said it. And in Fatawa Sirajiyyah (97), it is even narrated that 'Isam ibn Yusuf (100), who used to give fatwa contrary to Imam A'zam, the reason was this: he frequently gave fatwa contrary to Imam Sahib's saying because he did not know the evidence for Imam Sahib's statements, whereas the evidence for others' statements was clear to him, so he gave fatwa based on others' statements." The gist of the answer is that it is necessary for a Hanafi to give fatwa based on Imam Abu Hanifah's (may Allah have mercy on him) saying, but on condition that he knows the evidence for Imam Sahib's saying; otherwise, he will adopt the saying of another. So the mashayikh who gave fatwa based on others' sayings apart from Imam Sahib, the reason was that they did not know the evidence for Imam Sahib's saying. Is it necessary for giving fatwa to know the evidence of the mufta bih saying? So I (Ibn Nujaym) say that this condition was in the time of the elders. In our time, for giving fatwa, only memorizing the issue well is sufficient, as is stated in Qunyah and others. This is the statement of Sahib al-Bahr, Allamah Ibn Nujaym.

Commentary on the drawing of the Mufti: So giving fatwa based on Imam Sahib's saying is not only permissible but obligatory, even if we do not know from where Imam Sahib said that. Based on this, in [Hadi Qadi?], the saying that he has deemed correct, i.e., the saying that strength of evidence is considered, is based on that condition. But now the scholars have decided that fatwa will be given based on Imam A'zam's saying (they have removed the condition of knowing the evidence). So from this it follows that it is obligatory upon us to give fatwa based on Imam Sahib's saying, even if the mashayikh gave fatwa contrary to Imam Sahib's saying. Because those people gave fatwa contrary to Imam Sahib's saying only because the condition for giving fatwa based on Imam A'zam's saying was missing in their case, and that condition was being aware of the evidence of Imam Sahib's saying. As for us, we will give fatwa based on Imam Sahib's saying, even if we do not know the evidence for his saying (because the condition of knowing the evidence no longer remains for us). And Muhaqqiq Ibn al-Humam (may Allah have mercy on him) in many places where the mashayikh gave fatwa based on the saying of the Sahibayn, he refuted them by saying that deviation from Imam Sahib's saying can only be done in case of weakness of evidence. (The clear meaning of Allamah's statement is that in every place it is necessary to give fatwa based on Imam Sahib's saying. And if someone doubts that Allamah also considered evidence, that when Imam Sahib's evidence is strong, it is necessary to give fatwa based on it, and if the evidence is weak, deviation from it can be done—in that case, giving fatwa based on Imam Sahib's saying is not necessary—then Ibn Nujaym answers this). But Allamah Ibn al-Humam possessed the ability to ponder over evidence (so for him, considering evidence is valid), and for those who do not possess the ability to ponder over evidence, it is necessary upon them to give fatwa based on Imam Sahib's saying.

Ahl al-Nazar: And here the meaning of importance is that a person knows fiqh well, can distinguish between the sayings of jurists, and has full ability to prefer some sayings over others.
The statement of Hadi could have given rise to an objection against the claimant of Sahib al-Bahr, so he is answering that statement.
Source pages p. 75

Commentary
This passage addresses a central methodological rule in Hanafi usul al-iftaa: the necessity for a mufti to know the evidence (dalil) behind the ruling he issues. The discussion opens with Ibn Nujaym relating a doubt: how can the mashayikh (later Hanafi scholars), who are muqallids (followers) of Imam Abu Hanifa, validly issue fatwas based on opinions other than the Imam's? Ibn Nujaym explains that this was permissible only when the mufti did not know the evidence for Imam Abu Hanifa's opinion; in such a case, he could follow another opinion whose evidence was clear to him. However, Ibn Nujaym then notes that this condition (knowing the dalil) applied in the time of the earlier elders. In his own time (and by extension, ours), it is sufficient for a mufti to simply have memorized the ruling well—the requirement to know the underlying evidence has been lifted. This is a critical shift: later Hanafi scholars collectively decided that the obligation is to follow Imam Abu Hanifa's opinion even without knowing its evidence. The passage then addresses Ibn al-Humam's position, which appears to reintroduce the consideration of evidence. Ibn al-Humam held that deviation from Imam Abu Hanifa's opinion is only permissible when his evidence is weak, and this requires the ability to critically examine evidence (al-nazar). Ibn Nujaym reconciles this by noting that Ibn al-Humam himself possessed such ability, but for those who do not, following Imam Abu Hanifa's opinion is obligatory unconditionally. The final paragraph defines 'ahl al-nazar' as those who have deep knowledge of fiqh and can distinguish and weigh different scholarly opinions. The overall ruling is clear: for the general mufti today, it is wajib to give fatwa according to Imam Abu Hanifa's opinion, regardless of knowledge of the evidence. This is the relied-upon position in the later Hanafi school.

Key Terms
مقلد (muqallid): A follower who adheres to a particular madhhab without independent reasoning.
دلیل (dalil): The evidence or proof from Qur'an, Sunnah, or other sources that supports a legal ruling.
قوت دلیل (quwwat al-dalil): The strength of the evidence underlying a legal ruling.
اہلیت نظر (ahliyyat al-nazar): The capability to critically examine and evaluate evidence and prefer one opinion over another.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Ibn Nujaym (rahimahullah), what was the condition for giving fatwa based on Imam Abu Hanifa's opinion in the earlier times?
A) The mufti must have memorized the issue well.
B) The mufti must know the evidence (dalil) for Imam Abu Hanifa's ruling.
C) The mufti must be a mujtahid.
D) The mufti must have written permission from the Imam.

Key Takeaway
The later Hanafi consensus is that a mufti must give fatwa according to Imam Abu Hanifa's opinion even without knowing its evidence; only ahl al-nazar may consider evidence strength.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa
intermediate
6 min
Obligation to Follow Imam Abu Hanifa in Fatwa
Ruling on wajib nature of fatwa according to Imam Abu Hanifa and meaning of ahl al-nazar.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the rule that it is wajib for non-mujtahid muftis to follow Imam Abu Hanifa's opinion in fatwa and identify the exception for ahl al-nazar.

Core Idea
For non-mujtahid muftis, following Imam Abu Hanifa's opinion in fatwa is wajib, even without knowing the evidence.

This passage from a classical rasm al-mufti text clarifies a critical point in Hanafi fatwa methodology: it is not merely permissible but obligatory for later muftis to give fatwa according to Imam Abu Hanifa's opinion, even if they do not know the evidence behind it. This rule was established by the consensus of later scholars who removed the condition of knowing the evidence for those who are not capable of independent legal reasoning (ahl al-nazar). The passage also defines ahl al-nazar and explains that only those with the ability to weigh evidence may deviate from Imam's opinion when the evidence is weak.

Guided Path
1
Identify the General Rule
The passage states that it is wajib (obligatory) to give fatwa according to Imam Abu Hanifa's opinion, even without knowing the evidence. This is the default ruling for muftis who are not ahl al-nazar.
The term 'wajib' indicates a binding obligation in fatwa.
2
Recognize the Historical Context
Earlier mashayikh (scholars) sometimes gave fatwa contrary to Imam Abu Hanifa because they were ahl al-nazar and the condition of knowing the evidence applied to them. Later scholars removed that condition for non-mujtahids.
This explains apparent contradictions in fatwa practice across eras.
3
Define Ahl al-Nazar
The passage defines ahl al-nazar as someone who knows fiqh well, can distinguish between jurists' sayings, and has full ability to prefer some sayings over others. This is the key exception to the general rule.
Knowledge of fiqh and capacity for tarjih are the core components.
4
Apply the Rule to Mufti Types
For a mufti who is ahl al-nazar, evidence consideration applies; for a mufti who is not, the condition of knowing evidence is removed and adherence to Imam Abu Hanifa is wajib.
Most later muftis fall into the second category.

Source Text

پس امام صاحب کے قول پر فتونی دینا نہ صرف جائز ہے بلکہ واجب ہے اگر چہ ہمیں معلوم نہ ہو که امام صاحب نے وہ بات کہاں سے فرمائی ہے۔ بناء علی ہذا حادی قدی میں جس قول کو صحیح قرار دیا ہے یعنی قوت دلیل کے معتبر ہونے کا قول تو وہ اسی شرط پر مبنی ہے مگر اب علماء نے طے کر دیا ہے کہ امام اعظم کے قول پر فتویٰ دیا جائے گا ( دلیل جاننے کی شرط ختم کر دی ہے ) تو اس سے یہ نتیجہ نکلتا ہے کہ ہمارے ذمہ امام صاحب کے قول پر فتوی دینا واجب ہے۔ اگر چہ مشائخ نے امام صاحب کے قول کے خلاف فتونی دیا ہو ۔ کیونکہ ان حضرات نے امام صاحب کے قول کے خلاف فتوئی اس لیے دیا تھا کہ ان کے حق میں امام اعظم کے قول پر فتوی دینے کی شرط مفقود تھی اور وہ شرط امام صاحب کے قول کی دلیل سے واقف ہونا تھی رہے ہم تو امام صاحب کے قول پر فتوی دیں گے اگر چہ ہمیں ان کے قول کی دلیل معلوم نہ ہو ۔ ( کیونکہ دلیل جاننے کی شرط ہمارے لیے باقی نہیں رہی) اور محقق ابن الہمام رحمہ اللہ نے متعدد مواقع میں مشائخ پر جہاں انہوں نے صاحبین کے قول پر فتوی دیا ہے یہ کہ کر رد کیا ہے کہ امام صاحب کے قول سے عدول صرف دلیل کی کمزوری کی صورت میں کیا جا سکتا ہے ( علامہ کی اس بات کا صاف مطلب یہ ہے کہ ہر جگہ امام صاحب کے قول پر فتویٰ دینا ضروری ہے اور اگر کوئی شبہ کرے کہ علامہ نے تو دلیل کا بھی اعتبار کیا ہے کہ جب امام صاحب کی دلیل قوی ہو تو اس پر فتوی دینا ضروری ہے دلیل ضعیف ہو تو اس سے عدول کیا جا سکتا ہے اس صورت میں امام صاحب کے قول پر فتویٰ دینا ضروری نہیں ہے تو ابن نجیم اس کا جواب دیتے ہیں) لیکن علامہ ابن الہمام دلیل میں غور و فکر کرنے کی اہلیت رکھتے تھے (اس لیے ان کے حق میں دلیل کا اعتبار ہے ) اور جو لوگ دلیل میں غور و فکر کرنے کی اہلیت نہیں رکھتے ان کے ذمہ امام صاحب کے قول پر فتویٰ دینا لازم ہے۔
اہلبیت نظر :
اور یہاں اہمیت کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ آدمی فقہ کو خوب جانتا ہو فقہاء کے اقوال کے درمیان امتیاز کر سکتا ہو اور اس میں بعض اقوال کو بعض پر ترجیح دینے کی پوری صلاحیت ہو ۔ حادی کی بات سے صاحب بحر کے مدعی پر اعتراض وارد ہو سکتا تھا اس لیے وہ اس عبارت کا جواب دے رہے ہیں ۔ ۱۲
Therefore, giving a fatwa according to the saying of Imam Sahib is not only permissible but obligatory, even if we do not know from where Imam Sahib derived that statement. Based on this, the statement in Hadi Qud which deemed a saying correct, i.e., the saying regarding the validity of strength of evidence, is based on that condition. But now the scholars have decided that fatwa will be given according to the saying of Imam A'zam (they have removed the condition of knowing the evidence). So from this it follows that it is obligatory upon us to give fatwa according to the saying of Imam Sahib, even if the mashayikh have given fatwa contrary to Imam Sahib's saying. Because those elders gave fatwa contrary to Imam Sahib's saying only because in their case the condition for giving fatwa according to Imam A'zam's saying was absent, and that condition was being acquainted with the evidence of Imam Sahib's saying. As for us, we will give fatwa according to Imam Sahib's saying, even if we do not know the evidence for his saying (because the condition of knowing the evidence no longer remains for us). And Muhagqiq Ibn al-Humam al-Hanafi, may Allah have mercy on him, has refuted the mashayikh in numerous places where they gave fatwa according to the saying of the Sahibayn, saying that deviation from Imam Sahib's saying can only be done in the case of weakness of evidence (the clear meaning of Allamah's statement is that it is necessary to give fatwa according to Imam Sahib's saying everywhere. And if someone doubts that Allamah also considered evidence in that if Imam Sahib's evidence is strong, it is necessary to give fatwa according to it; if the evidence is weak, deviation from it can be done, and in this case it is not necessary to give fatwa according to Imam Sahib's saying, then Ibn Nujaym answers this.) But Allamah Ibn al-Humam was capable of deep consideration in evidence (therefore, evidence is considered in his case) and those who are not capable of deep consideration in evidence, it is obligatory upon them to give fatwa according to Imam Sahib's saying.
Ahl al-Nazar:
And here the meaning of importance is that a person knows fiqh well, can distinguish between the sayings of the jurists, and has full ability to prefer some sayings over others. An objection could have been raised by Hadi's statement against the claimant of Sahib Bahr, so he is answering that statement. 12

Commentary
This passage discusses a key rasm al-mufti rule: the obligation to follow Imam Abu Hanifa's opinion in fatwa. The author states that it is not only permissible but wajib to give fatwa according to Imam Abu Hanifa's saying, even if one does not know the evidence behind it. This is because later scholars have removed the condition of knowing the evidence for the mufti who is not a mujtahid. The passage then addresses an apparent contradiction: why did earlier mashayikh sometimes give fatwa contrary to Imam Abu Hanifa? The answer is that they were capable of examining evidence (ahl al-nazar), so for them the condition of evidence knowledge applied. However, for later muftis who lack this capability, the condition is removed, and they must simply follow Imam Abu Hanifa. The passage defines 'ahl al-nazar' as someone who knows fiqh well, can distinguish between differing opinions, and can prefer some over others. This is a critical refinement: the rasm rule is that for non-mujtahid muftis, taqlid of Imam Abu Hanifa is obligatory, while for those capable of ijtihad, evidence consideration may apply.

Key Terms
اہلبیت نظر (ahl al-nazar): A person who knows fiqh well, distinguishes between jurists' sayings, and can prefer some over others

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because later scholars have removed the condition of knowing the evidence for non-mujtahids
B) Because Imam Abu Hanifa's evidence is always strong
C) Because the mashayikh always did so
D) Because it is easier for the mufti

Key Takeaway
The operative ruling (mufta bihi) for non-mujtahid muftis is to follow Imam Abu Hanifa's opinion unconditionally, as established by later Hanafi consensus.

The Preponderance Rule for Mufti Qualification
Rasm al-Mufti: Preponderance condition for qualification

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the condition for mufti qualification and apply the qawida 'religious matters are based on the predominant' to determine when a mufti is considered competent.

Core Idea
A mufti qualifies when correct fatawa outnumber incorrect ones – preponderance governs religious matters.

This lesson addresses a foundational qualification for a mufti: the requirement that his correct answers must outweigh his incorrect ones. The underlying legal maxim is that religious rulings are built on overwhelming probability. We will also examine a historical condition from Ibn al-Mubarak and how it relates to the later reliance on taqlid within the established madhhab.

Guided Path
1
State the basic condition
Identify the explicit condition given in the passage: a person is not qualified to give fatwa until the number of correct answers exceeds the number of incorrect ones. This is the quantitative threshold.
The condition is expressed in terms of 'ghalabah' (preponderance).
2
Recognise the underlying qawida
The passage invokes the qawida 'Umoor shar'iyyah ka madaar a'imm wa aghlab par hai'. State that this is a minor (sughra) maxim that gives legal weight to the predominant side.
This qawida is used in fatwa and qadha when weighing correct vs incorrect answers.
3
Contextualise Ibn al-Mubarak's condition
Ibn al-Mubarak required knowledge of hadith, qiyas, and Imam A'zam's sayings. Understand that this condition is interpreted as referring to a time before the madhhab was fully codified.
Ibn Nujaym explains that this represents one of two views in the Hanafi school regarding proof knowledge.
4
Distinguish between the two Hanafi views
The two views: (1) a mufti must know the dalil of the mufta bihi qawl, or (2) it is not necessary. Ibn al-Mubarak's statement aligns with the first view, but the second view is operative after codification.
After the madhhab became well-founded, taqlid suffices; proof knowledge is no longer required for issuing fatwa.
5
Apply the qawida to practice
Now that the madhhab is fully established, a mufti qualifies by knowing the authoritative positions and having more correct answers than incorrect ones. The qawida ensures that his fatawa are accepted based on preponderance.
This reduces the burden on the mufti: he need not independently derive rulings but must be accurate.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اہلیت فتوی اور کوئی شخص فتوی دینے کا اس وقت تک اہل نہیں ہو سکتا جب تک اس کے درست جوابوں کی تعداد نادرست جوابوں سے زیادہ نہ ہو جائے کیونکہ جب درست جوابات کی تعداد زیادہ ہوگی تو وہی غالب ہوں گے۔ اور غالب کے مقابلہ میں مغلوب کا اعتبار نہیں کیا جاتا کیونکہ امور شرعیہ کا مدار ائم و اغلب پر ہے جیسا کہ فتاوی ولوالجیہ (۹۱) کی کتاب القضاء میں ہے اور علامہ کر دری (۴۱) کی کتاب مناقب الامام الاعظم میں ہے کہ حضرت عبدالله بن المبارک رحمہ اللہ (۹۸) سے دریافت کیا گیا کہ آدمی کے لیے فتویٰ دینا اور قاضی بننا کب جائز ہے؟ تو آپ نے جواب دیا کہ: جب آدمی حدیث شریف اور قیاس سے پوری طرح واقف ہو جائے اور وہ امام اعظم کے اقوال کو پوری طرح جانتا ہو اور وہ اس کو خوب محفوظ ہوں۔ (یہاں ایک بار پھر یہ شبہ ہوسکتا ہے کہ امام ابن المبارک دلیل کا اعتبار کر رہے ہیں ۔ وہ مفتی کے لیے حدیث و قیاس کی معرفت ضروری قرار دے رہے ہیں۔ ابن نجیم اس کا جواب دیتے ہیں ) اور عبد اللہ بن المبارک کا یہ قول ہمارے علماء کی دو روایتوں میں سے ایک پر محمول ہے وہ دو روایتیں یہ ہیں (۱) فتوی دینے کے لیے مفتی بہ قول کی دلیل معلوم ہونا ضروری ہے (۲) ضروری نہیں ہے۔ ابن المبارک کا قول پہلی روایت پر مبنی ہے ) اور مذہب کے آخری شکل اختیار کرنے سے پہلے کی بات ہے۔ اب مذہب کے مدلل ہو جانے کے بعد ان امور کی (یعنی حدیث و قیاس کو جانے کی ) کوئی حاجت نہیں ۔ کیونکہ اب مفتی اور قاضی کے لیے تقلید ممکن ہے ( علامہ ابن نجیم کی عبارت پوری ہوئی ) ۔
Qualification for fatwa: A person cannot be qualified to give fatwa until the number of his correct answers exceeds the number of incorrect ones. Because when the number of correct answers becomes more, they become predominant. And the outweighed is not considered against the predominant, because religious matters are based on the overwhelming and the predominant. As it is in Fatawa Walwajiyya, book of Qada, and in Allama Karkari's book Manaqib al-Imam al-A'zam that Abdullah ibn al-Mubarak (may Allah have mercy on him) was asked: When is it permissible for a person to give fatwa and become a judge? He replied: When a person is fully acquainted with hadith and qiyas, and knows the sayings of Imam A'zam thoroughly, and has them well memorized. (Here it may be doubted that Imam Ibn al-Mubarak relies on proof; he deems knowledge of hadith and qiyas necessary for the mufti. Ibn Nujaym responds:) And this statement of Abdullah ibn al-Mubarak is interpreted according to one of two narrations of our scholars. Those two narrations are: (1) For giving fatwa, it is necessary to know the proof of the mufta bih qawl; (2) It is not necessary. The statement of Ibn al-Mubarak is based on the first narration, and it is before the madhhab took its final shape. Now after the madhhab has become well-founded, there is no need for these matters (i.e., knowing hadeeth and qiyas), because taqlid is possible for the mufti and the judge. (End of Ibn Nujaym's passage).
Source pages p. 77

Commentary
This passage is a rasm rule from Usul al-Iftaa, establishing the qualification for a mufti. The initial condition is quantitative: a mufti must have more correct answers than incorrect ones. The underlying principle is that religious rulings are based on overwhelming probability (ghalabah), as stated explicitly: 'umoor shar'iyyah ka madaar a'imm wa aghlab par hai'. This is a qawida that gives weight to the preponderant opinion. Then the passage presents a statement from Abdullah ibn al-Mubarak, a famous early scholar, who required a mufti to know hadith, qiyas, and the sayings of Imam A'zam. Ibn Nujaym explains this by saying it refers to one of two transmitted positions in the Hanafi school: either the mufti must know the proof (dalil) of the qawl he issues, or he need not. Ibn al-Mubarak's condition is based on the former, but it applied before the madhhab was fully codified and its rulings were systematically supported with proofs. After the madhhab became established, a non-mujtahid mufti can simply follow (taqlid) the authoritative positions. Thus, the requirement of knowing proofs is no longer needed for a mufti who operates within the fully developed madhhab. This sets the stage for the later discussion on non-mujtahid muftis who are merely transmitters.

Key Terms
مفتی بہ قول (mufta bihi qawl): The saying that is relied upon for issuing the fatwa, i.e., the preferred opinion in the madhhab.
تقلید (taqlid): Following the established opinion of a mujtahid without necessarily knowing the detailed proofs.
غالب (ghalib): The predominant or overwhelming side, which is given legal weight.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the primary condition for a person to be qualified to give fatwa?
A) He must have complete knowledge of hadith and qiyas.
B) His correct answers must outnumber his incorrect ones.
C) He must be a mujtahid.
D) He must have studied under a recognised scholar for 10 years.

Key Takeaway
A mufti's qualification rests on his correct fatawa outweighing his incorrect ones, supported by the qawida that religious matters are based on the predominant; after madhhab codification, taqlid suffices, and independent proof knowledge is not required.

The Non-Mujtahid Mufti as a Transmitter (Naqil)
Resolving internal dispute on non-mujtahid mufti's role

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the role of a non-mujtahid mufti in the Hanafi fatwa hierarchy and explain the distinction between a mufti and a naqil.

Core Idea
A non-mujtahid mufti is not a real mufti; he is a transmitter of the mujtahid's words.

This passage addresses a crucial tension in Hanafi fatwa practice: can a mufti who is not a mujtahid issue fatwas without knowing the proofs behind them? Ibn Nujaym said it is wajib to give fatwa on Imam A'zam's qawl even without knowing the proof. Al-Ramli objects, citing Imam A'zam's own requirement that one must know the proof. The resolution lies in the concept of 'naql' (transmission), which redefines the non-mujtahid's role. Understanding this distinction is essential for correctly applying the Hanafi fatwa hierarchy.

Guided Path
1
Identify the conflicting claims
First, identify Ibn Nujaym's claim (wajib to give fatwa on Imam's qawl even without knowing proof) and the apparent contradiction from Imam A'zam's statement that one must know the proof before giving fatwa.
Note that both claims are from authoritative Hanafi sources.
2
Understand the objection and its consequences
Examine al-Ramli's objection: if knowing the proof is required, then a non-mujtahid without that knowledge cannot give fatwa at all. This would effectively abolish fatwa today if no mujtahid exists.
3
Grasp the resolution: naql (transmission)
Al-Ramli resolves the problem by arguing that a non-mujtahid does not 'give fatwa' in the true sense—he merely transmits the mujtahid's words. For transmission, knowledge of the proof is not required.
This redefines the non-mujtahid as a naqil, not a mufti.
4
Recognize the role of the mashayikh
The later mashayikh (like Imam Muhammad and Imam Abu Yusuf) were aware of the proofs and could give tarjih. They sometimes preferred the qawl of a student over Imam A'zam based on stronger evidence. Their role is distinct from that of the ordinary non-mujtahid.
5
Apply the rule to the modern fatwa context
A non-mujtahid mufti today should present the relied-upon (mufta bihi) ruling of the madhhab as transmitted by the mashayikh, without needing to trace every proof. His job is accurate transmission, not ijtihad.

اور ہم میں جب دلائل میں غور وفکر کرنے کی صلاحیت نہیں ہے اور ہم تفریح و تاصیل

The non-mujtahid mufti is only a transmitter of fatawa:
(al-Ramli's critique of Ibn Nujaym)
I (Allama Shami) say that the inconsistency in Ibn Nujaym's speech is not hidden from you. For this reason, Khayr al-Din al-Ramli (may Allah have mercy on him) objected to this passage in the margin of al-Bahr, that Ibn Nujaym's saying that it is obligatory for us to give fatwa on the saying of Imam A'zam even if we do not know from where he derived that saying, contradicts the saying of Imam A'zam: 'It is not permissible for anyone to give fatwa on our saying unless he knows from which proof we said it.' Because Imam's saying clearly indicates that it is not permissible for a non-mujtahid to give fatwa at all. Then how can this saying be used as evidence that giving fatwa on Imam A'zam's saying is wajib? If someone objects that today there is no mujtahid mufti, then is it no longer permissible to give fatwa at all? (Al-Ramli answers:) So I say that what the non-mujtahid gives is not actually a fatwa; he only transmits the words of the mujtahid (and for mere transmission, knowing the proof is not necessary). On that basis, it is also permissible to transmit the statement of someone other than Imam A'zam. Then how did it become obligatory upon us to give fatwa on Imam A'zam's saying even if the mashayikh have given fatwa contrary to his saying? When we are merely transmitters of the fatawa of these mashayikh. (End of Ramli's passage)
The mashayikh were well acquainted with Imam A'zam's proofs:
(Clarification and further refutation of Ramli's rejection)
The explanation is that the mashayikh were acquainted with Imam's proofs and knew where he derived his saying. They were also acquainted with the proofs of the statements of Imam's students. Then they prefer the proofs of the later scholars over Imam's proof and give fatwa accordingly. It cannot be assumed that they deviated from Imam's saying because they did not know its proof, for we see that they established proofs and filled books with them, and then they say the fatwa is, for example, on the saying of Imam Yusuf.
.....
And when we do not have the ability to reflect on proofs, and we engage in tafri' (deriving sub-rules) and ta'sil (establishing principles).
Source pages p. 77

Commentary
This passage is a critical refinement of a rasm rule regarding the status of a non-mujtahid mufti. It presents an internal Hanafi dispute between Ibn Nujaym and later scholars like al-Ramli and al-Shami. Ibn Nujaym had stated that it is wajib to give fatwa on Imam A'zam's qawl even without knowing its proof. Al-Ramli objects, citing Imam A'zam's own statement that no one should give fatwa on his words without knowing the proof. This seems to forbid fatwa by non-mujtahids entirely. Al-Ramli resolves this by arguing that a non-mujtahid is not giving a fatwa in the true sense; he is merely transmitting (naql) the mujtahid's saying. For transmission, knowledge of the proof is not required. He further questions how it can be wajib to follow Imam A'zam's qawl when the later mashayikh sometimes issued fatawa contrary to it. The reply (from al-Shami) clarifies that the mashayikh were fully aware of Imam's and his students' proofs, and they gave fatwa on the preponderant proof, not out of ignorance. Thus, for the later non-mujtahid muftis, who lack the ability for ijtihad, their role is simply to transmit the fatawa of the mashayikh. The passage ends by noting that those without ijtihad capacity engage in tafri' (deriving branches) and ta'sil (establishing principles) based on the established madhhab. This carefully delineates the hierarchy of muftis and the role of the non-mujtahid.

Key Terms
غیر مجتہد مفتی (ghair mujtahid mufti): A mufti who is not capable of ijtihad; he only transmits the rulings of a mujtahid.
ناقل (naqil): Transmitter; one who conveys the saying of a mujtahid without issuing independent ijtihad.
مشائخ (mashayikh): Later scholars of the madhhab, such as those who gave tarjih (preference) among the positions of the early imams.
تفریع (tafri'): The process of deriving new sub-rules (furu) from the established principles (usul).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to al-Ramli's response, what is the true role of a non-mujtahid mufti?
A) He performs ijtihad with the help of the madhhab.
B) He merely transmits the statements of a mujtahid.
C) He must know the proof of every ruling he gives.
D) He cannot give fatwa at all.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi fatwa hierarchy, a non-mujtahid mufti is essentially a transmitter (naqil) of the mujtahid's words, not a true mufti.

Authority of Non-Mujtahid Muftis and the Tarjih of the Mashayikh
Refuting a doubt on non-mujtahid fatwa authority and explaining mashayikh tarjih

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi hierarchy of muftis by identifying the role of a non-mujtahid mufti and explaining why following the mashayikh's tarjih is obligatory.

Core Idea
A non-mujtahid mufti is a transmitter; he must follow the rajih opinion determined by the mashayikh.

Imam Abu Hanifa's statement that 'it is not permissible to give fatwa on our word until he knows from where we said it' might seem to forbid non-mujtahid muftis. However, later Hanafi scholars (mashayikh) clarified that a non-mujtahid is merely a transmitter of rulings, not an independent issuer. This lesson unpacks the hierarchy: only the mashayikh, who are mujtahids within the madhhab, perform tarjih (weighting) among early opinions, and ordinary muftis must follow their preferred (rajih) opinions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the doubt
Recognize the apparent objection: Imam Abu Hanifa's statement seems to require knowledge of the proof for fatwa, which a non-mujtahid lacks. This raises the question whether non-mujtahid fatwa is permissible.
The doubt is based on a literal reading of the Imam's words.
2
Understand Ramli's response
Ramli argues that a non-mujtahid's fatwa is not a true fatwa but a transmission of the mujtahid's statement. For transmission, knowing the proof is not necessary, just as one can transmit a hadith without knowing its chain.
This reframes the role of the mufti as a naqil (transmitter).
3
Recognize the role of mashayikh
The mashayikh (mujtahids fi al-madhhab) knew the proofs of Imam Abu Hanifa and his students. They weighed the evidence and sometimes preferred the students' opinions over the Imam's. Their tarjih is binding because they performed ijtihad within the madhhab.
Mashayikh are not mere transmitters; they are ashab al-tarjih.
4
Determine the obligation of non-mujtahids
Since non-mujtahids lack the ability to weigh proofs, their duty is to transmit the rajih (preferred) opinions as determined by the mashayikh. This is obligatory, just as it would be to follow the mashayikh if they were alive.
The non-mujtahid must follow the tarjih; he cannot choose based on his own preference.
5
Apply to contemporary practice
Today's muftis, being non-mujtahids, must consult reliable Hanafi fatwa collections (e.g., Radd al-Muhtar, Fatawa Hindiyya) that reflect the mashayikh's tarjih and issue fatwa accordingly.
This ensures consistency and authority within the madhhab.

شرح رسم المفتی
ہے اگر چہ ہم نہ جانتے ہوں کہ امام صاحب نے وہ قول کہاں سے کیا ہے یہ بات امام اعظم رحمہ اللہ کی اس بات کے خلاف ہے کہ " کسی کے لیے بھی جائز نہیں کہ ہمارے قول پر فتوی دے جب تک کہ وہ یہ نہ جان لے کہ ہم نے کس دلیل سے بات کہی ہے کیوں کہ امام صاحب کا یہ قول صاف اس بات پر دلالت کرتا ہے کہ : "غیر مجتہد کے لیے فتوی دینا ہی جائز نہیں" پھر اس قول سے اس بات پر کیسے استدلال کیا جا سکتا ہے کہ امام اعظم کے قول پر فتوی دینا واجب ہے؟ اور اگر کوئی شبہ کرے کہ آج کل تو مجتہد مفتی کا وجود نہیں، تو کیا اب فتویٰ دینا ہی جائز نہیں ؟ رملی اس کا جواب دیتے ہیں : )

شروع رسم المفتی
کی شرائط حاصل کرنے میں مشائخ کے درجہ تک نہیں پہنچ سکے ہیں تو ہمارے ذمہ ان مشائخ کے اقوال کو نقل کرنا ہے کیونکہ وہی حضرات مذہب حنفی کے وہ پیروکار ہیں جنہوں نے اپنے آپ کو مذہب کو مدلل کرنے کے لیے اور اپنے اجتہاد سے اس کو سنوارنے کے لیے تیار کر رکھا ہے۔
تائیدات
(1) اور وہ بات آپ ضرور دیکھ لیں جو ہم پہلے علامہ قاسم کے حوالہ سے ذکر کر آئے ہیں کہ مسلکی مجتہدین کا دور اس وقت تک ختم نہیں ہوا جب تک انہوں نے تمام اختلافی مسائل میں غور و خوض نہیں کر لیا اور ترجیح وتصیح کا کام پایہ تکمیل تک نہیں پہنچا دیا الی قولہ ) پس ہمارے ذمہ راج کی پیروی لازم ہے اور اس کے مطابق عمل کرنا ضروری ہے جیسا کہ وہ حضرات اگر اپنی

کے علاوہ کوئی صورت نہیں ہے"
حتى يعلم من این قلنا؟ کا پہلا مطلب پھر آپ جان لیں کہ امام اعظم کا جو ارشاد ہے کہ لا يحل لا حدان ان يفتي بقولنا حتى يعلم من این قلنا؟ ( کسی کے لیے بھی ہمارے قول پر فتوی دینا جائز نہیں تا آنکہ وہ جان لے کہ ہم نے کہاں سے وہ قول کیا ہے؟) اس ارشاد کے دو مطلب ہو سکتے ہیں۔ پہلا مطلب وہ ہے جو عبارت کے ظاہری اور متبادر معنی ہیں اور وہ یہ ہیں کہ جب اس کے نزدیک کسی مسئلہ میں آپ کے فتاوی کا نام مجمع الفتاوی ہے وہ ابھی تک مخطوط ہیں اور اس کا نسخہ بصرہ میں ہے (اعلام
How do you give fatwa? Explanation of Rasm al-Mufti. It is against the statement of Imam A'zam that 'it is not permissible for anyone to give fatwa on our word until he knows from where we said it' because his statement clearly indicates that 'giving fatwa is not permissible for a non-mujtahid'. Then how can this be used as evidence that giving fatwa on Imam A'zam's word is obligatory? If someone objects that nowadays there is no mujtahid mufti, then is giving fatwa not permissible at all? Ramli answers: I say that the fatwa given by a non-mujtahid is not actually a fatwa; he only transmits the statement of a mujtahid that he said such-and-such (and for mere transmission, knowing the proof is not necessary). From this perspective, it is also permissible to transmit the statement of someone other than Imam Sahib. Then why has it become obligatory upon us to give fatwa on Imam Sahib's statement, even if the later scholars (mashayikh) gave fatwa against his statement, when we are only transmitters of those mashayikh's fatwas? (Ramli's statement ends) The mashayikh were well aware of Imam A'zam's proofs. Explanation of the refutation by Ramli and additional refutation: The explanation is that the mashayikh knew Imam Sahib's proofs and knew from where he derived his statement. They also knew the proofs of the statements of Imam Sahib's students. Then they prefer the proofs of the students over Imam Sahib's proof and give fatwa accordingly. It cannot be assumed that they deviated from Imam Sahib's statement because they were unaware of his proof, for we see that they have compiled proofs in books and then they say that fatwa is, for example, on Imam Yusuf's statement. ... And when we do not have the ability to ponder over proofs and we are not able to reach the rank of the mashayikh in acquiring the conditions of fatwa, then it is upon us to transmit the statements of those mashayikh, because they are the followers of the Hanafi school who have prepared themselves to substantiate the school and refine it with their ijtihad. Corroborations: (1) You must note what we previously mentioned from Allama Qasim that the era of madhhab-based mujtahids did not end until they had thoroughly examined all disputed issues and brought the work of weighting and correction to completion. (up to his saying) So it is necessary for us to follow the preferred (rajih) opinion and act accordingly, just as it would be obligatory to follow them if they gave fatwa during their lifetime. (2) In the fatwa collection of Allama Ibn al-Shami (1011H) it is stated: It is not permissible for a judge or mufti to deviate from Imam Sahib's statement unless one of the mashayikh explicitly indicates that fatwa is on the statement of someone other than Imam Sahib. In summary, it is not permissible for a judge to decide based on the statement of someone other than Imam Sahib in a matter where no preference has been given to the other's statement by the mashayikh, but rather they have preferred Imam Sahib's proof over others. If he does so, his decision will not be executable; there is no option but to break such a decision. Then you should know that Imam A'zam's directive: 'It is not permissible for anyone to give fatwa on our word until he knows from where we said it' has two possible meanings. The first meaning is the apparent and obvious sense of the phrase, which is that when in his view, regarding a particular issue, your fatwas... the collection named Majma' al-Fatawa is still in manuscript and its copy is in Basra. (from A'lam)
Source pages p. 78

Commentary
This passage is a detailed discussion on the authority of non-mujtahid muftis in the Hanafi school, addressing a doubt arising from Imam Abu Hanifa's statement that one must know the proof before giving fatwa on his opinion. The author presents Ramli's response that a non-mujtahid is merely a transmitter, not a genuine mufti, and transmission does not require knowledge of the proof. Then the author clarifies that later mashayikh (mujtahids within the madhhab) who gave fatwa against Imam Abu Hanifa's opinion did so after weighing proofs and preferring the opinions of his students where their proofs were stronger. Since contemporary muftis lack the ability to weigh proofs themselves, they must follow the rajih (preferred) opinions as determined by those mashayikh. The passage also cites Ibn Abidin to emphasize that a judge or mufti cannot deviate from Imam Abu Hanifa's opinion unless the mashayikh have explicitly preferred another view. Finally, it unpacks Imam Abu Hanifa's statement, noting two possible interpretations: the apparent one (fatwa requires knowing the proof) and a deeper one (implied later in the text but not fully given here). The overall ruling is that non-mujtahids must rely on tarjih of the mashayikh.

Key Terms
غیر مجتہد (ghayr mujtahid): A person who has not reached the level of ijtihad; in this context, a muqallid who transmits rulings without independent reasoning.
مشائخ (mashāyikh): Later Hanafi scholars (mujtahids fi al-madhhab) who performed tarjih (weighting) among early opinions.
راجح (rājiḥ): The preferred opinion after weighing proofs, which must be followed by muqallids.
ترجیح و تصیح (tarjīḥ wa taṣḥīḥ): The process of weighing and correcting juristic opinions within the madhhab.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the duty of a non-mujtahid mufti in the Hanafi school?
A) To issue fatwas based on his own ijtihad.
B) To transmit the statements of the mashayikh and follow their tarjih.
C) To only give fatwa on Imam Abu Hanifa's opinion.
D) To stop giving fatwa altogether.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi madhhab, a non-mujtahid mufti must follow the preferred opinion (rajih) as determined by the mashayikh, because he is a transmitter, not a mujtahid.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa
intermediate
8 min
The Hierarchy of Muftis: From Mashayikh to Naqil Fatawa
Explaining the hierarchy and duty of muftis

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the three levels of muftis (mujtahid mutlaq, mujtahid fi al-madhhab, naqil fatawa) and state the duty of each in giving fatwa according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Only mashayikh can refine the madhhab; lesser scholars must transmit their rulings.

This lesson clarifies the Hanafi hierarchy of muftis. The text first establishes that those who have not reached the rank of the mashayikh must transmit their rulings. It then provides corroborations from Allamah Qasim and Ibn Abidin on the necessity of following the preferred view and not deviating from Imam Abu Hanifa. Understanding this hierarchy is essential for knowing who can give fatwa and on what basis.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three categories of mufti
From the text, extract the categories: mujtahid mutlaq (absolute), mujtahid fi al-madhhab (within school), and naqil fatawa (transmitter). Note that the first two are mentioned indirectly through the discussion of mashayikh and mujtahideen.
The text focuses on the latter two, but the hierarchy is implied.
2
Understand the role of mashayikh
The mashayikh are those who have reached a level of ijtihad within the Hanafi school. They are responsible for tarjih (preference) and tasih (correction) of rulings. Their era ends only after all disputes are examined.
This is corroborated by Allamah Qasim's statement.
3
Recognize the obligation of taqlid for non-mujtahids
For a mufti who is not a mujtahid fi al-madhhab, taqlid is wajib. He must accept the rulings of the school without knowing the evidence. This is derived from Ibn al-Humam's quote.
Taqlid is defined as accepting without knowing the evidence.
4
Explain the duty of naqil fatawa
The naqil fatawa (transmitter) must simply copy the fatwa of the mashayikh. He cannot exercise independent judgment.
This is stated at the beginning: 'upon us is to transmit the statements of those mashayikh.'

دلیل معارض دلیل سے محفوظ ہے اور یہ بات تمام دلائل کا جائزہ لینے پر موقوف ہے اور یہ کام مجتہد ہی کر سکتا ہے۔ اور صرف یہ جاننا کہ فلاں مجتہد نے فلاں حکم فلاں دلیل سے اخذ کیا ہے محض بے فائدہ ہے۔ اس لیے مفتی کے لیے دلیل جاننا ضروری ہے کا مطلب یہ لینا ہو گا کہ وہ اس دلیل کا حال بھی جانتا ہو کہ اس کے لیے اس مسئلہ میں یقین کے ساتھ امام کی تقلید اور دوسروں کو اس پر فتوی دینا درست ہو اور یہ بات مجتہد فی المذہب مفتی ہی کے لیے ممکن ہے اور وہی درحقیقت مفتی ہے دوسرے لوگ تو ناقل فتاوی ہیں۔ پہلے مطلب پر اشکال: لیکن قول امام کا مذکورہ بالا مطلب لینا بعید ہے کیونکہ یہ مجتہد فی المذہب مفتی جب اجتہاد مطلق کے درجہ تک نہیں پہنچا ہے تو اس پر اس کی تقلید لازم ہے جو اجتہاد مطلق کے درجہ تک پہنچ چکا ہے اور مقلد پر قول امام کی دلیل جاننا لازم نہیں۔ البتہ ایک رائے کے مطابق جو معتزلہ کی ہے اپنے امام کی دلیل کا جاننا ضروری ہے۔ علامہ ابن الہمام التحریر میں لکھتے ہیں: مسئلہ: جو شخص مجتہد مطلق نہیں ہے اس پر تقلید لازم ہے۔ اگر چہ وہ فقہ کے بعض مسائل میں یا بعض علوم میں مثلاً علم الفرائض میں مجتہد مطلق ہو اجتہاد میں تجزی (تقسیم) کے جواز کے قول کی بنا پر۔ اور یہی قول برحق ہے۔ لہذا جن
How do you give a fatwa? Beginning of Rasm al-Mufti: Those who have not reached the rank of the mashayikh in acquiring the conditions (of fatwa) — upon us is to transmit the statements of those mashayikh, because they are the followers of the Hanafi school who have prepared themselves to substantiate the school and to refine it with their ijtihad. Corroborations: (1) And you must definitely see that which we mentioned earlier from the reference of Allamah Qasim: that the era of madhhab-based mujtahids has not ended until they have thoroughly examined all disputed issues and the work of tarjih and tasih has been completed up to the end of his statement: 'Thus upon us is the following of the rajih and acting according to it is necessary, just as if those individuals gave a fatwa during their lifetime, following it would be necessary.' (2) And in the Fatawa of Allamah Ibn al-Shami (101): It is not permissible for a qadi or mufti to deviate from the statement of Imam Sahib, unless one of the mashayikh explicitly states that the fatwa is on the statement of someone other than Imam Sahib. In short, it is not permissible for a qadi to decide a case on a statement other than that of Imam Sahib when preference has not been given to that statement by the mashayikh, rather the mashayikh have preferred Imam Sahib's evidence over others' evidence. If he does so, his decision will not be effective; there is no option but to break such a decision. So that he knows from where we said: The first meaning. Then you should know that the statement of Imam A'zam: 'It is not lawful for anyone to give a fatwa by our statement until he knows from where we said it.' This statement can have two meanings. The first meaning is that which is apparent and immediately understood from the phrase: that when he (the mufti) knows the evidence for a ruling in a matter... etc. (The text continues with details).
Source pages p. 79

Commentary
This passage from the beginning of Rasm al-Mufti discusses the conditions for giving fatwa. It first establishes that those who have not reached the high rank of the mashayikh (senior scholars) must simply transmit their rulings, because these mashayikh are the ones qualified to argue for the madhhab and refine it through ijtihad. The text then presents two corroborations: first, that the era of madhhab-based mujtahids has not ended until all disputed issues have been examined and preference (tarjih) completed, so we must follow the preferred view; second, from Ibn Abidin's Fatawa, that a qadi or mufti cannot deviate from Imam Abu Hanifa's view unless mashayikh explicitly state that fatwa is on another view. Then the text turns to explaining Imam Abu Hanifa's famous statement: 'It is not lawful for anyone to give a fatwa by our statement until he knows from where we said it.' The first interpretation is that the mufti must know the evidence (dalil) for the ruling he gives. However, this would limit fatwa-giving to mujtahids, as taqlid is defined as accepting a statement without knowing the evidence. Knowing the evidence and its soundness is the work of a mujtahid. The second interpretation (implied but not fully explained in the text) is that this statement only applies to a mujtahid fi al-madhhab, while others are mere transmitters (naqil) of fatwa. The text critiques the first interpretation, noting that it is far-fetched because a mujtahid fi al-madhhab himself is not a mujtahid mutlaq and must follow the mujtahid mutlaq. The passage ends with a quote from Ibn al-Humam in Al-Tahrir affirming that taqlid is obligatory for non-mujtahids, even if they have ijtihad in some areas like fara'id (inheritance law), based on the permissibility of tajzi' al-ijtihad.

Key Terms
مجتہد فی المذہب (mujtahid fi al-madhhab): A scholar who has ijtihad within the Hanafi school, able to prefer and refine rulings based on evidence but not reaching the level of absolute ijtihad.
ناقل فتاوی (naqil fatawa): A person who merely transmits the fatwa of qualified scholars without personal ijtihad.
تقلید (taqlid): Accepting an imam's statement without knowing its evidence.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, who is required to know the evidence for the rulings they give?
A) Every mufti, regardless of rank
B) Only the mujtahid fi al-madhhab
C) Only the Mujtahid Mutlaq
D) Both B and C

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school distinguishes between mujtahids who must know evidence and muqallids who transmit, and Imam Abu Hanifa's statement on knowing evidence applies to the former.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa

Two Interpretations of Imam Abu Hanifa's Statement on Knowing Evidence
Interpreting Imam Abu Hanifa's statement on knowing evidence

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the two possible interpretations of Imam Abu Hanifa's statement, identify which one is adopted by the Hanafi school, and justify the adoption.

Core Idea
The first interpretation (mufti must know evidence) is far-fetched; the second restricts it to mujtahid fi al-madhhab.

This lesson delves into the famous statement of Imam Abu Hanifa: 'It is not lawful for anyone to give a fatwa by our statement until he knows from where we said it.' The text presents two interpretations. The first, apparent meaning is that every mufti must know the evidence. However, this is critiqued as it would make fatwa impossible for most. The second interpretation, which is adopted, confines the requirement to a mujtahid fi al-madhhab. Understanding this is crucial for appreciating the Hanafi hierarchy of muftis.

Guided Path
1
Quote Imam Abu Hanifa's statement
Locate the statement in the text: 'لا يحل لأحد أن يفتي بقولنا حتى يعلم من أين قلنا' (It is not lawful for anyone to give a fatwa by our statement until he knows from where we said it).
This is the central text being interpreted.
2
Explain the first interpretation
The first interpretation is the 'zahiri' (apparent) meaning: the mufti must know the evidence (dalil) for the ruling. For example, to give a fatwa on witt being wajib, he must know the source (e.g., hadith of witt).
This interpretation would limit fatwa to mujtahids only.
3
Understand the critique of the first interpretation
The text argues that this interpretation is 'ba'eed' (far-fetched) because it contradicts the definition of taqlid (accepting without evidence). Also, knowing evidence and its soundness is the work of a mujtahid. Thus, if we accept this, only mujtahids can give fatwa.
The critique logically leads to the second interpretation.
4
Identify the second interpretation
The second interpretation (implied) is that the statement is directed at a mujtahid fi al-madhhab. He is required to know the evidence to verify the school's position. The ordinary mufti (naqil) is not included.
This reconciles the statement with the practice of taqlid.
5
Confirm the adopted view
The text supports the second interpretation by citing Ibn al-Humam and stating that taqlid is wajib for non-mujtahids. The first interpretation is considered weak.
This is the standard Hanafi position.

How do you give a fatwa? Beginning of Rasm al-Mufti: Those who have not reached the rank of the mashayikh in acquiring the conditions (of fatwa) — upon us is to transmit the statements of those mashayikh, because they are the followers of the Hanafi school who have prepared themselves to substantiate the school and to refine it with their ijtihad. Corroborations: (1) And you must definitely see that which we mentioned earlier from the reference of Allamah Qasim: that the era of madhhab-based mujtahids has not ended until they have thoroughly examined all disputed issues and the work of tarjih and tasih has been completed up to the end of his statement: 'Thus upon us is the following of the rajih and acting according to it is necessary, just as if those individuals gave a fatwa during their lifetime, following it would be necessary.' (2) And in the Fatawa of Allamah Ibn al-Shami (101): It is not permissible for a qadi or mufti to deviate from the statement of Imam Sahib, unless one of the mashayikh explicitly states that the fatwa is on the statement of someone other than Imam Sahib. In short, it is not permissible for a qadi to decide a case on a statement other than that of Imam Sahib when preference has not been given to that statement by the mashayikh, rather the mashayikh have preferred Imam Sahib's evidence over others' evidence. If he does so, his decision will not be effective; there is no option but to break such a decision. So that he knows from where we said: The first meaning. Then you should know that the statement of Imam A'zam: 'It is not lawful for anyone to give a fatwa by our statement until he knows from where we said it.' This statement can have two meanings. The first meaning is that which is apparent and immediately understood from the phrase: that when he (the mufti) knows the evidence for a ruling in a matter... etc. (The text continues with details).
Source pages p. 79

Commentary
This passage from the beginning of Rasm al-Mufti discusses the conditions for giving fatwa. It first establishes that those who have not reached the high rank of the mashayikh (senior scholars) must simply transmit their rulings, because these mashayikh are the ones qualified to argue for the madhhab and refine it through ijtihad. The text then presents two corroborations: first, that the era of madhhab-based mujtahids has not ended until all disputed issues have been examined and preference (tarjih) completed, so we must follow the preferred view; second, from Ibn Abidin's Fatawa, that a qadi or mufti cannot deviate from Imam Abu Hanifa's view unless mashayikh explicitly state that fatwa is on another view. Then the text turns to explaining Imam Abu Hanifa's famous statement: 'It is not lawful for anyone to give a fatwa by our statement until he knows from where we said it.' The first interpretation is that the mufti must know the evidence (dalil) for the ruling he gives. However, this would limit fatwa-giving to mujtahids, as taqlid is defined as accepting a statement without knowing the evidence. Knowing the evidence and its soundness is the work of a mujtahid. The second interpretation (implied but not fully explained in the text) is that this statement only applies to a mujtahid fi al-madhhab, while others are mere transmitters (naqil) of fatwa. The text critiques the first interpretation, noting that it is far-fetched because a mujtahid fi al-madhhab himself is not a mujtahid mutlaq and must follow the mujtahid mutlaq. The passage ends with a quote from Ibn al-Humam in Al-Tahrir affirming that taqlid is obligatory for non-mujtahids, even if they have ijtihad in some areas like fara'id (inheritance law), based on the permissibility of tajzi' al-ijtihad.

Key Terms
مجتہد فی المذہب (mujtahid fi al-madhhab): A scholar who has ijtihad within the Hanafi school, able to prefer and refine rulings based on evidence but not reaching the level of absolute ijtihad.
ناقل فتاوی (naqil fatawa): A person who merely transmits the fatwa of qualified scholars without personal ijtihad.
تقلید (taqlid): Accepting an imam's statement without knowing its evidence.

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, which interpretation of Imam Abu Hanifa's statement is mufta bihi (operative for fatwa)?
A) Every mufti must know the evidence
B) Only mujtahid fi al-madhhab must know the evidence
C) Only Mujtahid Mutlaq must know the evidence
D) Muftis must know the evidence only if they are giving fatwa on disputed issues

Key Takeaway
Imam Abu Hanifa's statement about knowing evidence is interpreted to apply only to a mujtahid fi al-madhhab, not to ordinary muftis who are transmitters.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa
intermediate

The Status of the Mujtahid fi al-Madhhab in Fatwa
Debate on evidence requirement for mujtahid fi al-madhhab

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the status of a mujtahid fi al-madhhab in the Hanafi fatwa hierarchy and evaluate the requirement for knowing dalil.

Core Idea
A mujtahid fi al-madhhab is not a pure muqallid; he must know the evidence to issue fatwas.

Who is qualified to issue fatwas? The Hanafi school distinguishes between the mujtahid mutlaq, the mujtahid fi al-madhhab, and the mere muqallid. A key question is whether a mujtahid fi al-madhhab must know the evidence (dalil) behind his imam's rulings. This passage from Rasm al-Mufti examines the debate, presenting the objection of the majority and the Hanafi response that such a scholar is effectively a mujtahid bound by the madhhab's principles.

Guided Path
1
Define Taqlid and Muqallid
Start by understanding the definition of taqlid: accepting a statement without knowing its evidence. A muqallid mahd is one who does not know the evidence.
This sets the baseline for the debate.
2
Identify the Two Opposing Views
One view (jumhur) holds that anyone not a mujtahid mutlaq must do taqlid, so even a mujtahid fi al-madhhab does not need to know the evidence. The other view (chosen in the Hanafi school) holds that a mujtahid fi al-madhhab is a mujtahid and must know the evidence.
The key is who counts as a mujtahid.
3
Analyze the Objection from Jumhur
Ibn al-Humam's statement in al-Tahrir is presented: taqlid is necessary for anyone not a mujtahid mutlaq, even if they have partial ijtihad. This suggests that knowing evidence is only for the mujtahid mutlaq.
This would exclude the mujtahid fi al-madhhab from needing to know dalil.
4
Examine the Hanafi Response
Ibn Amir Haj, quoting al-Zarkashi, argues that equating the mujtahid fi al-madhhab with a common muqallid is incorrect. These scholars possess ijtihad capabilities and have only committed not to found a new madhhab. Ibn al-Munir confirms they are mujtahids.
The response resolves the apparent contradiction.
5
Determine the Mufta Bihi Position
The preferred view (mukhtar) is that the mujtahid fi al-madhhab is a mujtahid, not a muqallid. Therefore, he must know the evidence to properly issue fatwas. This is the operative ruling for fatwa today.
This clarifies the hierarchy of muftis.

Source Text

شروع رسم السنتي

اپنے امام کا مذہب ثابت ہو جائے ۔ مثلاً امام اعظم کے نزدیک وتر کی نماز واجب ہے تو اس کے لیے اس حکم پر فتوی دینا اس وقت جائز ہے جب وہ امام صاحب کے قول کی دلیل جان لے۔ مصداق خاص
اور بلا شک دار تیاب یہ ارشاد اس تفسیر کے مطابق مجتہد مفتی کے ساتھ خاص ہو گا مقلد محض مفتی کے لیے یہ ارشاد نہیں ہے کیونکہ تقلید کسی کا قول اس کی دلیل جانے بغیر لینے کا نام ہے۔ علماء نے فرمایا ہے کہ اس تعریف کی رو سے امام کے قول کو دلیل جان کر لینا تقلید سے خارج ہو گیا۔ کیونکہ وہ تقلید نہیں ہے بلکہ دلیل سے مسئلہ اخذ کرنا ہے مجتہد سے مسئلہ اخذ کرتا نہیں ہے۔ بلکہ یہ بھی کہا گیا ہے کہ امام کے قول کی دلیل جان کر اس کو لینا اجتہاد کا نتیجہ ہے کیونکہ دلیل کی معرفت مجتہد ہی کو ہو سکتی ہے۔ اس لیے کہ دلیل کا جاننا یہ جاننے پر موقوف ہے کہ وہ دلیل معارض دلیل سے محفوظ ہے اور یہ بات تمام دلائل کا جائزہ لینے پر موقوف ہے اور یہ کام مجتہد ہی کر سکتا ہے۔ اور صرف یہ جاننا کہ فلاں مجتہد نے فلاں حکم فلاں دلیل سے اخذ کیا ہے محض بے فائدد ہے۔ اس لیے مفتی کے لیے دلیل جانا ضروری ہے" کا مطلب یہ لینا ہو گا کہ وہ اس دلیل کا حال بھی جانتا ہوتا کہ اس کے لیے اس مسئلہ میں یقین کے ساتھ امام کی تقلید اور دوسروں کو اس پر فتوی دینا درست ہو اور یہ بات مجتہد فی المذہب مفتی ہی کے لیے ممکن ہے اور وہی درحقیقت مفتی ہے دوسرے لوگ تو ناقل فتاوی ہیں۔

پہلے مطلب پر اشکال : لیکن قول امام کا مذکورہ بالا مطلب لینا بعید ہے کیونکہ یہ مجتہد فی المذہب مفتی جب اجتہاد مطلق کے درجہ تک نہیں پہنچا ہے تو اس پر اس کی تقلید لازم ہے جو اجتہاد مطلق کے درجہ تک پہنچ چکا ہے اور مقلد پر قول امام کی دلیل جانا لازم نہیں البتہ ایک رائے کے مطابق جو معتزلہ کی ہے اپنے امام کی دلیل کا جاننا ضروری ہے۔ علامہ ابن الہمام التحریر میں لکھتے ہیں: مسئلہ: جو شخص مجتہد مطلق نہیں ہے اس پر تقلید لازم ہے۔ اگر چہ وہ فقہ کے بعض مسائل میں یا بعض علوم میں مثلاً علم الفرائض میں مجتہد مطلق ہو اجتہاد میں تجزی (تقسیم) کے جواز کے قول کی بنا پر ۔ اور یہی قول برحق ہے۔ لہذا جن مسائل میں وہ اجتہاد پر قادر نہیں ہے دوسروں کی تقلید کرے گا اور عالم ( جانے والے) کے بارے میں کہا گیا ہے کہ اس پر تقلید اس شرط کے ساتھ لازم ہے کہ اس کے لیے مجتہد کی دلیل کی صحت واضح ہو ورنہ عالم کے لیے اس کی تقلید جائز نہیں ہے اھ (التقریر ج ۳ ص ۳۴۴) اور پہلا قول جمہور کا ہے اور دوسرا بعض معتزلہ کا جیسا کہ تحریر کے شارح نے بیان کیا ہے . پس امام ابن الہمام کا یہ قول کہ جو شخص مجتہد مطلق نہیں ہے اس پر تقلید لازم ہے اور تقلید کی وہ تعریف جو ہم اوپر ذکر کر آئے ہیں، دونوں اس بات پر دلالت کرتے ہیں کہ دلیل کا جاننا صرف مجتہد مطلق پر ضروری ہے۔ دوسروں پر یہ بات لازم نہیں ہے۔ خواہ وہ دوسرا مجتہد فی المذہب ہی کیوں نہ ہو ( خلاصہ اعتراض یہ ہے کہ جمہور کے قول کے مطابق مجتہد فی المذہب مفتی بھی عام مقلدین کی طرح ہے اس کے لیے بھی قول امام کی دلیل جاننا ضروری نہیں ہے پس امام صاحب کے قول کا پہلا مطلب درست نہیں ہے )

جواب:
لیکن التحریر کے شارح علامہ ابن امیر حاج رحمہ اللہ (۳۹) نے شافعی عالم علامہ بد الدین زرکشی رحمہ اللہ (۱۰۲) سے نقل کیا ہے کہ:
مجتہد فی المذہب کو آنکھ بند کر کے محض عامی کے ساتھ لاحق کرنا محل نظر ہے خاص طور پر مذاہب اربعہ کے وسیع علم رکھنے والے متبعین کو ۔ کیونکہ ان حضرات نے اپنے آپ کو عام مقلدین کے مقام پر کھڑا نہیں کیا ہے اور ان کو مجتہدین کے ساتھ لاحق کرنا بھی ممکن نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ ایک مجتہد دوسرے مجتہد کی تقلید نہیں کرتا۔ اور دونوں درجوں کے درمیان کوئی واسطہ بھی نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ حالتیں کل دو ہی ہیں۔ ابن المنیر کہتے ہیں کہ مختار یہ ہے کہ یہ حضرات مجتہد ہیں مگر انہوں نے اس بات کا التزام کیا ہے کہ وہ کوئی نیا مذہب شروع نہیں کریں گے اور ان کے مجتہد ہونے کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ ان میں اجتہاد کی صلاحیتیں موجود ہیں اور ان کے اس التزام کی وجہ کہ وہ کوئی نیا مذ ہب شروع نہیں کریں گے یہ ہے کہ کوئی ایسا نیا مذہب شروع کرنا جس کی جملہ فروعات کے لیے ایسے اصول وقواعد ہوں جو
Beginning of Rasm al-Mufti... That the madhhab of one's imam is established. For example, according to Imam A'zam, Witr prayer is obligatory. So issuing a fatwa on this ruling for him is permissible only when he knows the evidence of the Imam's statement. Specific application. And without doubt, this statement, according to this interpretation, is specific to the mujtahid mufti; it is not for the mere muqallid mufti, because taqlid is to take someone's statement without knowing its evidence. The scholars have said that according to this definition, taking the Imam's statement after knowing the evidence is excluded from taqlid, because it is not taqlid but rather deriving the ruling from evidence. It is not taking the ruling from the mujtahid. Rather, it has also been said that taking the Imam's statement after knowing its evidence is a result of ijtihad, because knowledge of evidence can only be possessed by a mujtahid. This is because knowing the evidence depends on knowing that the evidence is protected from a conflicting evidence, and that depends on reviewing all evidences, and only a mujtahid can do this. And merely knowing that a certain mujtahid derived a certain ruling from a certain evidence is completely useless. Therefore, the meaning of 'it is necessary for the mufti to know the evidence' is that he also knows the condition of that evidence so that for him, taqlid of the Imam in that issue with certainty and giving fatwa to others on it is correct, and this is only possible for a mujtahid fi al-madhhab mufti, and he is in reality the mufti; others are just narrators of fatwas. Objection to the first meaning: But taking the above meaning of the Imam's statement is far-fetched, because when this mujtahid fi al-madhhab mufti has not reached the level of ijtihad mutlaq, then taqlid of one who has reached ijtihad mutlaq is incumbent upon him, and on a muqallid, knowing the evidence of the Imam's statement is not necessary. However, according to one opinion of the Mu'tazila, knowing the evidence of one's Imam is necessary. 'Allamah Ibn al-Humam writes in al-Tahrir: Issue: Whoever is not a mujtahid mutlaq, taqlid is necessary for him, even if he is a mujtahid mutlaq in some issues of fiqh or in some sciences, for example, in the science of fara'id, based on the opinion allowing tajzi' in ijtihad. And this is the correct opinion. Therefore, in issues where he is not capable of ijtihad, he will do taqlid of others. And regarding the 'alim, it has been said that taqlid is necessary for him on the condition that the correctness of the mujtahid's evidence is clear to him; otherwise, taqlid is not permissible for the 'alim. (al-Taqrir vol. 3 p. 344) And the first opinion is that of the jumhur, and the second is of some Mu'tazila, as the commentator of al-Tahrir explained. So the statement of Imam Ibn al-Humam that taqlid is necessary for whoever is not a mujtahid mutlaq, and the definition of taqlid that we mentioned above, both indicate that knowing the evidence is necessary only for the mujtahid mutlaq. It is not necessary for others, even if the other is a mujtahid fi al-madhhab. (Summary of the objection: According to the jumhur's opinion, the mujtahid fi al-madhhab mufti is like a common muqallid; for him too, knowing the evidence of the Imam's statement is not necessary. So the first meaning of the Imam's statement is not correct.) Response: But the commentator of al-Tahrir, 'Allamah Ibn Amir Haj (39), has narrated from the Shafi'i scholar 'Allamah Badr al-Din al-Zarkashi (102) that: To blindly equate the mujtahid fi al-madhhab with a common layman is open to scrutiny, especially regarding the followers who possess extensive knowledge of the four schools. Because these people have not placed themselves at the level of common muqallids, and it is not possible to equate them with the mujtahids, because one mujtahid does not do taqlid of another mujtahid. And there is no intermediary between the two levels. Because there are only two states. Ibn al-Munir says that the chosen view is that these people are mujtahids, but they have committed themselves not to establish a new madhhab. And the proof that they are mujtahids is that they possess the capabilities of ijtihad. And the reason for their commitment not to establish a new madhhab is that to establish a new madhhab whose principles and rules cover all its branches that...
Source pages p. 80

Commentary
This passage is a discussion of a key rasm al-mufti rule: whether a mufti who is a mujtahid fi al-madhhab must know the evidence (dalil) of his imam's rulings. The author begins by stating that according to a certain interpretation, the requirement to know the evidence applies only to a mujtahid mufti, not to a mere muqallid. Taqlid is defined as accepting someone's statement without knowing its evidence. The scholars clarify that if one knows the evidence, it is no longer taqlid but ijtihad or deriving from evidence. Then an objection is raised: the mujtahid fi al-madhhab is not a mujtahid mutlaq, so taqlid is still incumbent on him, and for a muqallid, knowing the evidence is not required. This is the position of the jumhur (majority). Ibn al-Humam in al-Tahrir supports this, stating that taqlid is necessary for anyone who is not a mujtahid mutlaq, even if they have partial ijtihad. However, a contrary opinion from some Mu'tazila holds that knowing the evidence is necessary. The author then presents a response from Ibn Amir Haj, quoting Badr al-Din al-Zarkashi, arguing that a mujtahid fi al-madhhab should not be equated with a common muqallid. Such scholars possess ijtihad capabilities and have only committed to not founding a new madhhab; they are effectively mujtahids. This debate clarifies the hierarchy of muftis: the mujtahid mutlaq, the mujtahid fi al-madhhab, and the muqallid. The relied-upon position in the Hanafi school is that the mujtahid fi al-madhhab is not a blind follower; he must understand the evidence to properly issue fatwas.

Key Terms
تقلید (taqlid): Accepting a statement of a mujtahid without knowing its evidence.
مجتہد فی المذہب (mujtahid fi al-madhhab): A scholar capable of ijtihad but committed to the principles of a specific madhhab.
مقلد محض (muqallid mahd): A mere follower who cannot evaluate evidence and simply follows a mujtahid.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the response quoted from Ibn Amir Haj, what is the status of a mujtahid fi al-madhhab?
A) He is a common muqallid who must blindly follow the imam.
B) He is a mujtahid who has committed not to establish a new madhhab.
C) He is a mujtahid mutlaq who can start a new madhhab.
D) He is not allowed to issue fatwas.

Key Takeaway
The mujtahid fi al-madhhab must know the evidence behind his imam's rulings because he is effectively a mujtahid, not a blind muqallid.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa
intermediate
8 min
The Mujtahid fi al-Madhhab: A Real Mujtahid or a Muqallid?
Debate on whether mujtahid fi al-madhhab must know the imam's evidence

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the relied-upon Hanafi position on whether a mujtahid fi al-madhhab mufti must know the evidence (dalil) of the imam, and identify the proofs and counter-arguments.

Core Idea
A mujtahid fi al-madhhab is a real mujtahid who must know dalil; his commitment not to start a new school does not negate this.

This passage delves into a critical debate: Is the mufti who is a mujtahid fi al-madhhab required to know the evidence behind the imam's rulings? The majority view initially equates him with a common muqallid, but the Hanafi response argues that he is in fact a mujtahid mutlaq in reality, thus necessitating knowledge of the dalil. This distinction has direct implications for how a mufti issues fatwas.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two opposing views
Note the first view (jumhur) that only mujtahid mutlaq needs dalil, and the second (some Mu'tazila) that a scholar must verify the evidence before following.
The second view is closer to the Hanafi position.
2
Analyze the objection against the first meaning of Ibn al-Humam's statement
If the mujtahid fi al-madhhab is like a muqallid, then Ibn al-Humam's rule would improperly require him to know dalil. Understand the contradiction.
3
Follow the Hanafi response via al-Zarkashi and Ibn al-Munir
Al-Zarkashi argues that equating mujtahid fi al-madhhab with a layman is incorrect; Ibn al-Munir states they are mujtahids who have committed to not starting a new school. The evidence is their ijtihad capability and examples of opposing the imam.
'Allamah Shami provides examples of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad opposing Abu Hanifa.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf and mufta bihi
The practical difference: The mujtahid fi al-madhhab mufti must verify the evidence before giving fatwa, while a common muqallid does not. The relied-upon position is that he must know dalil.
