آپ تونی کیسے دیں؟
شرح رسم السنتي
مسائل میں وہ اجتہاد پر قادر نہیں ہے دوسروں کی تقلید کرے گا اور عالم ( جانے والے) کے بارے میں کہا گیا ہے کہ اس پر تقلید اس شرط کے ساتھ لازم ہے کہ اس کے لیے مجتہد کی دلیل کی صحت واضح ہو ورنہ عالم کے لیے اس کی تقلید جائز نہیں ہے اھ (التقریر ج ۳ ص ۳۴۴) اور پہلا قول جمہور کا ہے اور دوسرا بعض معتزلہ کا جیسا کہ تحریر کے شارح نے بیان کیا ہے . پس امام ابن الہمام کا یہ قول کہ جو شخص مجتہد مطلق نہیں ہے اس پر تقلید لازم ہے اور تقلید کی وہ تعریف جو ہم اوپر ذکر کر آئے ہیں، دونوں اس بات پر دلالت کرتے ہیں کہ دلیل کا جاننا صرف مجتہد مطلق پر ضروری ہے۔ دوسروں پر یہ بات لازم نہیں ہے۔ خواہ وہ دوسرا مجتہد فی المذہب ہی کیوں نہ ہو ( خلاصہ اعتراض یہ ہے کہ جمہور کے قول کے مطابق مجتہد فی المذہب مفتی بھی عام مقلدین کی طرح ہے اس کے لیے بھی قول امام کی دلیل جاننا ضروری نہیں ہے پس امام صاحب کے قول کا پہلا مطلب درست نہیں ہے )
جواب:
لیکن التحریر کے شارح علامہ ابن امیر حاج رحمہ اللہ (۳۹) نے شافعی عالم علامہ بد الدین زرکشی رحمہ اللہ (۱۰۲) سے نقل کیا ہے کہ:
مجتہد فی المذہب کو آنکھ بند کر کے محض عامی کے ساتھ لاحق کرنا محل نظر ہے خاص طور پر مذاہب اربعہ کے وسیع علم رکھنے والے متبعین کو ۔ کیونکہ ان حضرات نے اپنے آپ کو عام مقلدین کے مقام پر کھڑا نہیں کیا ہے اور ان کو مجتہدین کے ساتھ لاحق کرنا بھی ممکن نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ ایک مجتہد دوسرے مجتہد کی تقلید نہیں کرتا۔ اور دونوں درجوں کے درمیان کوئی واسطہ بھی نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ حالتیں کل دو ہی ہیں۔ ابن المنیر کہتے ہیں کہ مختار یہ ہے کہ یہ حضرات مجتہد ہیں مگر انہوں نے اس بات کا التزام کیا ہے کہ وہ کوئی نیا مذہب شروع نہیں کریں گے اور ان کے مجتہد ہونے کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ ان میں اجتہاد کی صلاحیتیں موجود ہیں اور ان کے اس التزام کی وجہ کہ وہ کوئی نیا مذ ہب شروع نہیں کریں گے یہ ہے کہ کوئی ایسا نیا مذہب شروع کرنا جس کی جملہ فروعات کے لیے ایسے اصول وقواعد ہوں جو

آپ توی کیسے دیں؟
شرح رسم الملتی
مقدمین کے اصولوں سے علیحدہ ہوں تقریباً ناممکن ہے۔ کیونکہ کہ متقدمین نے تمام ممکن صورتوں کا احاطہ کر لیا ہے۔ ہاں وہ کسی ضابطہ میں کسی امام کی تقلید کر سکتے ہیں پھر اگر کسی خاص جزئیہ میں ان کے لیے اپنے امام کے علاوہ کسی اور امام کے قول کی صحت ظاہر ہو جائے تو اس وقت ان کے لیے اپنے امام کی تقلید جائز نہ ہوگی مگر اس کی مثال ملنا بہت مشکل ہے کیونکہ متقدمین کی نظر بہت وسیع تھی۔ ان (التقرير والتحبير ج ۳ ص ۳۴۵)
مگر علامہ شامی رحمہ اللہ نے منہیہ میں لکھا ہے کہ اس کی مثالیں بکثرت موجود ہیں ۔ امام اعظم رحمہ اللہ کے تلامذہ نے بعض اصول میں اور بہت سی فروع میں امام صاحب کی مخالفت کی ہے۔ پس ابن المنیر کا اس کو مستبعد قرار دینا صحیح نہیں ہے۔ خود علامہ ابن امیر حاج نے تحریر کی
شرح میں اس کی طرف اشارہ کیا ہے۔ خلاصہ جواب یہ ہے کہ مجتہد فی المذہب مفتی در حقیقت مجتہد مطلق ہوتا ہے اس لیے اس پر دلیل اور اس کا حال جاننا ضروری ہے مگر چونکہ اس نے نیا مذ ہب شروع نہ کرنے اور دوسرے مجتہد مطلق کی تقلید کرنے کا التزام کیا ہے اس لیے اس کا شمار مقلدین میں کیا جاتا ہے مگر اس کی
حیثیت عام مقلدین سے ممتاز ہے )
قول امام کا دوسرا مطلب: امام اعظم کے قول میں جو دو احتمال تھے ان میں سے دوسرا احتمال یہ ہے کہ اس ارشاد کا مطلب ہے: امام کے اصولوں سے تخریج و استنباط کر کے امام کے قول کے مطابق فتویٰ دیتا (یعنی امام کا قول کس اصل پر مبنی ہے؟ یہ بات جان کر پھر اس قول پر دوسری جزئیات کو متفرع کرنا ) علامہ ابن الہام رحمہ اللہ الحریر میں اور ابن امیر حاج رحمہ اللہ اس کی شرح التقریر والتجبیر میں فرماتے ہیں: مسئله غیر مجید مفتی کسی مجتہد کے مذہب کے مطابق اس کے اصول پر تخریج کر کے فتویٰ دے سکتا ہے۔ اس کے مذہب کو بعینہ نقل کرنے کا مسئلہ زیر بحث نہیں ہے۔ بشرطیکہ وہ مجتہد کے مبنی سے واقف ہو یعنی وہ مجتہد کے احکام کے ماخذ کو جانتا ہو ان میں غور وفکر کرنے کی صلاحیت رکھتا ہوں مجتہد کے قواعد پر تفریح
How should a fatwa be given? Sharp of Rasm al-Mufti. Regarding matters, one who is not capable of ijtihad will follow others (taqlid). And concerning the scholar (the knowledgeable one), it has been said that taqlid is obligatory upon him on the condition that the correctness of the mujtahid's evidence is clear to him; otherwise, taqlid is not permissible for him. End (al-Taqrir, vol. 3, p. 344). The first statement is of the majority (jumhur), and the second of some Mu'tazila, as explained by the commentator of al-Tahrir. So the statement of Imam Ibn al-Humam that 'the one who is not a mujtahid mutlaq, taqlid is necessary for him, and the definition of taqlid that we mentioned above,' both indicate that knowing the evidence is only necessary for the mujtahid mutlaq. It is not necessary for others, even if that other is a mujtahid fi al-madhhab. (Summary of objection: According to the jumhur's view, the mufti who is a mujtahid fi al-madhhab is like the general muqallid; it is not necessary for him to know the evidence of the imam's statement. So the first meaning of Imam al-Humam's statement is not correct.) Answer: But the commentator of al-Tahrir, 'Allamah Ibn Amir Haj (39), narrated from the Shafi'i scholar 'Allamah Badr al-Din al-Zarkashi (102) that: To blindly equate the mujtahid fi al-madhhab with the common layman is open to consideration, especially regarding the followers who have extensive knowledge of the four schools. Because these people have not placed themselves at the level of common muqallids, nor is it possible to attach them to the mujtahids, for one mujtahid does not follow another mujtahid, and there is no intermediary between the two ranks, because there are only two states. Ibn al-Munir says that the chosen view is that these people are mujtahids, but they have committed that they will not start a new school, and the evidence for their being mujtahids is that they possess the capabilities of ijtihad. And the reason for their commitment not to start a new school is that starting a new school whose entire branches have principles and rules that are separate from the principles of the earlier scholars is almost impossible. Because the earlier scholars have encompassed all possible cases. Yes, they can follow an imam in a certain discipline. Then if, in a particular matter, the correctness of another imam's statement besides their own imam becomes evident to them, then at that time it will not be permissible for them to follow their own imam. But finding an example of this is very difficult because the vision of the early scholars was very broad. (al-Taqrir wa al-Tahbir, vol. 3, p. 345). But 'Allamah Shami, in his Manhiyyah, wrote that examples of this are abundant. The students of Imam A'zam opposed the Imam in some principles and many branches. Therefore, Ibn al-Munir's deeming it improbable is not correct. 'Allamah Ibn Amir Haj himself indicated this in his commentary on al-Tahrir. The summary of the answer is that the mufti who is a mujtahid fi al-madhhab is in reality a mujtahid mutlaq, so knowing the evidence and its condition is necessary for him. But because he has committed not to start a new school and to follow another mujtahid mutlaq, he is counted among the muqallids, but his status is distinct from the common muqallid. Second meaning of the imam's statement: The second of the two possibilities in Imam A'zam's statement is that the meaning of this instruction is: he gives fatwa by takhrij and istinbat from the imam's principles according to the imam's statement (i.e., knowing upon which principle the imam's statement is based, then deriving other issues upon that statement). 'Allamah Ibn al-Humam in al-Tahrir and Ibn Amir Haj in its commentary al-Taqrir wa al-Tahbir state: The issue is that a non-mujtahid mufti can give fatwa by takhrij on the principles of a mujtahid according to his school; the issue of transmitting the school verbatim is not under discussion. Provided that he is aware of the mujtahid's foundation, i.e., he knows the source of the mujtahid's rulings, has the ability to reflect and ponder upon them, and [can] derive [rulings] on the mujtahid's principles.
Source pages p. 81

Commentary
This passage is a debate (ikhtilaf) concerning the status of the mujtahid fi al-madhhab (a scholar capable of ijtihad within the school) and whether he is required to know the evidence (dalil) of the imam. The text first states the view of the majority (jumhur) that only the mujtahid mutlaq must know dalil; the mujtahid fi al-madhhab is like a muqallid. An objection is raised: if this is true, then Imam Ibn al-Humam's statement that 'one who is not a mujtahid mutlaq must do taqlid' would be problematic because it would include the mujtahid fi al-madhhab. The answer is given via a narration from al-Zarkashi and Ibn al-Munir, who argue that the mujtahid fi al-madhhab is actually a mujtahid mutlaq who has committed to not starting a new school. Therefore, he does need to know dalil, though he is counted among the muqallids due to his commitment. The evidence includes the existence of examples where the students of Imam Abu Hanifa opposed him in certain principles and branches, showing they exercised independent ijtihad. The passage then moves to the second meaning of the imam's statement: that the mufti must perform takhrij (derivation) on the imam's principles, not merely transmit. This requires knowledge of the imam's foundational principles. Thus, the overall lesson is that the mujtahid fi al-madhhab must know the evidence; he is not a blind follower.

Key Terms
مجتہد فی المذہب (mujtahid fi al-madhhab): A scholar who has the capacity for ijtihad but commits to following the principles of a particular imam and does not start a new madhhab.
مقلد (muqallid): One who follows a mujtahid without necessarily knowing the evidence. The text distinguishes common muqallids from the mujtahid fi al-madhhab who is considered a muqallid in classification only.
تخریج (takhrij): The process of deriving rulings for new cases based on the established principles and qawaid of the imam, rather than directly transmitting his statements.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon position in this passage, does a mufti who is a mujtahid fi al-madhhab need to know the evidence (dalil) of the imam?
A) No, because he is a muqallid like a common layman.
B) Yes, because he is in reality a mujtahid mutlaq and must know the basis of the rulings.
C) Only if he chooses to start a new madhhab.
D) No, but he must memorize all the imam's rulings.

Key Takeaway
The mujtahid fi al-madhhab mufti must know the evidence (dalil) of the imam; his status is distinct from that of a common muqallid.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa

Conditions for the Mujtahid Fil-Madhhab: The Mufti's Required Qualification
Explaining the second meaning of 'qaul al-imam' and the required qualifications for a mufti

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the three opinions on a mufti's required knowledge of the imam's usul and state the preferred Hanafi view (mukhtar) for fatwa-giving.

Core Idea
A mufti must derive rulings from the imam's principles, not merely transmit them — otherwise fatwa is impermissible in disputed issues.

This passage clarifies the term 'qaul al-imam' (the saying of the Imam) by presenting three scholarly opinions on what qualifies a person to issue fatwa within the Hanafi madhhab. The core debate is whether a mufti must understand and apply the usul of the imam (takhrij) or whether simple transmission (naql) suffices. Understanding this hierarchy is essential for anyone aspiring to the rank of mufti.

Guided Path
1
Identify the second meaning of 'qaul al-imam'
Recognize that the second meaning refers to deriving fatwa by takhrij (extraction) from the imam's principles, not just transmitting his words.
This is the foundation of the mujtahid fil-madhhab concept.
2
List the three opinions on mufti qualification
Extract the three views: (1) mufti must know the usul and be capable of takhrij, (2) allowed only if no absolute mujtahid exists, (3) absolutely permissible as mere transmission.
The first is preferred; the second is weak; the third is rebutted.
3
Note the evidence and rebuttals
For the first: narration from Abu Yusuf and Zufar. For the third: mufti as naql. Rebuttal: distinction between naql and takhrij.
The third opinion conflates transmission with derivation.
4
Identify the preferred view (mukhtar)
The preferred view is the first: mufti must be a mujtahid fil-madhhab, possessing full access to the imam's principles and ability to debate.
This view is chosen by many verifiers, including Ibn al-Humann and others.
5
Apply the rule: distinguish takhrij from naql
Understand that transmitting existing rulings is allowed, but deriving new rulings (takhrij) requires ijtihad within the madhhab.
This distinction is crucial for avoiding error in fatwa.

Source Text

قول امام کا دوسرا مطلب: امام اعظم کے قول میں جو دو احتمال تھے ان میں سے دوسرا احتمال یہ ہے کہ اس ارشاد کا مطلب ہے: امام کے اصولوں سے تخریج و استنباط کر کے امام کے قول کے مطابق فتویٰ دیتا (یعنی امام کا قول کس اصل پر مبنی ہے؟ یہ بات جان کر پھر اس قول پر دوسری جزئیات کو متفرع کرنا ) علامہ ابن الہام رحمہ اللہ الحریر میں اور ابن امیر حاج رحمہ اللہ اس کی شرح التقریر والتجبیر میں فرماتے ہیں: مسئله غیر مجید مفتی کسی مجتہد کے مذہب کے مطابق اس کے اصول پر تخریج کر کے فتویٰ دے سکتا ہے۔ اس کے مذہب کو بعینہ نقل کرنے کا مسئلہ زیر بحث نہیں ہے۔ بشرطیکہ وہ مجتہد کے مبنی سے واقف ہو یعنی وہ مجتہد کے احکام کے ماخذ کو جانتا ہو ان میں غور وفکر کرنے کی صلاحیت رکھتا ہوں مجتہد کے قواعد پر تفریح کرنے پر قادر ہوا فرق و جمع پر اس کو پوری قدرت حاصل ہو اور اس بارے میں مباحثہ کر سکتا ہو ۔ غرض اسے پوری دسترس حاصل ہو کہ وہ نئی جزئیات کے احکام جو صاحب مذہب سے مروی نہیں ہیں، امام کے اصولوں سے مستنبط کرے اور ایسا ہی شخص مجتہد فی المذہب کہلاتا ہے اور جو شخص ایسی صلاحیتوں کا مالک نہیں ہے اس کے لیے فتویٰ دینا جائز نہیں ہے۔“ اور ہندی کی شرح بدیع (۹۷) میں ہے کہ: ” ہمارے اصحاب میں سے اور دوسرے حضرات میں سے بہت سے محققین کے نزدیک یہی قول مختار ہے کیونکہ ہمارے ائمہ میں سے امام ابو یوسف اور امام زفر وغیر ہما سے یہ قول مروی ہے کہ کسی کے لیے بھی ہمارے قول پر فتوی دینا جائز نہیں ہے جب تک وہ جان نہ لے کہ ہم نے کہاں سے قول کیا ہے؟“ اور بعض حضرات نے یہی بات بایں الفاظ کہی ہے کہ " جس کو اقوال یاد ہوں اور دلائل نہ جانتا ہو تو اس کے لیے مختلف فیہ مسائل میں فتوی دینا جائز نہیں ہے۔" اور دوسرا قول یہ ہے کہ: اگر کوئی مجتہد موجود نہ ہو تو فتوی دینا درست ہے اور اس قول کو علامہ ابن الہمام نے ضعیف قرار دیا ہے۔ اور تیسرا قول یہ ہے کہ: " مطلقاً فتونی دینا جائز ہے، یعنی خواہ وہ مآخذ سے واقف ہو یا نہ ہو اور خواہ کوئی مجتہد موجود ہو یا نہ ہو۔ یہ قول صاحب بدیع علامہ ابن السماعاتی (۱۰۳) کا اور بہت سے علماء کا مختار ہے۔ کیونکہ وہ مفتی محض ناقل ہے اور نقل میں عالم ( مجتہد ) اور غیر عالم کے درمیان کوئی فرق نہیں ہے۔ مگر ان حضرات کی دلیل کا یہ جواب دیا گیا ہے کہ نقل کے سلسلہ میں تو کوئی اختلاف نہیں ہے۔ اختلاف تخریج کے سلسلہ میں ہے۔ کیونکہ کسی مجتہد کے مذہب کو بعینہ نقل کرنا قبول روایت کی شرائط مثلاً عدالت وغیرہ کے ساتھ بالاتفاق جائز ہے ( دونوں کتابوں کی عبارت تلخیص کر کے پیش کی گئی ہے اور وہ یہاں پوری ہوئی۔ دیکھئے التقریر ج ۳ ص ۳۴۶) فوائد میں ( علامہ شامی ) کہتا ہوں کہ سراج الدین ہندی رحمہ اللہ (۹۷) کی ذکر کردہ باتوں سے درج ذیل امور واضح ہوتے ہیں۔
The second meaning of the saying of the Imam: Among the two probabilities in the statement of Imam A'zam, the second probability is that this instruction means: he gives fatwa in accordance with the Imam's statement by extracting and deducing from the Imam's principles (i.e., he knows on which principle the Imam's statement is based, then he derives other particulars from that statement). Allama Ibn al-Humann in al-Tahrir and Ibn Amir Hajj in its commentary al-Taqrir wa al-Tahbir say: An unauthenticated issue: a mufti can give fatwa by making takhrij on the principles of a mujtahid according to his madhhab. The issue of transmitting his madhhab exactly is not under discussion. Provided that he is aware of the basis of the mujtahid, i.e., he knows the sources of the mujtahid's rulings, has the ability to reflect on them, is capable of deriving from the mujtahid's rules, has full power over distinction and combination, and can debate in this matter. In short, he has full access so that he can deduce the rulings of new particulars that are not narrated from the master of the madhhab from the Imam's principles. Such a person is called a mujtahid fil-madhhab, and for one who does not possess such abilities, issuing fatwa is not permissible. And in Hindi's Sharh Badi' (97) it is stated: According to many verifiers among our associates and others, this saying is chosen because from our Imams, Imam Abu Yusuf and Imam Zufar and others narrated this statement: 'It is not permissible for anyone to give fatwa on our saying until he knows from where we said it.' And some people said the same in these words: 'He who remembers the sayings but does not know the proofs, it is not permissible for him to give fatwa in disputed issues.' The second saying is: If no mujtahid is present, then giving fatwa is correct, and Allama Ibn al-Humann declared this saying weak. And the third saying is: 'Absolutely giving fatwa is permissible, i.e., whether he is aware of the sources or not, and whether a mujtahid is present or not.' This is the chosen view of the author of Badi', Allama Ibn al-Sima'ati (103), and many scholars, because the mufti is merely a transmitter, and in transmission there is no difference between a scholar (mujtahid) and a non-scholar. But the response to their proof is: There is no disagreement regarding transmission. The disagreement is regarding takhrij. Because transmitting the exact madhhab of a mujtahid is unanimously permissible with the conditions of accepting narration such as uprightness, etc. (The text of both books has been summarized and presented here, and it is complete here. See al-Taqrir vol. 3 p. 346). Benefits: I (Allama Shami) say: From the statements mentioned by Siraj al-Din Hindi (97), the following matters become clear.
Source pages p. 82

Commentary
This passage discusses the second interpretation of the phrase 'qaul al-imam' in the context of fatwa-giving. It clarifies that a mufti who is a mujtahid fil-madhhab must be able to derive rulings from the foundational principles (usul) of the imam of the madhhab, not merely transmit existing rulings. The passage presents three opinions on whether a mufti needs knowledge of the imam's sources: (1) the preferred view (from Abu Yusuf and Zufar) that it is required, (2) a weaker view allowing fatwa in absence of a mujtahid, and (3) the view that a mufti is merely a transmitter and needs no such knowledge. The author favors the first, as it preserves the integrity of ijtihad within the madhhab.

Key Terms
مجتہد فی المذہب (mujtahid fil-madhhab): A person who can derive rulings on new cases by applying the principles of a specific imam (e.g., Abu Hanifa) to new particulars, without being an absolute mujtahid.
تخریج (takhrij): The process of deriving a ruling for a new case from the established principles of the imam, by analogy or extension.
نقل (naql): Mere transmission of the imam's existing rulings without understanding their basis or ability to derive new rulings.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the preferred view (مختار) in this passage, what is required of a mufti in the Hanafi madhhab?
A) He must memorize all the rulings of Imam Abu Hanifa.
B) He must be able to derive rulings from the imam's principles (usul).
C) He must be an absolute mujtahid independent of any madhhab.
D) He must only transmit the exact words of the imam without any derivation.

Key Takeaway
The mufta bihi view is that a Hanafi mufti must be a mujtahid fil-madhhab, capable of deriving rulings from Imam Abu Hanifa's usul, not merely transmitting them.

The Ijtihad Requirement for Fatwa
Discussion on qualifications for fatwa and three scholarly opinions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three scholarly opinions on giving fatwa and identify the mufta bihi position of the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Fatwa requires knowledge of sources and derivation; mere transmission is insufficient for new cases.

Issuing a fatwa is a serious responsibility. This passage addresses a fundamental question: must a mufti be a mujtahid? The Hanafi school presents three opinions, ranging from strict prohibition to absolute permission. Understanding these opinions and their evidence is crucial for any future mufti.

Guided Path
1
Define mujtahid fil-madhhab
Understand the third level of mujtahid: one who can derive rulings from the Imam's principles for new cases not found in transmitted texts.
This is the minimum qualification according to the first opinion.
2
Identify the three opinions
Distinguish between: 1) impermissible without knowledge of sources (mukhtar), 2) permissible only if no mujtahid exists (weak), 3) absolutely permissible (Ibn al-Sama'ati).
Each opinion has a different view on the mufti's role.
3
Analyze the evidence for each
Examine the dalil: first opinion relies on narrations from Abu Yusuf and Zufar; third opinion compares mufti to a transmitter. Note the Hanafi response distinguishing transmission from derivation.
The core distinction is between naql (transmission) and takhrij (derivation).
4
Determine the tarjih
The first opinion is the mufta bihi according to most Hanafi scholars, as stated in al-Hindi's commentary. Ibn al-Humam declared the second opinion weak.
Tarjih is based on strength of dalil and scholarly consensus.
5
Apply the thamarah al-khilaf
Practically, a non-mujtahid may transmit established rulings (naql) but cannot issue fatwa on new or disputed cases (takhrij). This protects the integrity of fatwa.
The third opinion's allowance is limited to transmission, not independent ijtihad.

فوائد
میں ( علامہ شامی ) کہتا ہوں کہ سراج الدین ہندی رحمہ اللہ (۹۷) کی ذکر کردہ باتوں سے درج ذیل امور واضح ہوتے ہیں۔

(1) یہ بات کہ لا يحل لا حدان يفتى الخ امام اعظم رحمہ اللہ کے اقوال کے ساتھ
خاص نہیں ہے بلکہ ان کے تلامذہ کے اقوال کی صورت حال بھی یہی ہے۔
(۲) مجتہد فی المذہب سے مراد سابق میں ذکر کردہ طبقات سبعہ میں سے تیسرے طبقہ کے لوگ ہیں ( دوسرے طبقہ کے حضرات مراد نہیں ہیں کیونکہ ہندی نے امام ابو یوسف اور امام زفر و غیر ہما کے قول پر بحث کی ہے اور یہ حضرات دوسرے طبقہ کے ہیں )
(۳) دوسرے طبقہ والے جو امام اعظم رحمہ اللہ کے تلامذہ ہیں وہ مجتہد مطلق ہیں البتہ وہ امام اعظم کی ان کے اکثر اصول وضوابط میں تقلید کرتے ہیں اور اس تقلید کی دو بنیادیں ہو
سکتی ہیں ۔ (الف) یا تو اس وجہ سے تقلید کرتے ہیں کہ ایک مجتہد کے لیے دوسرے مجتہد کی تقلید جائز ہے اور اس مسئلہ میں امام صاحب سے دو روایتیں مروی ہیں اور جواز کی روایت کی تائید امام ابو یوسف کے ایک واقعہ سے ہوتی ہے کہ جب آپ نے جمعہ کی نماز پڑھ لی تو لوگوں نے آپ کو بتایا کہ حمام کے حوض میں چوہا پایا گیا ہے تو آپ نے فرمایا کہ: "ہم اہل مدینہ (امام مالک) کی تقلید کرتے ہیں اور امام محمد رحمہ اللہ سے مروی ہے کہ مجتہد مطلق اپنے سے بڑے ذی علم کی تقلید
کر سکتا ہے۔ (ب) یا اس وجہ سے تقلید کرتے ہیں کہ ان کا اجتہاد اس مسئلہ میں امام اعظم کے اجتہاد کے موافق ہو گیا ہے۔ چنانچہ اسی قسم کی بات بعض شوافع سے مروی ہے۔ مثلاً علامہ ابو بکر محمد بن علی بن اسماعیل قفال شاشی رحمہ اللہ ( د ۲۹ ف ۳۶۵ھ) شیخ ابو علی حسن بن حاجب بن حمید شاشی رحمہ اللہ ( متوفی ۳۱۴ ھ ) اور قاضی حسین بن محمد مرور و زی رحمہ اللہ (متوفی ۳۶۲ھ) فرمایا کرتے تھے کہ ہم امام شافعی کے مقلد نہیں ہیں بلکہ ہماری رائے ان کی رائے کے موافق ہو
گئی ہے۔ اسی قسم کی بات امام ابوحنیفہ کے تلاندہ مثالی امام ابو یوسف اور امام محمد کے بارے میں بدرجہ اولی کہی جاسکتی ہے۔ کیونکہ ان حضرات نے بہت کی جزئیات میں امام صاحب کی مخالفت کی
ے آپ کا مرو الروز میں انتقال ہوا ہے ( اعلام ۲ ص ۲۰۴)
1 + How do you give fatwa? Ar. The condition of Rasm al-Mufti: He must be capable of distinguishing and combining (different evidences) and have full ability to discuss it. In short, he must have complete command so that he can derive rulings for new particulars not transmitted from the founder of the school from the Imam's principles. Such a person is called a mujtahid fil-madhhab. One who does not possess these abilities is not permitted to give fatwa. And in al-Hindi's commentary on al-Badi' (97) it says: "This is the chosen opinion according to many researchers among our associates and others, because it is narrated from our Imams, Abu Yusuf and Zufar and others, that it is not permissible for anyone to give fatwa on our statement unless he knows from where we made the statement." And some scholars said in these words: "One who memorizes the statements but does not know the evidences, it is not permissible for him to give fatwa in disputed issues." The second opinion is: If there is no mujtahid present, then giving fatwa is correct, but Allamah Ibn al-Humam declared this weak. The third opinion is: "Giving fatwa is absolutely permissible, whether he is aware of the sources or not, and whether a mujtahid is present or not. This is the chosen opinion of the author of al-Badi', Allamah Ibn al-Sama'ati (103), and many scholars. Because the mufti is merely a transmitter, and in transmission there is no difference between a scholar (mujtahid) and a non-scholar." However, the response to their evidence is that there is no dispute in transmission; the dispute is in derivation. Because transmitting the exact words of a mujtahid's school, with the conditions of accepting a narration such as integrity etc., is unanimously permissible. (The text of both books has been summarized and presented here fully. See al-Taqrir, vol. 3, p. 346) Benefits: I (Allamah Shami) say that from the points mentioned by Siraj al-Din al-Hindi (97), the following matters become clear: (1) The ruling 'لا يحل لأحد أن يفتي' (It is not permissible for anyone to give fatwa) is not exclusive to Imam Azam's statements, but the same situation applies to the statements of his students. (2) By mujtahid fil-madhhab is meant the people of the third level among the previously mentioned seven levels (not the second level, because al-Hindi discussed the statement of Imam Abu Yusuf, Imam Zufar, and others, and these are from the second level). (3) The second level, who are the students of Imam Azam, are absolute mujtahids, but they follow the Imam (تقليد) in most of his principles and rules. This following can have two bases: (a) Either they follow because it is permissible for one mujtahid to follow another mujtahid, and there are two narrations from Imam on this issue. The permissibility narration is supported by an incident of Imam Abu Yusuf: when he finished the Friday prayer, people informed him that a mouse was found in the bath's reservoir, so he said: 'We follow the people of Madinah (Imam Malik)' and it is narrated from Imam Muhammad that an absolute mujtahid can follow someone more knowledgeable than him. (b) Or they follow because their ijtihad happened to coincide with Imam Azam's ijtihad in that issue. Similar statements are narrated from some Shafi'i scholars, e.g., Allamah Abu Bakr Muhammad bin Ali bin Ismail al-Qaffal al-Shashi (d. 365 AH), Shaykh Abu Ali al-Hasan bin Hajib bin Hamid al-Shashi (d. 314 AH), and Qadi Husayn bin Muhammad al-Marwaruzi (d. 362 AH). They used to say: 'We are not followers of Imam Shafi'i, rather our opinion coincided with his opinion.' The same can be said, with more reason, about Imam Abu Hanifa's students like Imam Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad, because they opposed the Imam in many particulars. He passed away in Marw al-Rudh (A'lam, 2:204).
Source pages p. 83

Commentary
This passage is a discussion on the qualifications required for issuing fatwa within the Hanafi school. It begins by stating the condition that a person must be a mujtahid fil-madhhab, meaning one who can derive rulings for new cases from the principles of Imam Abu Hanifa. The author then presents three scholarly opinions on the permissibility of fatwa for those who lack this ability. The first opinion, attributed to Imam Abu Yusuf and Imam Zufar and considered the strongest by many, holds that it is impermissible to give fatwa without knowing the sources of the school. The second opinion, declared weak by Ibn al-Humam, allows fatwa only when no mujtahid is present. The third opinion, favored by Ibn al-Sama'ati and others, permits fatwa absolutely because the mufti is merely a transmitter. The response to this third opinion clarifies that the dispute is not about transmission but about derivation (takhrij). Following this, Allamah Shami extracts benefits from the earlier discussion: First, the ruling of Imam Azam applies equally to his students. Second, 'mujtahid fil-madhhab' refers to the third level of scholars, not the second (which includes Abu Yusuf and Zufar). Third, the second-level mujtahids are absolute mujtahids but they follow the Imam either because it is permissible for one mujtahid to follow another, or because their own ijtihad coincided with his. Examples from Shafi'i scholars illustrate the latter point. The passage thus clarifies the hierarchy of muftis and the conditions under which fatwa is valid.

Key Terms
مجتہد فی المذہب (mujtahid fil-madhhab): A person capable of deriving rulings for new cases not found in transmitted texts, using the principles of Imam Abu Hanifa.
مفتی محض ناقل (mufti mahd naqil): A mufti who merely transmits the established rulings of the school without independent reasoning.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the first opinion (mukhtar), why is it impermissible for a non-mujtahid to give fatwa?
A) Because he cannot ensure the transmission is accurate.
B) Because he does not know the source and reasoning behind the ruling.
C) Because he lacks justice and integrity.
D) Because it is forbidden for anyone to give fatwa nowadays.

Key Takeaway
The relied-upon Hanafi position is that a mufti must be a mujtahid fil-madhhab, capable of deriving rulings from the school's principles.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa
intermediate
8 min
The Principle of Fatwa: Knowing the Derivation
Explaining the principle and hierarchy of fatwa giving.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule that a fatwa requires knowledge of the derivation and distinguish between mujtahid mutlaq and mujtahid fil madhhab.

Core Idea
A fatwa from the madhhab is not permissible unless the mufti knows how the ruling was derived.

In this passage, the author explains a foundational principle of Hanafi fatwa: it is not enough to simply know the ruling of Imam Abu Hanifa; one must understand the methodology (manhaj) behind it. This applies equally to the rulings of his students. The passage then defines who is qualified to give fatwa by istinbat and takhrij within the madhhab.

Guided Path
1
Identify the rule
Find the Arabic statement of the rule: 'لا يحل لأحد أن يفتي بقولنا حتى يعلم من أين قلنا'. Understand its meaning: giving fatwa with the madhhab's qawl requires knowing the source and derivation.
This rule is a foundational qawida for muftis.
2
Clarify the scope
The rule applies to Imam Abu Hanifa's statements and also to his students' statements. It is not limited to a single imam.
3
Distinguish between mujtahid mutlaq and mujtahid fil madhhab
The passage explains that the second tabaqah (Abu Yusuf, Muhammad, Zufar) are mujtahid mutlaq, but they follow Imam Abu Hanifa in most principles. The third, fourth, and fifth tabaqah are mujtahid fil madhhab who derive rulings within the madhhab's methodology.
Note: mujtahid mutlaq can give fatwa independently, but they chose to follow Imam Abu Hanifa.
4
Understand the two reasons for their taqlid
Either because a mujtahid can follow another (permissibility), supported by the incident of Abu Yusuf and Imam Malik, or because their ijtihad coincides with the imam's.
This shows the flexibility within the madhhab.

ان جزئیات کی تخریج امام شافعی کے ضوابط پر نہ کی ہو ( منبہیہ تمام ہوا ) ۔ خلاصه کلام مذکورہ بالا گفتگو سے یہ بات متحقق ہوئی کہ امام اعظم اور ان کے تلامذہ کا یہ قول کہ لا يحل لأحد أن يفتي بقولنا حتى يعلم من أين قلنا؟ کا مصداق مجتہد فی المذہب کا استنباط و تخریج کے طور پر فتوی دینا ہے (یعنی اس کے دو مطلبوں میں سے دوسرا مطلب صحیح ہے ) جیسا کہ تحریر اور شرح بدیع کی عبارتوں سے معلوم ہوا۔ مجتہد فی المذہب کون ہے؟ اور ظاہر یہ ہے کہ طبقہ ثالثہ رابعہ اور خالصہ والے مجتہد فی المذہب ہیں اور دیگر حضرات کو نقل پر اکتفا کرنی چاہیے اور ہمارے ذمہ ما بعد طبقات والے ان طبقات ثلاثہ والوں سے جو نقل کریں اس کی پیروی کرنا ہے یعنی ان کے وہ استنباطات جن کے بارے میں متقدمین سے کوئی صراحت مروی نہیں ہے اور ان کی متقدمین کے اقوال میں ترجیحات اگر چہ وہ امام صاحب کے علاوہ کے قول کو ترجیح دیں۔ جیسا کہ ہم اس بحث کے آغاز میں مفصل بیان کر آئے ہیں ۔
How do you give a fatwa? (1) This statement that 'It is not permissible for anyone to give a fatwa with our saying until he knows from where we said it' is not specific to Imam A'zam's statements, but the condition of his students' statements is also the same. (2) By 'mujtahid fil madhhab' is meant the people of the third class among the previously mentioned seven classes (the people of the second class are not meant because Hindi discussed the statement of Abu Yusuf, Zufar, and others, and these people are of the second class). (3) Those of the second class who are students of Imam A'zam are mujtahid mutlaq, but they follow Imam A'zam in most of his principles and regulations, and this following can have two bases: (a) either they follow because it is permissible for one mujtahid to follow another mujtahid, and on this issue two narrations are transmitted from Imam Sahib, and the narration of permissibility is supported by an incident of Imam Abu Yusuf: when he had prayed Jumu'ah, people told him that a mouse was found in the tank of the bathhouse, so he said, 'We follow the people of Madinah (Imam Malik)'; and it is narrated from Imam Muhammad that a mujtahid mutlaq can follow a greater scholar. (b) Or they follow because their ijtihad in that issue coincided with Imam A'zam's ijtihad. Accordingly, a similar kind of statement is narrated from some Shafi'is. For example, Allama Abu Bakr Muhammad bin Ali bin Ismail Qaffal Shashi (d. 365 AH), Sheikh Abu Ali Hasan bin Hajib bin Humaid Shashi (d. 314 AH), and Qadi Husain bin Muhammad Marwazi (d. 362 AH) used to say: 'We are not followers of Imam Shafi'i; rather, our opinion has coincided with his opinion.' The same kind of statement can be said a fortiori about Imam Abu Hanifa's students like Imam Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad, because these people contradicted Imam Sahib in many details. He died in Marw al-Rudh (A'lam 2:204). This is evidence that they are not his followers. Nevertheless, the statements of these students will not be excluded from the Hanafi madhhab, as its detail has passed before. Allama Shami wrote in Manhiya: 'Then I saw a writing of a reliable scholar which is exactly this: Ibn al-Mulqin (104) said in Tabaqat al-Shafi'iyyah: Beneficial point. Ibn Burhan (105) said in al-Awsat: There is disagreement among our seniors and Hanafi seniors regarding Imam Muzani (102), Ibn Suraij (107), Imam Abu Yusuf, and Imam Muhammad. Some call them mujtahid mutlaq and some mujtahid fil madhhab. And Imam al-Haramayn (108) said: In my opinion, all of Imam Muzani's opinions are takhrijat because he did not contradict Imam Shafi'i in principles. His case is not like that of Imam Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad, because both of them contradict their imam even in principles. And Imam Rafi'i (109) said in Bab al-Wudu: Imam Muzani's singular opinions will not be counted in the Shafi'i madhhab when Imam Muzani did not derive those details on the basis of Imam Shafi'i's principles. (Manhiya finished).' Summary: From the above discussion, it became certain that the application of the statement of Imam A'zam and his students, 'It is not permissible for anyone to give a fatwa with our saying until he knows from where we said it,' is that the mujtahid fil madhhab gives fatwa by way of istinbat and takhrij (i.e., the second meaning of its two meanings is correct), as understood from the expressions of Tahrir and Sharh Badi'. Who is mujtahid fil madhhab? It is apparent that the third, fourth, and fifth classes are mujtahid fil madhhab, and others should suffice with naql (transmission). And upon us, the later classes, is to follow what the three classes transmit, i.e., their istinbatat regarding which no explicit statement from the early scholars is transmitted, and their tarjihat (preferences) among the statements of the early scholars, even if they prefer a statement other than Imam Sahib's; as we have explained in detail at the beginning of this discussion.
Source pages p. 84

Commentary
This passage is an explanation of a foundational principle of Hanafi fatwa: 'It is not permissible for anyone to give a fatwa with our saying until he knows from where we said it.' The author begins by clarifying that this rule applies not only to Imam Abu Hanifa but also to his senior students. He then defines 'mujtahid fil madhhab' as the third class of the seven classes, not the second class. The second class (Abu Yusuf, Muhammad, Zufar) are mujtahid mutlaq, but they follow Imam Abu Hanifa in most principles. Two reasons are given: either because a mujtahid may follow another mujtahid, supported by Abu Yusuf's incident where he followed Imam Malik on the issue of a mouse in a bathhouse, or because their ijtihad coincided with Imam Abu Hanifa's. The author then cites Allama Shami quoting an inter-madhhab comparison: some Shafi'i scholars debated whether Imam Muzani was mujtahid mutlaq or mujtahid fil madhhab, contrasting him with Abu Yusuf and Muhammad who contradicted their imam even in principles. The conclusion is that the rule applies primarily to mujtahid fil madhhab giving fatwa by istinbat and takhrij. The third, fourth, and fifth classes are identified as mujtahid fil madhhab; others must rely on naql. The lower classes follow what these three classes transmit, including their preferences even if they differ from Imam Abu Hanifa.

Key Terms
مجتهد في المذهب (mujtahid fil madhhab): A jurist of the third tabaqah who can derive rulings within the confines of the madhhab's principles and methodology.
مجتهد مطلق (mujtahid mutlaq): An independent jurist capable of ijtihad without adherence to a particular madhhab, of the second tabaqah.
طبقات سبعہ (tabaqat sab'ah): The seven classes of mujtahids in the Hanafi madhhab as per Rasm al-Mufti.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what does the phrase 'لا يحل لأحد أن يفتي بقولنا حتى يعلم من أين قلنا' mean for fatwa?
A) Only Imam Abu Hanifa's students can give fatwa.
B) A mufti must know the derivation of the ruling before giving it.
C) It is permissible to give fatwa without knowing the source if the ruling is well-known.
D) Mujtahid mutlaq are exempt from this rule.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi madhhab requires that anyone giving fatwa based on the imam's rulings must understand the derivation, not just the ruling itself.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa
advanced
10 min
Classification of the Sahibayn: Mujtahid Mutlaq or Mujtahid fil Madhhab?
Explaining the classification dispute and its resolution.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi classification of Imam Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad as mujtahid mutlaq and evaluate the opposing view.

Core Idea
Imam Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad are mujtahid mutlaq because they contradicted Imam Abu Hanifa in principles, yet their rulings remain within the madhhab.

This passage delves into a nuanced debate about the status of Imam Abu Hanifa's senior students. Some scholars, including from the Shafi'i school, classified them as mujtahid fil madhhab, akin to Imam Muzani. However, the Hanafi position asserts they are mujtahid mutlaq due to their independent ijtihad in principles. The passage uses this discussion to clarify the definition of mujtahid fil madhhab.

Guided Path
1
Identify the dispute
The passage presents a disagreement: are Imam Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad mujtahid mutlaq or mujtahid fil madhhab? Some Hanafi and Shafi'i scholars lean toward the latter.
2
Present the Hanafi evidence
The Hanafi position is that they are mujtahid mutlaq because they contradicted Imam Abu Hanifa in principles (usul), not just in details (furu).
3
Compare with Imam Muzani
Imam al-Haramayn argued that Imam Muzani did not contradict Imam Shafi'i in principles, so he is mujtahid fil madhhab, unlike the Sahibayn.
This distinction is key.
4
Understand the practical implication
A mujtahid mutlaq's fatwa can override a clear text of the madhhab in some cases, whereas a mujtahid fil madhhab cannot. This affects fatwa practice.

آپ فتوی کیسے دیں؟ (1) یہ بات کہ لا يحل لأحد أن يفتي بقولنا حتى يعلم من أين قلنا؟ امام اعظم رحمہ اللہ کے اقوال کے ساتھ خاص نہیں ہے بلکہ ان کے تلامذہ کے اقوال کی صورت حال بھی یہی ہے۔ (۲) مجتہد فی المذہب سے مراد سابق میں ذکر کردہ طبقات سبعہ میں سے تیسرے طبقہ کے لوگ ہیں ( دوسرے طبقہ کے حضرات مراد نہیں ہیں کیونکہ ہندی نے امام ابو یوسف اور امام زفر و غیر ہما کے قول پر بحث کی ہے اور یہ حضرات دوسرے طبقہ کے جمعہ کی نماز پڑھ لی تو لوگوں نے آپ کو بتایا کہ حمام کے حوض میں چوہا پایا گیا ہے تو آپ نے فرمایا کہ: 'ہم اہل مدینہ (امام مالک) کی تقلید کرتے ہیں' اور امام محمد رحمہ اللہ سے مروی ہے کہ مجتہد مطلق اپنے سے بڑے ذی علم کی تقلید کر سکتا ہے۔ (ب) یا اس وجہ سے تقلید کرتے ہیں کہ ان کا اجتہاد اس مسئلہ میں امام اعظم کے اجتہاد کے موافق ہو گیا ہے۔ چنانچہ اسی قسم کی بات بعض شوافع سے مروی ہے۔ مثلاً علامہ ابو بکر محمد بن علی بن اسماعیل قفال شاشی رحمہ اللہ (د ۳۶۵ھ) شیخ ابو علی حسن بن حاجب بن حمید شاشی رحمہ اللہ (متوفی ۳۱۴ھ) اور قاضی حسین بن محمد مروروزی رحمہ اللہ (متوفی ۳۶۲ھ) فرمایا کرتے تھے کہ ہم امام شافعی کے مقلد نہیں ہیں بلکہ ہماری رائے ان کی رائے کے موافق ہو گئی ہے۔ اسی قسم کی بات امام ابوحنیفہ کے تلامذہ مثالی امام ابو یوسف اور امام محمد کے بارے میں بدرجہ اولی کہی جاسکتی ہے۔ کیونکہ ان حضرات نے بہت سی جزئیات میں امام صاحب کی مخالفت کی ہے۔ آپ کا مروالروز میں انتقال ہوا ہے ( اعلام ۲ ص ۲۰۴) یہ ہے جو ان کے مقلد نہ ہونے کی دلیل ہے۔ مگر بایں ہمہ ان تلامذہ کے اقوال مذہب حنفی سے خارج نہ ہوں گے جیسا کہ اس کی تفصیل پہلے گزر چکی ہے۔ علامہ شامی رحمہ اللہ نے منہیہ میں لکھا ہے کہ پھر میں نے ایک قابل اعتماد عالم کی تحریر دیکھی جو بعینہ یہ ہے کہ ابن الملقن (۱۰۴) نے طبقات الشافعیہ میں فرمایا ہے۔ فائده ابن برہان (۱۰۵) نے اوسط میں فرمایا ہے کہ ہمارے اکابر اور حنفی اکابر میں امام مزنی (۱۰۲) ابن سریج (۱۰۷) امام ابو یوسف اور امام محمد کے بارے میں اختلاف ہوا ہے۔ بعض ان کو مجتہد مطلق کہتے ہیں اور بعض مجتہد فی المذہب اور امام الحرمین (۱۰۸) نے فرمایا ہے کہ میرے خیال میں امام مزنی کی تمام رائے تخریجات ہیں کیونکہ انہوں نے امام شافعی کی اصول میں مخالفت نہیں کی ہے۔ ان کا معاملہ امام ابو یوسف اور امام محمد جیسا نہیں ہے کیونکہ وہ دونوں حضرات اصول میں بھی اپنے امام کی مخالفت کرتے ہیں اور امام رافعی (۱۰۹) نے باب الوضو میں فرمایا ہے کہ امام مزنی کے تفردات مذہب شافعی میں شمار نہیں کئے جائیں گے جب کہ امام مزنی نے آغاز میں مفصل بیان کر آئے ہیں ۔
How do you give a fatwa? (1) This statement that 'It is not permissible for anyone to give a fatwa with our saying until he knows from where we said it' is not specific to Imam A'zam's statements, but the condition of his students' statements is also the same. (2) By 'mujtahid fil madhhab' is meant the people of the third class among the previously mentioned seven classes (the people of the second class are not meant because Hindi discussed the statement of Abu Yusuf, Zufar, and others, and these people are of the second class). (3) Those of the second class who are students of Imam A'zam are mujtahid mutlaq, but they follow Imam A'zam in most of his principles and regulations, and this following can have two bases: (a) either they follow because it is permissible for one mujtahid to follow another mujtahid, and on this issue two narrations are transmitted from Imam Sahib, and the narration of permissibility is supported by an incident of Imam Abu Yusuf: when he had prayed Jumu'ah, people told him that a mouse was found in the tank of the bathhouse, so he said, 'We follow the people of Madinah (Imam Malik)'; and it is narrated from Imam Muhammad that a mujtahid mutlaq can follow a greater scholar. (b) Or they follow because their ijtihad in that issue coincided with Imam A'zam's ijtihad. Accordingly, a similar kind of statement is narrated from some Shafi'is. For example, Allama Abu Bakr Muhammad bin Ali bin Ismail Qaffal Shashi (d. 365 AH), Sheikh Abu Ali Hasan bin Hajib bin Humaid Shashi (d. 314 AH), and Qadi Husain bin Muhammad Marwazi (d. 362 AH) used to say: 'We are not followers of Imam Shafi'i; rather, our opinion has coincided with his opinion.' The same kind of statement can be said a fortiori about Imam Abu Hanifa's students like Imam Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad, because these people contradicted Imam Sahib in many details. He died in Marw al-Rudh (A'lam 2:204). This is evidence that they are not his followers. Nevertheless, the statements of these students will not be excluded from the Hanafi madhhab, as its detail has passed before. Allama Shami wrote in Manhiya: 'Then I saw a writing of a reliable scholar which is exactly this: Ibn al-Mulqin (104) said in Tabaqat al-Shafi'iyyah: Beneficial point. Ibn Burhan (105) said in al-Awsat: There is disagreement among our seniors and Hanafi seniors regarding Imam Muzani (102), Ibn Suraij (107), Imam Abu Yusuf, and Imam Muhammad. Some call them mujtahid mutlaq and some mujtahid fil madhhab. And Imam al-Haramayn (108) said: In my opinion, all of Imam Muzani's opinions are takhrijat because he did not contradict Imam Shafi'i in principles. His case is not like that of Imam Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad, because both of them contradict their imam even in principles. And Imam Rafi'i (109) said in Bab al-Wudu: Imam Muzani's singular opinions will not be counted in the Shafi'i madhhab when Imam Muzani did not derive those details on the basis of Imam Shafi'i's principles. (Manhiya finished).' Summary: From the above discussion, it became certain that the application of the statement of Imam A'zam and his students, 'It is not permissible for anyone to give a fatwa with our saying until he knows from where we said it,' is that the mujtahid fil madhhab gives fatwa by way of istinbat and takhrij (i.e., the second meaning of its two meanings is correct), as understood from the expressions of Tahrir and Sharh Badi'. Who is mujtahid fil madhhab? It is apparent that the third, fourth, and fifth classes are mujtahid fil madhhab, and others should suffice with naql (transmission). And upon us, the later classes, is to follow what the three classes transmit, i.e., their istinbatat regarding which no explicit statement from the early scholars is transmitted, and their tarjihat (preferences) among the statements of the early scholars, even if they prefer a statement other than Imam Sahib's; as we have explained in detail at the beginning of this discussion.

The author begins by clarifying that this rule applies not only to Imam Abu Hanifa but also to his senior students. He then defines 'mujtahid fil madhhab' as the third class of the seven classes, not the second class. The second class (Abu Yusuf, Muhammad, Zufar) are mujtahid mutlaq, but they follow Imam Abu Hanifa in most principles. Two reasons are given: either because a mujtahid may follow another mujtahid, supported by Abu Yusuf's incident where he followed Imam Malik on the issue of a mouse in a bathhouse, or because their ijtihad coincided with Imam Abu Hanifa's. The author then cites Allama Shami quoting an inter-madhhab comparison: some Shafi'i scholars debated whether Imam Muzani was mujtahid mutlaq or mujtahid fil madhhab, contrasting him with Abu Yusuf and Muhammad who contradicted their imam even in principles. Checkpoint
According to the passage, why are Imam Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad considered mujtahid mutlaq by the Hanafi school?
A) Because they never contradicted Imam Abu Hanifa.
B) Because they contradicted Imam Abu Hanifa in principles (usul).

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi madhhab classifies its senior students as mujtahid mutlaq when they contradict in principles, yet their rulings remain integral to the school.

Mujtahid fi al-Madhhab and Ibn al-Humam's Authority
Clarifying who qualifies as mujtahid fi al-madhhab and Ibn al-Humam's status

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the characteristics of a mujtahid fi al-madhhab and apply the criteria to evaluate whether a later scholar like Ibn al-Humam qualifies for tarjih.

Core Idea
A mujtahid fi al-madhhab derives rulings within the madhhab's usul and prefers opinions, but must not leave its circle.

The Hanafi madhhab has a clear hierarchy of jurists, from absolute mujtahids to mere transmitters. This lesson explores the critical middle category: mujtahid fi al-madhhab, who can perform istinbat and tarjih. Using the example of Imam al-Muzani and the Hanafi founding imams, we uncover the criteria. Then we apply these to the towering figure of Ibn al-Humam, whose rank as ashab al-tarjih is affirmed but qualified.

Guided Path
1
Identify the key terms
Define 'mujtahid fi al-madhhab', 'ashab al-tarjih', and 'takhrij' as they appear in the passage. Note the distinction from mujtahid mutlaq.
Use the provided key terms list.
2
Trace the dispute about al-Muzani and the Hanafi imams
Analyze the difference: Abu Yusuf and Muhammad opposed their imam in usul, thus they are mujtahid fi al-madhhab. Al-Muzani did not oppose al-Shafi'i in usul, so his rulings are takhrijat.
This establishes the Hanafi criterion for mujtahid fi al-madhhab.
3
Determine who can issue fatwa by istinbat
The passage concludes that Abu Hanifa's statement about knowing the source applies specifically to mujtahid fi al-madhhab of strata 3-5. Others must only transmit.
Note the thamarah: binding fatwa vs. transmitted fatwa.
4
Apply to Ibn al-Humam: evaluate his rank
Ibn Nujaym calls him 'ahl li al-nazar fi al-dalil', placing him among ashab al-tarjih. However, his opinions are followed only when they do not leave the madhhab's circle.
This is the operative rule for later scholars.

فائده
ابن برہان (۱۰۵) نے اوسط میں فرمایا ہے کہ ہمارے اکابر اور حنفی اکابر میں امام مزنی (۱۰۲) ابن سریج (۱۰۷) امام ابو یوسف اور امام محمد کے بارے میں اختلاف ہوا ہے۔ بعض ان کو مجتہد مطلق کہتے ہیں اور بعض مجتہد فی المذہب اور امام الحرمین (۱۰۸) نے فرمایا ہے کہ میرے خیال میں امام مزنی کی تمام را ئیں تخریجات ہیں کیونکہ انہوں نے امام شافعی کی اصول میں مخالفت نہیں کی ہے۔ ان کا معاملہ امام ابو یوسف اور امام محمد جیسا نہیں ہے کیونکہ وہ دونوں حضرات اصول میں بھی اپنے امام کی مخالفت کرتے ہیں اور امام رافعی (۱۰۹) نے باب الوضو میں فرمایا ہے کہ امام مزنی کے تفردات مذہب شافعی میں شمار نہیں کئے جائیں گے جب کہ امام مزنی نے ان جزئیات کی تخریج امام شافعی کے ضوابط پر نہ کی ہو (منبہیہ تمام ہوا)۔
خلاصه کلام مذکورہ بالا گفتگو سے یہ بات متح ہوئی کہ امام اعظم اور ان کے تلامذہ کا یہ قول کہ لا یجل لاحد أن یفتی بقولنا حتى یعلم من أین قلنا؟ کا مصداق مجتہد فی المذہب کا استنباط و تخریج کے طور پر فتوی دینا ہے (یعنی اس کے دو مطلبوں میں سے دوسرا مطلب صحیح ہے) جیسا کہ تحریر اور شرح بدیع کی عبارتوں سے معلوم ہوا۔
مجتہد فی المذہب کون ہے؟ اور ظاہر یہ ہے کہ طبقہ ثالثہ رابعہ اور خالصہ والے مجتہد فی المذہب ہیں اور دیگر حضرات کو نقل پر اکتفا کرنی چاہیے اور ہمارے ذمہ ما بعد طبقات والے ان طبقات ثلاثہ والوں سے جو نقل کریں اس کی پیروی کرنا ہے یعنی ان کے وہ استنباطات جن کے بارے میں متقدمین سے کوئی صراحت مروی نہیں ہے اور ان کی متقدمین کے اقوال میں ترجیحات اگر چہ وہ امام صاحب کے علاوہ کے قول کو ترجیح دیں۔ جیسا کہ ہم اس بحث کے آغاز میں مفصل بیان کر آئے ہیں۔ کیونکہ ان حضرات نے جس قول کو بھی ترجیح دی ہے محض انکل سے ترجیح نہیں دی ہے بلکہ ان کے مآخذ سے واقف ہونے کے بعد ہی ترجیح دی ہے جیسا کہ ان کی تصنیفات اس بات پر شاہد ہیں۔ یہ بات علامہ ابن نجیم کی اس رائے کے خلاف ہے جو انہوں نے البحر الرائق ج۶ ص۲۷۰ میں بیان کی ہے۔
امام ابن الہمام کا مرتبہ:
(تنبیہ) بحر کی عبارت صریح ہے کہ محقق ابن الہام رحمہ اللہ اصحاب ترجیح میں سے ہیں۔
کیونکہ ابن نجیم نے ان کے بارے میں کہا ہے کہ: هو اهل للنظر في الدلیل. (بحر ج ۲ ص ٢٧٠) وہ دلیل میں غور و فکر کرنے کی صلاحیت رکھتے ہیں۔
پس ہم ان روایات یا اقوال میں ان کی پیروی کر سکتے ہیں جن کو وہ مدلل کرتے ہیں یا ترجیح دیتے ہیں بشرطیکہ وہ مذہب کے دائرہ سے نہ نکلیں۔ کیونکہ ان کی کچھ رائیں ایسی بھی ہیں جن میں انہوں نے مذہب کی مخالفت کی ہے۔ ان میں ان کی پیروی نہیں کی جائے گی جیسا کہ یہ بات ان کے شاگرد علامہ قاسم رحمہ اللہ نے کہی ہے۔
اور ان میں یہ صلاحیت کیسے نہیں ہو سکتی، ان کے بارے میں تو ان کے ایک معاصر برہان انباسی نے یہ فرمایا ہے کہ: لو طلبت حجج الدین ما کان في بلد نا من یقوم بها غیره. اگر میں دین کے دلائل جاننا چاہوں تو ہمارے شہر میں ... ابن الہمام کے علاوہ کوئی ایسی شخصیت نہیں ہے جو ان کو پیش کر سکے۔
میں (علامہ شامی) کہتا ہوں بلکہ علامہ محقق شیخ الاسلام علی مقدسی رحمہ اللہ (۱۱۰) نے منظوم کنز کی شرح میں باب نکاح الرقیق میں صراحت کی ہے کہ ابن الہمام اجتہاد کے مرتبہ تک پہنچے ہوئے ہیں۔
علامہ قاسم کا مقام:
اور اس طرح خود علامہ قاسم بن قطلو بخارحمہ اللہ (۱۰) شہ سواروں کے اسی دستہ کا ایک فرد
رد الختار ج ۲ ص ۳۸۸ و ج ۳ ص ۳۷ میں بھی ابن الہام کے بارے میں گفتگو ہے ۱۲۔
Allama Shami (may Allah have mercy on him) wrote in al-Munyah that then I saw the writing of a reliable scholar, which is exactly: Ibn al-Mulqin (104) said in Tabaqat al-Shafi'iyyah. Benefit: Ibn Burhan (105) said in al-Awsat that our elders and the Hanafi elders differed regarding Imam al-Muzani (102), Ibn Surayj (107), Imam Abu Yusuf, and Imam Muhammad. Some call them absolute mujtahids and some mujtahid fi al-madhhab. And Imam al-Haramayn (108) said: In my opinion, all of Imam al-Muzani's opinions are takhrijat (derivations) because he did not oppose Imam al-Shafi'i in principles. His case is not like that of Imam Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad because those two opposed their imam even in principles. And Imam al-Rafi'i (109) said in Bab al-Wudu that the singular views of Imam al-Muzani will not be counted in the Shafi'i madhhab when he did not derive those details based on Imam al-Shafi'i's principles. (al-Munyah completed). The summary of the above discussion is that the saying of Imam A'zam and his students: 'It is not permissible for anyone to give fatwa with our saying until he knows from where we said it' applies to a mujtahid fi al-madhhab giving fatwa by way of istinbat and takhrij (i.e. the second of its two meanings is correct) as understood from the expressions of al-Tahrir and Sharh al-Badi'. Who is a mujtahid fi al-madhhab? And it is apparent that those of the third, fourth, and fifth strata are mujtahid fi al-madhhab, and others must be content with transmission. It is upon us, those after these strata, to follow what they transmit from these three strata, i.e. their istinbatat (deductions) regarding which no explicit statement is transmitted from the earlier scholars, and their preferences among the sayings of the earlier scholars, even if they prefer the saying of someone other than Imam Sahib. Because those persons have not given preference merely by opinion, but after being aware of the sources, as their works testify. This is contrary to the view of Allama Ibn Nujaym which he stated in al-Bahr al-Raiq, vol. 6, p. 270. The rank of Imam Ibn al-Humam: (Warning) The text of al-Bahr is explicit that the investigator Ibn al-Humam (may Allah have mercy on him) is among the people of tarjih. Because Ibn Nujaym said about him: 'He is capable of reflection on the evidence.' (al-Bahr, vol. 2, p. 270). So we can follow him in those narrations or sayings which he substantiates or prefers, provided they do not leave the circle of the madhhab. Because some of his opinions oppose the madhhab. He will not be followed in those, as his student Allama Qasim (may Allah have mercy on him) said. And how can he not have this ability? About him, his contemporary Burhan al-Anbasi said: 'If I wanted to know the proofs of the religion, there is no one in our city who could present them except Ibn al-Humam.' I (Allama Shami) say, rather, the investigator Shaykh al-Islam Ali al-Maqdisi (110) stated explicitly in his commentary on Manzum al-Kanz, in the chapter on Nikah al-Raqiq, that Ibn al-Humam reached the rank of ijtihad. The status of Allama Qasim: And similarly, Allama Qasim ibn Qutlubugha (10) himself is an individual of this same troop. In Radd al-Mukhtar, vol. 2, p. 388 and vol. 3, p. 37, there is also discussion about Ibn al-Humam.
Source pages p. 85

Commentary
This passage from Sharh Rasm al-Mufti (a work on the rules of issuing fatwa) discusses two related issues: (1) who qualifies as a mujtahid fi al-madhhab, and (2) the authority of later scholars like Ibn al-Humam. The passage begins by citing a debate from Shafi'i sources about whether Imam al-Muzani and others like Ibn Surayj were mujtahid mutlaq or mujtahid fi al-madhhab, contrasting them with the Hanafi imams Abu Yusuf and Muhammad who opposed their imam in usul. The author then concludes that the famous statement attributed to Abu Hanifa and his students—'It is not permissible for anyone to give fatwa with our saying until he knows from where we said it'—applies specifically to a mujtahid fi al-madhhab, not to a mere transmitter. These mujtahid fi al-madhhab belong to the third, fourth, and fifth strata (tabaqat) of Hanafi jurists. Such scholars may engage in istinbat (deduction) and tarjih (preference) based on understanding the sources, but later scholars must follow their deductions and preferences. The author then discusses Ibn al-Humam specifically, citing Ibn Nujaym's acknowledgment that he is capable of 'reflection on the evidence' (ahl li al-nazar fi al-dalil). This places him among the ashab al-tarjih (people of preference). However, the author qualifies that we follow Ibn al-Humam only when his rulings remain within the circle of the madhhab; if he clearly opposes the established madhhab, we do not follow him. The passage gives authority weight from later usul al-iftaa works, specifically from Ibn Abidin's commentary. The key principle established is that ijtihad within the madhhab is permissible for qualified scholars, but the scope is limited: they derive rulings based on the usul of the madhhab and prefer between transmitted opinions, but they may not contradict the foundational principles of the madhhab.

Key Terms
مجتہد فی المذہب (mujtahid fi al-madhhab): A jurist who is qualified to derive rulings within the framework of a specific madhhab, using its usul, and to prefer between transmitted opinions
اصحاب ترجیح (ashab al-tarjih): Scholars who are capable of preferring one transmitted opinion over another based on strength of evidence
تخریج (takhrij): Derivation of a ruling by applying the principles (usul) of the founder to new cases not explicitly stated

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is Ibn al-Humam considered among the ashab al-tarjih?
A) He claimed ijtihad for himself
B) Ibn Nujaym said he is capable of reflection on evidence
C) He wrote many books on fiqh
D) He opposed Imam Abu Hanifa

Key Takeaway
The authority to perform istinbat and tarjih within the Hanafi madhhab belongs to mujtahid fi al-madhhab of the third to fifth strata; later scholars like Ibn al-Humam may be followed only when their rulings remain within the madhhab's circle.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa
advanced
10 min
Ranks of Mujtahids and Conditions for Fatwa
Discussing scholarly ranks and conditions for tarjih/fatwa

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the conditions for giving fatwa in the Hanafi madhhab and apply the hierarchy of scholars to determine whose tarjih is authoritative.

Core Idea
Fatwa without knowing the source is invalid; only those with ijtihad capacity can weigh evidence.

This passage addresses a critical question in Hanafi usul al-iftaa: who is qualified to give tarjih (preference among opinions) and to issue fatwa? It presents a core condition narrated from Imam Abu Hanifa himself: the mufti must know the source of the ruling. The text then applies this principle to evaluate later scholars like Ibn al-Humam, Qasim, and Ibn Nujaym, clarifying their ranks and the limits of their authority. Understanding this hierarchy is essential for anyone who wishes to derive fatwa correctly within the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core condition for fatwa
Locate the narration from Imam Abu Hanifa: 'It is not permissible for anyone to give a fatwa on our saying until he knows where we got that saying from.' This is the fundamental rule.
This is a qawl sahabi (Imam Abu Hanifa's statement) that serves as a dalil for the condition.
2
Distinguish between grades of scholars
Note that the passage ranks Ibn al-Humam as a 'people of tarjih' (mujtahid fi al-madhhab), while Ibn Nujaym is considered a muqallid who lacks the ability to examine evidence independently.
The dispute about Ibn Nujaym illustrates the practical application of the condition.
3
Analyze the dispute between Allamah Biray and the author
Allamah Biray argued that Ibn Nujaym's work al-Ashbah qualifies him as a mujtahid fi al-madhhab. The author rebuts that knowing many rules does not equate to ijtihad; one must also have the capacity to weigh evidence.
The thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence) is that Ibn Nujaym's tarjihs are not binding if they contradict other scholars.
4
Apply the condition to the scholars mentioned
Ibn al-Humam is accepted because his tarjih is based on evidence; Ibn Nujaym's derivations are rejected because he himself admitted the obligation to follow the Imam (taqlid).
This shows how the condition 'knowing the source' functions as a filter.

کیا ہے تو جب یہ ممانعت میرے سامنے آئی میں نے ائمہ کے اقوال کے مآخذ تلاش کئے اور اللہ کے فضل سے ان کی بڑی مقدار پر قابو پالیا اور بہت سے مصنفین کی کتابوں میں جو باتیں ہیں ان کی تقلید پر میں نے قناعت نہیں کی الخ۔ اور علامہ قاسم نے ایک دوسرے رسالہ میں لکھا ہے کہ میں بفضلہ تعالٰی وہی بات کہتا ہوں جو امام طحاوی رحمہ اللہ (۱۷) نے ابن حربویہ سے کہی تھی کہ لَا يَقَلِدُ إِلَّا عَصَبِيٌّ أَوْ غَبِيٍّ ( تقليد یا تو متعصب آدمی کرتا ہے یا نجی ! ) ابن حجیم کا مقام: اور صاحب بحر کے اس قول ہے کہ یجب علينا الافتاء بقول الامام الخ۔ ( بحرج ۶ ص ۲۷۰) یعنی ہمارے لیے امام اعظم کے قول پر فتویٰ دینا واجب ہے۔ اس قول سے یہ سمجھا جا سکتا ہے کہ خود ابن نجیم دلیل میں غور وفکر کرنے کی صلاحیت نہیں رکھتے ۔ پس اگر وہ دوسرے فقہاء کی تصریح کے خلاف کسی قول کی تصحیح کریں تو اس کا اعتبار نہیں کیا جائے گا چہ جائے کہ قواعد کلیہ پر ان کی تخریجات و استنباطات کا اعتبار کیا جائے؟ اور علامہ بیری رحمہ اللہ کی رائے صحیح نہیں ہے۔ انہوں نے ابن نجیم کی الاشباہ میں جہاں یہ عبارت آئی ہے النوع الاول: معرفة القواعد انج (ص ۱۵) یعنی پہلی نوع ان قواعد کے سلسلہ میں ہے جن کی طرف جزئیات لوٹائی جاتی ہیں اور جن پر احکام کی تفریح کی جاتی ہے اور وہ قواعد در حقیقت فقہی ضوابط ہیں۔ جن کے جاننے سے فقیہ اجتہاد کے درجہ تک ترقی کرتا ہے اگر چہ وہ اجتہاد فتوئی میں ہو اور میں ان ضوابط کی بیشتر جزئیات جانے میں کامیاب ہو گیا ہوں الخ جہاں یہ عبارت آئی ہے۔ وہاں علامہ بیری نے پہلے مجتہد فی المذہب کی تعریف کی ہے جو ہم ان کے
These people who have given preference to any statement have not given preference merely out of inclination, but only after becoming aware of its sources, as their writings bear witness. This is contrary to the opinion of Allamah Ibn Nujaym, which he stated in al-Bahr al-Ra'iq vol.6 p.270. The rank of Imam Ibn al-Humam: (Note) The text of al-Bahr is explicit that the investigator Ibn al-Humam, may Allah have mercy on him, is among the people of tarjih. Because Ibn Nujaym said about him: 'He is capable of examining the evidence' (al-Bahr vol.2 p.270). So we can follow him in the narrations or statements that he proves or prefers, provided they do not depart from the circle of the madhhab. Because some of his opinions are in opposition to the madhhab; he will not be followed in these, as his student Allamah Qasim, may Allah have mercy on him, said. And how could he not have this ability? One of his contemporaries, Burhan al-Anbasi, said: 'If I sought the proofs of religion, in our city there is none other than Ibn al-Humam who could present them.' I (Allamah Shami) say, rather Allamah al-Muhaqqiq Shaykh al-Islam Ali Maqdisi, may Allah have mercy on him, in his commentary on Manzum al-Kanz in the chapter of Nikah al-Raqiq, explicitly stated that Ibn al-Humam reached the rank of ijtihad. And likewise Allamah Qasim bin Qutlubugha, may Allah have mercy on him, is one of the same group of riders; in Radd al-Mukhtar vol.2 p.388 and vol.3 p.37, there is also discussion about Ibn al-Humam. [Page 87] ... because he wrote at the beginning of his treatise named Raf' al-Ishtibah 'an Mas'alah al-Miyah: 'When our scholars, may Allah be pleased with them all, prevented those who have the ability to reflect from pure taqlid,' as narrated by Shaykh Imam Allamah Abu al-Haq Ibrahim bin Yusuf. He said: Imam Abu Yusuf, may Allah have mercy on him, narrated from Imam Abu Hanifa, may Allah have mercy on him, that he said: 'It is not permissible for anyone to give a fatwa on our saying until he knows where we got that saying from.' So when this prohibition came to me, I researched the sources of the sayings of the imams, and by Allah's grace I mastered a great amount of them, and I was not satisfied with mere taqlid of the writings of many authors, etc. And Allamah Qasim wrote in another treatise: 'I, by His grace, say what Imam Tahawi, may Allah have mercy on him, said to Ibn Harbawayh: Only a bigoted person or a dullard does taqlid.' The rank of Ibn Nujaym: And the statement of the author of al-Bahr is that 'We must give fatwa according to the saying of the Imam, etc.' (al-Bahr vol.6 p.270), meaning it is obligatory for us to give fatwa according to the saying of the Great Imam. From this statement, it can be understood that Ibn Nujaym himself does not possess the ability to examine evidence. So if he corrects a saying contrary to the explicit statements of other jurists, it will not be accepted, let alone his derivations from general rules and his deductions. And the opinion of Allamah Biray is not correct. His statement in Ibn Nujaym's al-Ashbah, where the phrase appears: 'The first type: knowledge of the rules, etc.' (p.15), meaning the first type is about the rules to which particulars are referred and on which rulings are branched; these rules are in fact fiqh maxims; by knowing them, a faqih advances to the rank of ijtihad, even if it be ijtihad in fatwa, and I have succeeded in knowing most of the particulars of these maxims, etc. There Allamah Biray defined the mujtahid fi al-madhhab, which we...
Source pages p. 86

Commentary
This passage is a discussion in rasm al-mufti (the method of issuing fatwa) concerning the hierarchy of scholars in the Hanafi madhhab and the conditions for giving fatwa. The author, likely Allamah Shami, is clarifying who among later scholars is qualified for tarjih (weighing evidence) and ijtihad. He begins by defending those who give preference to certain rulings, stating they do so based on knowledge of sources, not mere opinion. He then contrasts this with Ibn Nujaym's view in al-Bahr al-Ra'iq. The passage then discusses the rank of Ibn al-Humam, affirming that he is among the people of tarjih as per Ibn Nujaym's own admission, and that his preferred opinions can be followed as long as they do not contradict the madhhab. It is noted that some of Ibn al-Humam's opinions oppose the madhhab, so those are not followed. His student Qasim supports this. Further, the narration from Imam Abu Hanifa is quoted: 'It is not permissible for anyone to give a fatwa on our saying until he knows where we got that saying from.' This is a fundamental condition for fatwa: the mufti must know the evidence and source of the ruling. The passage then discusses the rank of Qasim, who also researched sources and condemned blind taqlid. Finally, it addresses Ibn Nujaym's rank, suggesting that his own statement about the obligation to follow the Imam implies that he (Ibn Nujaym) is not a mujtahid, and therefore his corrections and derivations should not be accepted if they contradict other jurists. The passage concludes by critiquing Allamah Biray's interpretation of Ibn Nujaym's work al-Ashbah. Overall, the passage sets forth the principle that only those with knowledge of the sources (mujtahidun) are qualified for tarjih, and that later scholars like Ibn Nujaym, while great, are limited in their ability to derive new rulings.

Key Terms
ترجیح (tarjīḥ): The process of preferring one legal opinion or evidence over another among conflicting views within the madhhab.
تقلید (taqlīd): Following a qualified imam without knowing the evidence for the ruling.
اجتہاد (ijtihād): The effort to derive rulings from the primary sources by those qualified. In the passage, ijtihad is of two types: absolute and within the madhhab (mujtahid fi al-madhhab).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the narration from Imam Abu Hanifa in this passage, what is a necessary condition for a mufti to give fatwa on Imam Abu Hanifa's sayings?
A) He must memorize all of Imam Abu Hanifa's rulings.
B) He must know the source from which Imam Abu Hanifa derived the ruling.
C) He must be a mujtahid mutlaq.
D) He must have studied for at least ten years.

Key Takeaway
A mufti must know the dalil of a ruling before issuing fatwa; only scholars who can weigh evidence (mujtahidun) are qualified for tarjih.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa
intermediate
6 min
Fatwa Hierarchy When No Narration Exists: The Rule of Majority and Ijtihad
A didactic nazm outlining mufti's procedure when no riwayah exists

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three-step hierarchy a Hanafi mufti follows when no direct riwayah is available and apply the rule of preferring the majority view among later scholars.

Core Idea
When no transmitted ruling exists, prefer the majority of later scholars; if still absent, exert ijtihad with fear of Allah.

This nazm (didactic poem) encodes a critical procedure for issuing fatwas in the Hanafi school. It outlines a stepwise hierarchy: first search for a riwayah, then consult the later authorities, and if they differ, adopt the majority view. If even the later scholars have no recorded opinion, the mufti must personally exert ijtihad — but with great caution and fear of divine accountability. This rule prevents arbitrary fatwas and ensures consistency within the school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the first source: riwayah
Confirm that the mufti's first duty is to search for a transmitted ruling (riwayah) from early Hanafi authorities like Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad al-Shaybani.
If a riwayah exists, the fatwa must follow it.
2
Apply the second step: consult later scholars and prefer majority
If no riwayah is found, the mufti turns to the later scholars (متأخرون). If they differ, the rule is to adopt the view held by the majority (الأكثر). The nazm names Imam Tahawi, Abu Hafs al-Kabir, Abu Ja'far al-Hindawani, and Abu al-Layth al-Samarqandi as examples.
This step ensures the fatwa is grounded in the cumulative understanding of the school.
3
Recognize the third step: ijtihad as final resort
If even the later scholars have no statement on the issue, the mufti must exert ijtihad using full effort (بجهده واجتهاد) and fear Allah's punishment.
This is a grave responsibility; the nazm warns that only a wretched person dares to issue rulings without qualification.
4
Understand the ethical warning
The poem emphasizes that the mufti must fear Allah's grip on the Day of Reckoning, highlighting the severe accountability for giving fatwas improperly.
This encourages carefulness and humility in issuing rulings.

Source Text

عَنْ عُلَمَائِنَا ذَوى الدّرَايَهُ -٣٢ ثُمَّ إِذَا لَمْ تُوجَدِ الرّوَايَهُ وَاخْتَلَفَ الَّذِينَ قَدْ تَأَخَّرُوا يُرَبَّحُ الَّذِي عَلَيْهِ الْأَكْثَرُ مِثْلُ الطَّحَاوِي وَأَبِى حَفْصِ الْكَبِيرُ وَابَوَى جَعْفَرٍ وَاللَّيْثِ الشَّهِيرُ ٣٧- وحيث لَمْ تُوجَد لهولاء مَقَالَةٌ وَاحْتِيجَ لِلافْتَاءُ فَلْيَنظُر الْمُفْتِى بِحِةٍ وَاجْتِهَادُ وَلْيَخْشَ بَطْشَ وَلْيَخْشَ بَطْشَ رَبِّهِ يَوْمَ الْمَعَادُ -٣٩ فَلَيْسَ يَجُسُرُ عَلَى الْأَحْكَامُ سوى شَقِي خَاسِرِ الْمَرَامُ ترجمہ: (۳۴) پھر جب کوئی روایت موجود نہ ہو۔ ہمارے فہم و بصیرت رکھنے والے علماء سے (۳۵) اور بعد کے فقہاء میں اختلاف ہو جائے ۔ تو اس قول کو ترجیح دی جائے گی جو اکثر کی رائے ہے۔ (۳۶) مثلاً امام طحاوی اور امام ابو حفص کبیر ۔ اور ابو جعفر ہندوانی اور مشہور امام ابواللیث سمرقندی۔ (۳۷) اور جہاں نہ موجود ہو ان حضرات کا بھی۔ کوئی قول اور فتویٰ کے لیے ضرورت پیش آئے۔ (۳۸) تو مفتی پوری کوشش اور محنت سے غور کرے۔ اور چاہیے کہ وہ قیامت کے دن کی پروردگار کی پکڑ سے ڈرے۔ (۳۹) کیونکہ احکام شرعیہ بیان کرنے پر دلیری نہیں کرتا۔ بد بخت خائب و خاسر آدمی کے علاوہ۔
From our scholars of insight. Then when no narration is found, and later scholars differed, the one upon which the majority is shall be preferred, like al-Tahawi, Abu Hafs al-Kabir, Abu Ja'far al-Hindawani, and al-Layth al-Shahir. And when not found from them a statement, and fatwa is needed, then let the mufti reflect with effort and ijtihad, and let him fear the grip of his Lord on the Day of Reckoning. For none dares to (issue) rulings except a wretched loser of the goal. Translation: (34) Then when no narration is present from our scholars of understanding and insight, (35) and the later jurists differed, then that opinion will be preferred that is the view of the majority. (36) For example, Imam Tahawi, Imam Abu Hafs al-Kabir, Abu Ja'far al-Hindawani, and the famous Imam Abu al-Layth al-Samarqandi. (37) And when their statement also is not found, and there is need for fatwa, (38) then the mufti should reflect with full effort and ijtihad, and he should fear the grip of his Lord on the Day of Reckoning. (39) For none dares to declare the rulings of Shari'ah except a wretched and loser of the goal.
Source pages p. 88

Commentary
This passage is a mnemonic poem (nazm) summarizing the hierarchy the mufti must follow when issuing fatwas. It is a central rule in Hanafi ifta' methodology. The first step is to look for a riwayah (transmitted ruling) from the early scholars. If none exists, the mufti turns to the later authorities (متأخرون). Among them, if there is ikhtilaf, the position of the majority (jama'ah or aksar) is preferred. The poem names four key later scholars: Imam Tahawi, Imam Abu Hafs al-Kabir, Abu Ja'far al-Hindawani, and Abu al-Layth al-Samarqandi. If even these later authorities have no statement on the issue, the mufti must then exert ijtihad using his own full capacity and reasoning (bi-hajih wa ijtihad). However, this is a grave responsibility — the poem warns the mufti to fear Allah's punishment on the Day of Judgment, as only a miserable person would dare to speak about Allah's rulings without proper qualification.

Key Terms
روایت (riwayah): A transmitted ruling from the early Hanafi authorities (e.g., Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad).
ذوی الدرایة (dhawi al-dirayah): Scholars possessing insight and the ability to derive rulings (opposed to mere narrators).
متأخرون (muta'akhkhirun): Later Hanafi jurists, typically those after the 4th century Hijri, such as al-Tahawi, al-Hindawani, etc.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the nazm, which scholars are mentioned as examples of later authorities whose majority opinion should be preferred?
A) Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad al-Shaybani
B) Imam Tahawi, Abu Hafs al-Kabir, Abu Ja'far al-Hindawani, Abu al-Layth al-Samarqandi
C) Imam Shafi'i, Malik, Ahmad ibn Hanbal
D) The Companions of the Prophet

Key Takeaway
The mufti must follow a strict hierarchy: first riwayah, then majority of later scholars, then ijtihad with fear of Allah.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa
intermediate
10 min
Hierarchy of Authorities in Fatwa Without Transmission
Explaining mufti's procedure when earlier riwaya is absent

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi hierarchy for issuing fatwa when no transmitted ruling (riwaya) from the early imams exists, identifying the correct order of authorities and the procedure for a mufti.

Core Idea
When no riwaya exists, the mufti must follow a defined hierarchy: start with the majority of later scholars, then ijtihad – never arbitrary preference.

This passage from Rasm al-Mufti provides the foundational procedure for a Hanafi mufti when facing a case for which no direct ruling from Imam Abu Hanifa or his early students is preserved. It establishes a clear, step-by-step hierarchy to ensure the fatwa remains within the madhhab's boundaries, even when earlier transmission is absent. The text also offers a stern warning about the gravity of fatwa and the need for piety and caution.

Guided Path
1
Identify the absence condition
Recognize the scenario: no riwaya (transmitted ruling) from the early imams (Imam Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad, etc.) is available for the given case.
Riwaya here refers to reports from the six books of zahir al-riwaya or nawadir.
2
Consult the later scholars (muta'akhkhirun)
If the early imams have no recorded ruling, turn to the opinions of the later Hanafi scholars, specifically the majority among them. The text names key authorities: Imam Tahawi, Abu Hafs al-Kabir, Abu Ja'far al-Hindwani, and Abu al-Layth al-Samarqandi.
The 'majority' (akthar) is given precedence over individual opinions.
3
Apply the majority rule
If the later scholars differ on the issue, the mufti must adopt the view held by the majority of these specified authorities. This ensures the fatwa aligns with the predominant position within the madhhab.
This step avoids arbitrary picking of a single scholar's view.
4
Fall back to ijtihad if no opinion exists
If no opinion is found from the later scholars, the mufti must engage in ijtihad – exerting his full capacity to derive a ruling from the general principles of the madhhab, while maintaining fear of Allah and awareness of the responsibility.
Ijtihad is a last resort, not a first option.
5
Refine with supplementary sources
Additional guidance from al-Hawi al-Qudsi and Fatawa Qadikhan provides a more detailed hierarchy: first Abu Yusuf, then Muhammad, then Zufar/Hasan, then later scholars' consensus, then majority, then ijtihad. Also, for non-zahir al-riwaya matters, compatibility with usul is checked.
These extras clarify the procedure further.

Source Text

شرح رسم المفتي
اور اس عبارت میں اس طرف اشارہ ہے کہ مصنف یعنی علامہ ابن نجیم فتوئی میں اس مرتبہ تک بلکہ اس سے کچھ اوپر تک پہنچ چکے ہیں اور یہ در حقیقت اللہ تعالیٰ کا پر فضل و کرم ہے کہ ان کو مخفی گوشوں سے واقف کر دیا اور وہ پوری واقفیت رکھنے والے حفاظ میں سے تھے۔"
