ترجمہ: (۳۴) پھر جب کوئی روایت موجود نہ ہو۔ ہمارے فہم و بصیرت رکھنے والے علماء سے (۳۵) اور بعد کے فقہاء میں اختلاف ہو جائے ۔ تو اس قول کو ترجیح دی جائے گی جو اکثر کی رائے ہے۔ (۳۶) مثلاً امام طحاوی اور امام ابو حفص کبیر ۔ اور ابو جعفر ہندوانی اور مشہور امام ابواللیث سمرقندی۔ (۳۷) اور جہاں نہ موجود ہو ان حضرات کا بھی۔ کوئی قول اور فتویٰ کے لیے ضرورت پیش آئے۔ (۳۸) تو مفتی پوری کوشش اور محنت سے غور کرے۔ اور چاہیے کہ وہ قیامت کے دن کی پروردگار کی پکڑ سے ڈرے۔ (۳۹) کیونکہ احکام شرعیہ بیان کرنے پر دلیری نہیں کرتا۔ بد بخت خائب و خاسر آدمی کے علاوہ۔

آپ فتوی کیسے دیں؟
شرح رسم المفتي
متقدمین سے روایت نہ ہو اور متاخرین میں اختلاف ہو تو کیا کیا جائے؟ الحاوي القدسي (۹۲) کے آخر میں ہے کہ جب کسی مسئلہ میں امام صاحب سے کوئی روایت نہ پائی جائے تو امام ابو یوسف کے ظاہر قول کو لیا جائے گا۔ پھر امام محمد کے ظاہر قول کو پھر امام زفر اور حسن بن زیادہ وغیرہ امام صاحب کے تمام بڑے تلامذہ کے اقوال کو آخر تک درجہ بدرجہ لیا جائے گا۔ اور جب کسی واقعہ میں ان حضرات سے کوئی صریح جواب مروی نہ ہو اور اس مسئلہ میں بعد کے مشائخ نے کلام کیا ہو اور وہ سب حضرات کسی ایک بات پر متفق ہوں تو اس کو لیا جائے گا اور اگر ان میں اختلاف ہو تو اکثر حضرات کے اس قول کو لیا جائے گا جس پر مشہور اکابر مثلا ابو حفص کبیر، ابو جعفر ہندوانی، ابواللیث سمرقندی، اور امام طحاوی وغیرہ نے اعتماد کیا ہو۔
متاخرین کا بھی کوئی قول نہ ہو تو کیا کیا جائے؟ اور اگر بعد کے مشائخ سے بھی قطعاً کوئی صریح حکم مروی نہ ہو تو مفتی اس واقعہ میں غور وفکر کرے اور اپنی پوری طاقت خرچ کرے تا کہ وہ کوئی ایسا حکم دریافت کر لے جس کے ذریعہ وہ اپنی ذمہ داری سے عہدہ برآ ہو سکے اور اس مسئلہ میں عقل سے گفتگو کرتے ہوئے اپنے منصب اور اس کی ذمہ داری کا احساس کرے اور اللہ تعالیٰ سے ڈرے کیونکہ فتویٰ دینا نہایت اہم معاملہ ہے اس کی جسارت ہر جاہل بد بخت ہی کرتا ہے۔
اور فتاویٰ قاضی خان میں ہے کہ: اگر مسئلہ غیر ظاہر الروایہ میں ہے تو اگر وہ مسئلہ ہمارے ائمہ کے اصول وضوابط کے موافق ہے تو اس پر عمل کیا جائے گا اور اگر کسی مسئلہ میں ہمارے ائمہ سے کوئی روایت نہ پائی جائے اور اس مسئلہ میں متاخرین کسی بات پر متفق ہوں تو اس پر عمل کیا جائے گا اور اگر متاخرین میں اختلاف ہو تو مفتی اجتہاد کرے اور اس کے نزدیک جو بات درست ہو اس کے مطابق فتوی دے اور اگر مفتی مقلد ہو مجتہد نہ ہو تو اپنی رائے میں افقہ کے قول کو لے اور جواب میں اس کا حوالہ دے اور اگر اس کے نزدیک جو افقہ ہے وہ کسی اور شہر میں ہے تو اس سے خط کے ذریعہ رابطہ قائم
How to give a fatwa? Previously mentioned. Then it is written: Sharh Rasm al-Mufti. And in this expression there is an indication that the author, Allamah Ibn Nujaym, has reached this rank and even slightly above, and this is truly Allah's grace that He acquainted him with hidden corners and he was among the preservers who had full familiarity. Allamah Pirzada's statement is incorrect because success in knowing most of these furu does not necessitate that he also had the ability to ponder evidences. His own words from al-Bahr indicate he did not have this ability. Then: 'Then when riwaya is not found and the later ones disagreed, the opinion of the majority is given precedence, like al-Tahawi, Abu Hafs al-Kabir, Abu Ja'far, and al-Layth al-Shahir. And when no statement of these is found and there is need for fatwa, then the mufti should look with insight and ijtihad, and fear his Lord's grasp on the Day of Return, for only a wretched, failing one dares to give legal rulings.' Translation: (34) Then when no riwaya is present from our scholars of understanding and insight. (35) And the later fuqaha differed, then the opinion of the majority is given precedence. (36) For example, Imam Tahawi, Imam Abu Hafs al-Kabir, Abu Ja'far al-Hindwani, and famous Imam Abu al-Layth al-Samarqandi. (37) And when no opinion of these is found and there is need for fatwa. (38) Then the mufti should exert full effort and careful consideration, and he should fear the punishment of his Lord on the Day of Judgment. (39) Because only a wretched, failing one dares to express legal rulings. How to give a fatwa? Sharh Rasm al-Mufti: When there is no narration from the early scholars and the later ones differ, what should be done? In al-Hawi al-Qudsi (92) it says: When in a matter no narration is found from Imam Abu Hanifa, then the apparent opinion of Imam Abu Yusuf is taken, then the apparent opinion of Imam Muhammad, then Imam Zufar, Hasan ibn Ziyad, etc., all the major students of the Imam, step by step until the end. And when in an incident no explicit answer is transmitted from these and the later mashayikh have spoken and they all agree on one matter, then that is taken. If they differ, then the opinion of the majority is taken, upon which the famous greats like Abu Hafs al-Kabir, Abu Ja'far al-Hindwani, Abu al-Layth al-Samarqandi, and Imam Tahawi have relied. What if there is no opinion of the later scholars? If absolutely no explicit ruling is transmitted from the later mashayikh, then the mufti should reflect and exert his full capacity to discover a ruling by which he can discharge his responsibility, and he should converse with reason, feel the gravity of his position and responsibility, and fear Allah, for giving fatwa is a very important matter; only an ignorant wretch dares it. And in Fatawa Qadikhan: If the matter is from non-zahir al-riwaya, then if it is in accordance with the principles and regulations of our imams, it is acted upon. And if in a matter no narration is found from our imams and the later ones agree on something, it is acted upon. If they differ, the mufti does ijtihad and gives fatwa according to what he deems correct. If the mufti is a muqallid, not a mujtahid, then he takes the opinion of the most knowledgeable in his view and cites him in the answer. If the one he considers most knowledgeable is in another city, he contacts him by letter.
Source pages p. 88

Commentary
This passage details the hierarchical methodology for a Hanafi mufti when issuing fatwas in cases where direct transmitted rulings (riwaya) from the founding imams are absent. It begins by critiquing a previous claim that Ibn Nujaym possessed both knowledge of furu and the ability to derive from evidences; the author argues that his own writings show otherwise. The core rule is presented in poetic form with explanation: when no riwaya exists from the early imams (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad, etc.), and the later scholars (muta'akhkhirun) differ, the opinion of the majority among them is given precedence. The passage lists key later authorities: Imam Tahawi, Abu Hafs al-Kabir, Abu Ja'far al-Hindwani, and Abu al-Layth al-Samarqandi. If even these later authorities have no recorded opinion, the mufti must exert ijtihad and issue a ruling based on his best reasoning, while being mindful of the grave responsibility. The passage then quotes al-Hawi al-Qudsi, which specifies a further hierarchy: first Abu Yusuf, then Muhammad, then Zufar and Hasan ibn Ziyad, and so on. If the later scholars agree, that is taken; if they differ, the majority is followed. If no later scholar's opinion exists, the mufti uses ijtihad. Finally, Fatawa Qadikhan adds that in non-zahir al-riwaya matters, the mufti checks compatibility with usul, and if a muqallid, he follows the opinion of the most knowledgeable scholar available, even if by correspondence. This text emphasizes the structured, cautious approach required in fatwa issuance.

Key Terms
رِوَايَة (riwaya): Transmitted report of a ruling from the early Hanafi imams (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad, etc.)
دِرَايَة (diraya): The ability to understand and derive rulings from evidences through legal reasoning and ijtihad.
مُتَقَدِّمُونَ (mutaqaddimun): Early Hanafi scholars, primarily the direct students of the imams (Abu Yusuf, Muhammad, Zufar, Hasan ibn Ziyad).
مُتَأَخِّرُونَ (muta'akhkhirun): Later Hanafi scholars from the 3rd century and beyond, such as Tahawi, Abu Hafs al-Kabir, etc.
ظَاهِرُ الرِّوَايَة (zahir al-riwaya): The most authoritative narrations transmitted from Imam Muhammad in his six books, forming the primary source for fatwa.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When no riwaya exists from Imam Abu Hanifa and the later scholars (muta'akhkhirun) differ on a issue, which opinion should the mufti give precedence to?
A) The opinion of any single later scholar the mufti prefers.
B) The opinion of the majority of the later scholars, such as Tahawi, Abu Hafs al-Kabir, etc.
C) The mufti's own ijtihad immediately without considering later scholars.
D) The opinion of Imam Shafi'i.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fatwa, the absence of a transmitted ruling triggers a strict hierarchy: first the majority of specified later scholars, then ijtihad – never arbitrary choice.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa
intermediate
8 min
The Hanafi Fatwa Ladder: From Imam Abu Hanifa to Later Scholars
Explaining the hierarchical order of fatwa authority.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to construct the hierarchical chain of authority a Hanafi mufti follows when no explicit ruling is found from Imam Abu Hanifa, and apply the rule of consensus and majority among later scholars.

Core Idea
Fatwa proceeds in order: Abu Hanifa → Abu Yusuf → Muhammad → major students → later scholars' consensus → majority.

When a mufti faces a new case with no direct ruling from Imam Abu Hanifa, he cannot simply give his own opinion. The classical Hanafi works prescribe a precise ladder of authority. This lesson guides you through that ladder—from the immediate students of Imam Abu Hanifa to the later mashayikh—and explains how consensus (ittifaq) and majority opinion (ra'y al-akthar) govern the selection.

Guided Path
1
Identify the gap
Recognize that there is no explicit ruling from Imam Abu Hanifa in the Zahir al-Riwayah or other transmitted sources for the case at hand.
2
Move to Imam Abu Yusuf
Take the apparent opinion (zahir qawl) of Imam Abu Yusuf, the foremost student of Abu Hanifa. The text states that if no narration from Abu Hanifa exists, the apparent opinion of Abu Yusuf is to be taken first.
3
Then Imam Muhammad
If no ruling is found from Abu Yusuf, take the apparent opinion of Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani.
4
Then other major students
Next in line are Imam Zufar, Hasan ibn Ziyad, and other senior disciples of Abu Hanifa, in a stepwise manner.
5
Later mashayikh: consensus then majority
If no explicit answer is found from the early students, look to the later scholars (mutākhkhirīn). If they agree on one ruling, that consensus is followed. If they differ, take the opinion of the majority, especially those specifically mentioned as reliable (e.g., Abu Hafs al-Kabir, Abu Ja'far al-Hindawani, etc.).

شمع رسم سلطنتی
متقدمین سے روایت نہ ہو اور متاخرین میں اختلاف ہو تو کیا کیا جائے؟ الحاوی القدی (۹۲) کے آخر میں ہے کہ جب کسی مسئلہ میں امام صاحب سے کوئی روایت نہ پائی جائے تو امام ابو یوسف کے ظاہر قول کو لیا جائے گا۔ پھر امام محمد کے ظاہر قول کو پھر امام زفر اور حسن بن زیادہ وغیرہ امام صاحب کے تمام بڑے تلامذہ کے اقوال کو آخر تک درجہ بدرجہ لیا جائے گا۔ اور جب کسی واقعہ میں ان حضرات سے کوئی صریح جواب مروی نہ ہو اور اس مسئلہ میں بعد کے مشائخ نے کلام کیا ہو اور وہ سب حضرات کسی ایک بات پر متفق ہوں تو اس کو لیا جائے گا اور اگر ان میں اختلاف ہو تو اکثر حضرات کے اس قول کو لیا جائے گا جس پر مشہور ا کا بر مثلا ابو حفص کبیر (۵۵) ابو جعفر ہندوانی (۶۱) ابواللیث سمرقندی (۵۱) اور امام طحاوی (۱۷) وغیرہ نے اعتماد کیا ہو۔
متاخرین کا بھی کوئی قول نہ ہو تو کیا کیا جائے؟ اور اگر بعد کے مشائخ سے بھی قطعاً کوئی صریح حکم مردی نہ ہو تو مفتی اس واقعہ میں غور وفکر کرے اور اپنی پوری طاقت خرچ کرے تا کہ وہ کوئی ایسا حکم دریافت کر لے جس کے ذریعہ وہ اپنی ذمہ داری سے عہدہ برآ ہو سکے اور اس مسئلہ میں انکل سے گفتگو نہ کرنے اپنے منصب اور اس کی ذمہ داری کا احساس کرے اور اللہ تعالیٰ سے ڈرے کیونکہ فتویٰ دینا نہایت اہم معاملہ ہے اس کی جسارت ہر جاہل بد بخت ہی کرتا ہے۔
اور فتاویٰ قاضی خان میں ہے کہ: اگر مسئلہ غیر ظاہر الروایہ میں ہے تو اگر وہ مسئلہ ہمارے ائمہ کے اصول وضوابط کے موافق ہے تو اس پر عمل کیا جائے گا اور اگر کسی مسئلہ میں ہمارے ائمہ سے کوئی روایت نہ پائی جائے اور اس مسئلہ میں متاخرین کسی بات پر متفق ہوں تو اس پر عمل کیا جائے گا اور اگر متاخرین میں اختلاف ہو تو مفتی اجتہاد کرے اور اس کے نزد یک جو بات درست ہو اس کے مطابق فتوی دے اور اگر مفتی مقلد ہو مجتہد نہ ہو تو اپنی رائے میں افقہ کے قول کو لے اور جواب میں اس کا حوالہ دے اور اگر اس کے نزدیک جو افقہ ہے وہ کسی اور شہر میں ہے تو اس سے خط کے ذریعہ رابطہ قائم کرے اور تحقیق کے بعد جواب لکھے اور انکل سے جواب نہ لکھ دئے حلال کو حرام اور حرام کو حلال کر کے اللہ تعالیٰ پر افترا پردازی سے ڈرے ( قاضی خان بر حاشیہ عالمگیری ج ص ۳)
فتوی میں صریح حوالہ ضروری ہے:
میں کہتا ہوں کہ قاضی خان رحمہ اللہ کے اس قول سے کہ: " اگر مفتی مقلد ہو مجتہد نہ ہوانی " یہ بات مفہوم ہوتی ہے کہ مقلد محض کے لیے ان مسائل میں جن میں کسی فقیہ سے صراحی حکم مروی نہیں ہے فتویٰ دینا جائز نہیں اور اس کی تائید اس قول سے ہوتی ہے جس کو البحر الرائق ( ج ۲ ص ۲۶۸) میں فتاوی تا تارخانیہ ( ج ۱ص ۸۲ مقدمہ کی ساتویں فصل ) سے نقل کیا ہے کہ اگر متاخرین میں اختلاف ہو تو مفتی کسی ایک کے قول کو لے اور اگر متاخرین میں سے کسی کا قول نہ پائے تو وہ خود اجتہاد کرے۔ جب کہ وہ فقہ کی وجوہ جانتا ہو اور فقہاء سے مشورہ بھی کرے اھ۔ تا تارخانیہ کا یہ قول کہ جب وہ فقہ کی جملہ تفصیلات سے واقف ہو الخ اس بات کی دلیل ہے کہ جو مفتی یہ نہیں جانتا بلکہ اس نے فقہ کی کوئی ایک کتاب یا اس کا اکثر حصہ پڑھ لیا ہے اور اس کو سمجھ لیا ہے اور اس میں کتابوں کی مراجعت کرنے کی صلاحیت پیدا ہو گئی ہے اور مشہور قابل اعتماد کتابوں میں مسئلہ کہاں ملے گا اس کو جاننے کی اس میں استعداد پیدا ہوگئی ہے ایسا شخص جب کوئی واقعہ کسی کتاب میں نہ پائے تو اس کے لیے جائز نہیں ہے کہ وہ اپنی رائے سے فتویٰ دے دے بلکہ اس کے ذمہ واجب ہے کہ اپنی لاعلمی ظاہر کرے جیسا کہ اس سے بڑے مرتبہ والوں نے لاعلمی ظاہر کی ہے یعنی مجتہدین صحابہ نے اور ان کے بعد کے مجتہدین نے بلکہ اس ہستی نے جو موید بالوحی تھی صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم۔ صریح جزئیہ نہ ملنے کی وجہ : اور غالب گمان یہ ہے کہ اس مفتی کا صراحت نہ پانا اس کی واقفیت کی کمی کی وجہ سے ہے یا مسئلہ مطلوبہ کے ذکر کا محل نہ جانے کی وجہ سے ہے کیونکہ شاید ہی کوئی واقعہ رونما ہوتا ہے مگر اس کا کتب مذہب میں ضرور تذکرہ ہوتا ہے۔ یا تو وہ بعینہ مذکور ہوتا ہے یا کوئی ایسا قاعدہ کلیہ مذکور ہوتا ہے جو اس واقعہ کو بھی شامل ہوتا ہے۔
How to give fatwa? Shama' Rasm Sultanati. What to do when there is no narration from the early scholars and the later scholars differ? At the end of Al-Hawi al-Qudsi (92) it is stated: When in a matter no narration is found from Imam Abu Hanifa, the apparent opinion of Imam Abu Yusuf will be taken. Then the apparent opinion of Imam Muhammad, then Imam Zufar and Hasan ibn Ziyad etc. all the major students of Imam Abu Hanifa up to the end will be taken step by step. And when there is no explicit answer narrated from these personalities in an incident, and later mashayikh have spoken about this matter and all of them agree on one thing, then that will be taken. And if there is disagreement among them, then the opinion of the majority of them will be taken, the one on which the renowned scholars relied, for example Abu Hafs al-Kabir (55), Abu Ja'far al-Hindawani (61), Abu al-Layth al-Samarqandi (51), and Imam al-Tahawi (17) etc. What to do when even the later scholars have no ruling? And if absolutely no explicit ruling is narrated from the later mashayikh, then the mufti should ponder and reflect on that incident and exert his full effort so that he may discover a ruling by which he can discharge his responsibility, and he should not discuss this matter with anyone but should realize his position and its responsibility, and fear Allah, because giving fatwa is a very important matter; only every ignorant wretch dares to do it. And in Fatawa Qadikhan it is stated: If the matter is from non-Zahir al-Riwayah, then if that matter is in accordance with the principles and rules of our imams, then it will be acted upon. And if no narration is found from our imams in a matter, and the later scholars are agreed on something, then that will be acted upon. And if the later scholars differ, then the mufti will exercise ijtihad and give fatwa according to what he deems correct. And if the mufti is a muqallid and not a mujtahid, then he should take the opinion of the most knowledgeable among his own people, and give the reference in his answer. And if the one who is most knowledgeable in his view is in another city, then he should correspond with him by letter, and after investigation write the answer, and he should not write an answer ignorantly, making halal into haram and haram into halal, fabricating against Allah; he should fear (Qadikhan, from marginalia of Alamgiri, vol. 3, p. ?). The necessity of clear reference in fatwa: I say that from this statement of Qadikhan: "If the mufti is a muqallid, not a mujtahid," it is understood that for a pure muqallid, giving fatwa in matters where no explicit ruling is narrated from any faqih is not permissible. And this is supported by that statement which is quoted in al-Bahr al-Raiq (vol. 2, p. 268) from Fatawa Tatarkhaniyya (vol. 1, p. 82, seventh chapter of introduction): that if the later scholars differ, the mufti should take one of their opinions, and if no opinion is found from the later scholars, then he should exercise ijtihad himself, provided he knows the reasons of fiqh and also consults with fuqaha. End. The statement of Tatarkhaniyya that "when he knows all the details of fiqh" etc. is evidence that a mufti who does not know this, but rather has read only one book of fiqh or most of it and understood it, and has developed the ability to refer to books and knows where to find the matter in well-known reliable books—such a person, when he does not find an incident in any book, it is not permissible for him to give fatwa from his own opinion. Rather, it is obligatory upon him to express his ignorance, just as those of higher rank expressed their ignorance, i.e., the mujtahid companions and the mujtahids after them, even the one who was supported by revelation, peace be upon him. The reason for not finding a clear case: And the dominant assumption is that this mufti's not finding a clear ruling is due to his lack of knowledge or not knowing the place of mention of the required matter, because hardly any incident occurs but its mention is necessarily found in the books of the madhhab. Either it is mentioned exactly, or a general principle is mentioned that includes that incident.
Source pages p. 89

Commentary
This passage from Aap Fatwa Kaisay Den explains a rasm al-mufti rule: the hierarchical method a Hanafi mufti must follow when no explicit ruling is found from the founding imams. The passage begins by citing Al-Hawi al-Qudsi, stating that if no narration exists from Imam Abu Hanifa, one takes the apparent opinion of Imam Abu Yusuf, then Imam Muhammad, then his other major students (Zufar, Hasan ibn Ziyad, etc.) in order. If even these students have no explicit answer, then one looks to the later mashayikh: if they agree, that consensus is followed; if they differ, the majority opinion is taken, especially that of renowned scholars like Abu Hafs al-Kabir, Abu Ja'far al-Hindawani, Abu al-Layth al-Samarqandi, and Imam al-Tahawi. If even the later scholars have no ruling, the mufti must exert personal effort (ijtihad) to derive a ruling, fully aware of his responsibility and fear of Allah. The passage then quotes Fatawa Qadikhan, which qualifies that for non-Zahir al-Riwayah matters, the mufti must ensure the ruling conforms to the principles of the Hanafi imams. If no transmission exists from the imams but later scholars agree, that is followed; if they differ, the mufti does ijtihad. Crucially, if the mufti is a muqallid (not a mujtahid), he must take the opinion of the most knowledgeable Hanafi scholar available and cite the reference. If that scholar is elsewhere, he must correspond. The author then comments that a pure muqallid cannot give fatwa from his own opinion in matters where no explicit ruling is found; rather he must admit his ignorance. The passage concludes with a powerful point: it is rare that an incident has no mention at all in the books of the madhhab—either explicitly or through a general principle. Thus, a mufti's failure to find a ruling is likely due to his own deficiency, not an actual gap in the madhhab.

Key Terms
ظاہر الروایہ (Zahir al-Riwayah): The six core books of Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani containing well-known transmitted rulings of the Hanafi school.
مقلد (muqallid): A mufti who follows the Hanafi madhhab without having the ability to perform ijtihad; he must rely on transmitted rulings from qualified scholars.
متاخرین (mutākhkhirīn): Later Hanafi scholars after the early generations (mutqaddimīn), whose opinions are consulted when no explicit ruling exists from the founding imams.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, after Imam Abu Hanifa, whose apparent opinion should be taken first?
A) Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani
B) Imam Zufar
C) Imam Abu Yusuf
D) Imam Abu Hafs al-Kabir

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi fatwa hierarchy ensures methodological consistency by prescribing a clear sequence of authority from Imam Abu Hanifa through his students to later scholars.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa
intermediate
10 min
The Muqallid Mufti's Duty: Admit Ignorance, Not Invent Rulings
Explaining the limitations of a muqallid mufti and the duty to admit ignorance when no explicit ruling is found.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify when a muqallid mufti must abstain from giving fatwa and instead admit ignorance, and apply the rule that a muqallid must rely on the most knowledgeable scholar or refer the question.

Core Idea
A muqallid mufti without ijtihad cannot issue a personal ruling; he must refer to experts or honestly declare his inability.

The passage emphasizes that not every mufti is qualified to derive rulings from sources. A muqallid (one who follows without independent ijtihad) faces strict limitations. When he cannot find an explicit ruling, he must not fabricate an answer. Instead, he should consult the most knowledgeable Hanafi scholar available, even by correspondence, or openly admit his ignorance. This lesson explores the reasoning behind this rule and the underlying assumption that nearly every case has a precedent in the madhhab.

Guided Path
1
Understand the muqallid's constraint
A muqallid mufti is not a mujtahid; he cannot derive rulings from general principles. He can only transmit established rulings with references.
2
Identify when explicit ruling is absent
When no explicit ruling is found from any faqih in the madhhab, a muqallid must not give an opinion from his own reasoning.
3
Apply the first option: consult more knowledgeable
The muqallid should take the opinion of the most knowledgeable Hanafi scholar available, citing the reference. If that scholar is in another city, he must correspond.
4
Second option: admit ignorance
If no authority can be reached, the muqallid must admit his inability, following the example of the Companions and even the Prophet (peace be upon him).
5
Recognize the underlying assumption
The passage asserts that hardly any incident occurs without mention in the madhhab books, either explicitly or through a general principle. Failure to find it indicates the mufti's lack of knowledge or poor search, not a gap in the school.

متقدمین سے روایت نہ ہو اور متاخرین میں اختلاف ہو تو کیا کیا جائے؟ الحاوی القدی (۹۲) کے آخر میں ہے کہ جب کسی مسئلہ میں امام صاحب سے کوئی روایت نہ پائی جائے تو امام ابو یوسف کے ظاہر قول کو لیا جائے گا۔ پھر امام محمد کے ظاہر قول کو پھر امام زفر اور حسن بن زیادہ وغیرہ امام صاحب کے تمام بڑے تلامذہ کے اقوال کو آخر تک درجہ بدرجہ لیا جائے گا۔ اور جب کسی واقعہ میں ان حضرات سے کوئی صریح جواب مروی نہ ہو اور اس مسئلہ میں بعد کے مشائخ نے کلام کیا ہو اور وہ سب حضرات کسی ایک بات پر متفق ہوں تو اس کو لیا جائے گا اور اگر ان میں اختلاف ہو تو اکثر حضرات کے اس قول کو لیا جائے گا جس پر مشہور ا کا بر مثلا ابو حفص کبیر (۵۵) ابو جعفر ہندوانی (۶۱) ابواللیث سمرقندی (۵۱) اور امام طحاوی (۱۷) وغیرہ نے اعتماد کیا ہو۔
متاخرین کا بھی کوئی قول نہ ہو تو کیا کیا جائے؟ اور اگر بعد کے مشائخ سے بھی قطعاً کوئی صریح حکم مردی نہ ہو تو مفتی اس واقعہ میں غور وفکر کرے اور اپنی پوری طاقت خرچ کرے تا کہ وہ کوئی ایسا حکم دریافت کر لے جس کے ذریعہ وہ اپنی ذمہ داری سے عہدہ برآ ہو سکے اور اس مسئلہ میں انکل سے گفتگو نہ کرنے اپنے منصب اور اس کی ذمہ داری کا احساس کرے اور اللہ تعالیٰ سے ڈرے کیونکہ فتویٰ دینا نہایت اہم معاملہ ہے اس کی جسارت ہر جاہل بد بخت ہی کرتا ہے۔
اور فتاویٰ قاضی خان میں ہے کہ: اگر مسئلہ غیر ظاہر الروایہ میں ہے تو اگر وہ مسئلہ ہمارے ائمہ کے اصول وضوابط کے موافق ہے تو اس پر عمل کیا جائے گا اور اگر کسی مسئلہ میں ہمارے ائمہ سے کوئی روایت نہ پائی جائے اور اس مسئلہ میں متاخرین کسی بات پر متفق ہوں تو اس پر عمل کیا جائے گا اور اگر متاخرین میں اختلاف ہو تو مفتی اجتہاد کرے اور اس کے نزد یک جو بات درست ہو اس کے مطابق فتوی دے اور اگر مفتی مقلد ہو مجتہد نہ ہو تو اپنی رائے میں افقہ کے قول کو لے اور جواب میں اس کا حوالہ دے اور اگر اس کے نزدیک جو افقہ ہے وہ کسی اور شہر میں ہے تو اس سے خط کے ذریعہ رابطہ قائم کرے اور تحقیق کے بعد جواب لکھے اور انکل سے جواب نہ لکھ دئے حلال کو حرام اور حرام کو حلال کر کے اللہ تعالیٰ پر افترا پردازی سے ڈرے ( قاضی خان بر حاشیہ عالمگیری ج ص ۳)
فتوی میں صریح حوالہ ضروری ہے:
میں کہتا ہوں کہ قاضی خان رحمہ اللہ کے اس قول سے کہ: " اگر مفتی مقلد ہو مجتہد نہ ہوانی " یہ بات مفہوم ہوتی ہے کہ مقلد محض کے لیے ان مسائل میں جن میں کسی فقیہ سے صراحی حکم مروی نہیں ہے فتویٰ دینا جائز نہیں اور اس کی تائید اس قول سے ہوتی ہے جس کو البحر الرائق ( ج ۲ ص ۲۶۸) میں فتاوی تا تارخانیہ ( ج ۱ص ۸۲ مقدمہ کی ساتویں فصل ) سے نقل کیا ہے کہ اگر متاخرین میں اختلاف ہو تو مفتی کسی ایک کے قول کو لے اور اگر متاخرین میں سے کسی کا قول نہ پائے تو وہ خود اجتہاد کرے۔ جب کہ وہ فقہ کی وجوہ جانتا ہو اور فقہاء سے مشورہ بھی کرے اھ۔ تا تارخانیہ کا یہ قول کہ جب وہ فقہ کی جملہ تفصیلات سے واقف ہو الخ اس بات کی دلیل ہے کہ جو مفتی یہ نہیں جانتا بلکہ اس نے فقہ کی کوئی ایک کتاب یا اس کا اکثر حصہ پڑھ لیا ہے اور اس کو سمجھ لیا ہے اور اس میں کتابوں کی مراجعت کرنے کی صلاحیت پیدا ہو گئی ہے اور مشہور قابل اعتماد کتابوں میں مسئلہ کہاں ملے گا اس کو جاننے کی اس میں استعداد پیدا ہوگئی ہے ایسا شخص جب کوئی واقعہ کسی کتاب میں نہ پائے تو اس کے لیے جائز نہیں ہے کہ وہ اپنی رائے سے فتویٰ دے دے بلکہ اس کے ذمہ واجب ہے کہ اپنی لاعلمی ظاہر کرے جیسا کہ اس سے بڑے مرتبہ والوں نے لاعلمی ظاہر کی ہے یعنی مجتہدین صحابہ نے اور ان کے بعد کے مجتہدین نے بلکہ اس ہستی نے جو موید بالوحی تھی صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم۔ صریح جزئیہ نہ ملنے کی وجہ : اور غالب گمان یہ ہے کہ اس مفتی کا صراحت نہ پانا اس کی واقفیت کی کمی کی وجہ سے ہے یا مسئلہ مطلوبہ کے ذکر کا محل نہ جانے کی وجہ سے ہے کیونکہ شاید ہی کوئی واقعہ رونما ہوتا ہے مگر اس کا کتب مذہب میں ضرور تذکرہ ہوتا ہے۔ یا تو وہ بعینہ مذکور ہوتا ہے یا کوئی ایسا قاعدہ کلیہ مذکور ہوتا ہے جو اس واقعہ کو بھی شامل ہوتا ہے۔
How to give fatwa? Shama' Rasm Sultanati. What to do when there is no narration from the early scholars and the later scholars differ? At the end of Al-Hawi al-Qudsi (92) it is stated: When in a matter no narration is found from Imam Abu Hanifa, the apparent opinion of Imam Abu Yusuf will be taken. Then the apparent opinion of Imam Muhammad, then Imam Zufar and Hasan ibn Ziyad etc. all the major students of Imam Abu Hanifa up to the end will be taken step by step. And when there is no explicit answer narrated from these personalities in an incident, and later mashayikh have spoken about this matter and all of them agree on one thing, then that will be taken. And if there is disagreement among them, then the opinion of the majority of them will be taken, the one on which the renowned scholars relied, for example Abu Hafs al-Kabir (55), Abu Ja'far al-Hindawani (61), Abu al-Layth al-Samarqandi (51), and Imam al-Tahawi (17) etc. What to do when even the later scholars have no ruling? And if absolutely no explicit ruling is narrated from the later mashayikh, then the mufti should ponder and reflect on that incident and exert his full effort so that he may discover a ruling by which he can discharge his responsibility, and he should not discuss this matter with anyone but should realize his position and its responsibility, and fear Allah, because giving fatwa is a very important matter; only every ignorant wretch dares to do it. And in Fatawa Qadikhan it is stated: If the matter is from non-Zahir al-Riwayah, then if that matter is in accordance with the principles and rules of our imams, then it will be acted upon. And if no narration is found from our imams in a matter, and the later scholars are agreed on something, then that will be acted upon. And if the later scholars differ, then the mufti will exercise ijtihad and give fatwa according to what he deems correct. And if the mufti is a muqallid and not a mujtahid, then he should take the opinion of the most knowledgeable among his own people, and give the reference in his answer. And if the one who is most knowledgeable in his view is in another city, then he should correspond with him by letter, and after investigation write the answer, and he should not write an answer ignorantly, making halal into haram and haram into halal, fabricating against Allah; he should fear (Qadikhan, from marginalia of Alamgiri, vol. 3, p. ?). The necessity of clear reference in fatwa: I say that from this statement of Qadikhan: "If the mufti is a muqallid, not a mujtahid," it is understood that for a pure muqallid, giving fatwa in matters where no explicit ruling is narrated from any faqih is not permissible. And this is supported by that statement which is quoted in al-Bahr al-Raiq (vol. 2, p. 268) from Fatawa Tatarkhaniyya (vol. 1, p. 82, seventh chapter of introduction): that if the later scholars differ, the mufti should take one of their opinions, and if no opinion is found from the later scholars, then he should exercise ijtihad himself, provided he knows the reasons of fiqh and also consults with fuqaha. End. The statement of Tatarkhaniyya that "when he knows all the details of fiqh" etc. is evidence that a mufti who does not know this, but rather has read only one book of fiqh or most of it and understood it, and has developed the ability to refer to books and knows where to find the matter in well-known reliable books—such a person, when he does not find an incident in any book, it is not permissible for him to give fatwa from his own opinion. Rather, it is obligatory upon him to express his ignorance, just as those of higher rank expressed their ignorance, i.e., the mujtahid companions and the mujtahids after them, even the one who was supported by revelation, peace be upon him. The reason for not finding a clear case: And the dominant assumption is that this mufti's not finding a clear ruling is due to his lack of knowledge or not knowing the place of mention of the required matter, because hardly any incident occurs but its mention is necessarily found in the books of the madhhab. Either it is mentioned exactly, or a general principle is mentioned that includes that incident.

Commentary
This passage from Aap Fatwa Kaisay Den explains a rasm al-mufti rule: the hierarchical method a Hanafi mufti must follow when no explicit ruling is found from the founding imams. The passage begins by citing Al-Hawi al-Qudsi, stating that if no narration exists from Imam Abu Hanifa, one takes the apparent opinion of Imam Abu Yusuf, then Imam Muhammad, then his other major students (Zufar, Hasan ibn Ziyad, etc.) in order. The passage then quotes Fatawa Qadikhan, which qualifies that for non-Zahir al-Riwayah matters, the mufti must ensure the ruling conforms to the principles of the Hanafi imams. If that scholar is elsewhere, he must correspond. The passage concludes with a powerful point: it is rare that an incident has no mention at all in the books of the madhhab—either explicitly or through a general principle. مقلد (muqallid): A mufti who follows the Hanafi madhhab without having the ability to perform ijtihad; he must rely on transmitted rulings from qualified scholars.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, if a muqallid mufti cannot find an explicit ruling from any Hanafi scholar, what must he do?
A) Use qiyas to derive a ruling
B) Give a fatwa based on his best understanding

Key Takeaway
A muqallid mufti lacks the authority for independent derivation; when explicit rulings are absent, his duty is to consult experts or honestly declare his inability.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa
intermediate
8 min
Clear Textual Reference (Sarih Hawala) is Mandatory
Establishes that a muqallid mufti must have a transmitted textual basis for his fatwa.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the conditions under which a muqallid mufti may issue a fatwa and apply the rule that a clear transmitted textual reference is mandatory.

Core Idea
A muqallid mufti cannot give fatwa without a transmitted textual source; personal opinion is forbidden.

This lesson establishes a foundational principle of Hanafi iftaa: a mufti who is a muqallid (follower of a madhhab) must have a clear, transmitted textual basis (sarih hawala) for any fatwa he issues. Without such a reference, he is not permitted to rely on his own reasoning or ijtihad. The passage from the source text, citing authoritative later Hanafi fatwa works, underscores this obligation and provides a practical guideline for muftis.

Guided Path
1
Identify the key terms
Understand the distinctions between sarih hawala, muqallid, mujtahid, and mutakhkhirin as used in the text.
These terms define the hierarchy of mufti qualification.
2
Distinguish mufti categories
Classify muftis into at least three levels: mujtahid (capable of ijtihad), muqallid of later scholars (can follow or perform ijtihad under conditions), and ordinary muqallid (must follow explicit transmitted rulings).
The text focuses on the ordinary muqallid.
3
Extract the core ruling
From Qadi Khan's statement, derive the rule: a mere muqallid cannot give fatwa on matters lacking an explicit transmitted ruling.
This is the central obligation.
4
Analyze the supporting evidence
Parse the quote from Fatawa Tatarhaniyya: if later scholars differ, take one; if none, only one who knows fiqh reasons and consults can do ijtihad.
This clarifies the threshold for ijtihad.
5
Apply to a scenario
Given a mufti with limited book knowledge who cannot find an explicit ruling, determine that he must admit ignorance and refrain from issuing a fatwa.
The text argues that inability to find a ruling is usually due to lack of familiarity.

فتوی میں صریح حوالہ ضروری ہے: میں کہتا ہوں کہ قاضی خان رحمہ اللہ کے اس قول سے کہ: ” اگر مفتی مقلد ہو مجتہد نہ ہوانی “ یہ بات مفہوم ہوتی ہے کہ مقلد محض کے لیے ان مسائل میں جن میں کسی فقیہ سے صراحی حکم مروی نہیں ہے فتویٰ دینا جائز نہیں اور اس کی تائید اس قول سے ہوتی ہے جس کو البحر الرائق ( ج ۲ ص ۲۶۸) میں فتاوی تا تارخانیہ ( ج ۱ص ۸۲ مقدمہ کی ساتویں فصل ) سے نقل کیا ہے کہ اگر متاخرین میں اختلاف ہو تو مفتی کسی ایک کے قول کو لے اور اگر متاخرین میں سے کسی کا قول نہ پائے تو وہ خود اجتہاد کرے۔ جب کہ وہ فقہ کی وجوہ جانتا ہو اور فقہاء سے مشورہ بھی کرے اھ۔ تا تارخانیہ کا یہ قول کہ جب وہ فقہ کی جملہ تفصیلات سے واقف ہو الخ اس بات کی دلیل ہے کہ جو مفتی یہ نہیں جانتا بلکہ اس نے فقہ کی کوئی ایک کتاب یا اس کا اکثر حصہ پڑھ لیا ہے اور اس کو سمجھ لیا ہے اور اس میں کتابوں کی مراجعت کرنے کی صلاحیت پیدا ہو گئی ہے اور مشہور قابل اعتماد کتابوں میں مسئلہ کہاں ملے گا اس کو جاننے کی اس میں استعداد پیدا ہوگئی ہے ایسا شخص جب کوئی واقعہ کسی کتاب میں نہ پائے تو اس کے لیے جائز نہیں ہے کہ وہ اپنی رائے سے فتویٰ دے دے بلکہ اس کے ذمہ واجب ہے کہ اپنی لاعلمی ظاہر کرے جیسا کہ اس سے بڑے مرتبہ والوں نے لاعلمی ظاہر کی ہے یعنی مجتہدین صحابہ نے اور ان کے بعد کے مجتہدین نے بلکہ اس ہستی نے جو موید بالوحی تھی صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم۔ صریح جزئیہ نہ ملنے کی وجہ : اور غالب گمان یہ ہے کہ اس مفتی کا صراحت نہ پانا اس کی واقفیت کی کمی کی وجہ سے ہے یا مسئلہ مطلوبہ کے ذکر کا محل نہ جانے کی وجہ سے ہے کیونکہ شاید ہی کوئی واقعہ رونما ہوتا ہے مگر اس کا کتب مذہب میں ضرور تذکرہ ہوتا ہے۔ یا تو وہ بعینہ مذکور ہوتا ہے یا کوئی ایسا قاعدہ کلیہ مذکور ہوتا ہے جو اس واقعہ کو بھی شامل ہوتا ہے۔
Clear reference in fatwa is necessary. I say: From the statement of Qadi Khan (may Allah have mercy on him): 'If the mufti is a muqallid, not a mujtahid...' it is understood that for a mere muqallid, giving fatwa in those issues for which no explicit ruling has been transmitted from any faqih is not permissible. This is supported by the statement quoted in al-Bahr al-Raiq (vol. 2, p. 268) from Fatawa Tatarhaniyya (vol. 1, p. 82, seventh chapter of the introduction): 'If there is disagreement among the later scholars, the mufti should take the saying of one of them; and if he does not find any saying of the later scholars, then he should perform ijtihad himself, provided he knows the reasons of fiqh and also consults the fuqaha.' This statement of Tatarhaniyya that 'when he is aware of all the details of fiqh etc.' indicates that a mufti who does not know that, but has only read one or most of one book of fiqh and understood it, and has acquired the ability to refer to books and knows where the issue is to be found in the reliable well-known books — such a person, when he does not find an incident in any book, it is not permissible for him to give fatwa from his own opinion. Rather, it is obligatory upon him to express his ignorance, just as those greater than him have expressed ignorance: i.e., the mujtahid Companions and the mujtahids after them, and even the one who was supported by revelation (peace be upon him). Reason for not finding an explicit case: The overwhelming presumption is that this mufti's not finding an explicit [ruling] is due to his lack of familiarity or not knowing the place where the required issue is mentioned, because rarely does an incident occur except that its mention is certainly found in the books of the madhhab. Either it is mentioned exactly, or there is a general maxim mentioned that includes that incident.
Source pages p. 90

Commentary
This passage is a carefully argued ruling on the essential condition for a muqallid mufti to issue a fatwa. It begins by stating the rule: a muqallid cannot give fatwa on matters lacking a transmitted explicit ruling. Then it supports this with a quote from Fatawa Tatarhaniyya that distinguishes between later scholars (mutakhkhirin) and cases where no ruling is found: if a later scholar's ruling exists, the mufti follows it; if not, only a scholar who knows the reasons of fiqh and can consult can do ijtihad. The author then applies this logically: a mufti who only knows one book cannot do ijtihad; he must admit ignorance. The authority weight here is from Fatawa Tatarhaniyya and Qadi Khan, which are later fatwa collections (mutakhkhirin). The text also gives a practical insight: the mufti's inability to find a ruling is likely because he hasn't looked properly; the ruling is probably out there. This emphasizes the necessity of thorough research. The passage thus lays down the foundational principle for the mufti's obligation to have a clear textual source for any fatwa.

Key Terms
صریح حوالہ (sarih hawala): A clear transmitted textual reference from a faqih or a reliable book
مقلد (muqallid): One who follows a particular madhhab without being a mujtahid
مجتہد (mujtahid): One capable of deriving rulings from primary sources
متاخرین (mutakhkhirin): Later scholars in the Hanafi madhhab after the early authorities

Key Terms from Source Passage

What must a muqallid mufti do if he cannot find an explicit ruling in the books?
A) Perform ijtihad
B) Admit his ignorance and abstain from giving fatwa
C) Use his personal opinion
D) Ask the questioner to go to another mufti

Key Takeaway
A muqallid mufti must have a clear transmitted textual reference for any fatwa; otherwise, it is wajib to refrain and admit ignorance.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa
intermediate
8 min
Prohibition of Fatwa from Nazir and Qawaid Kulliyya
A rule forbidding fatwa from nazir and qawaid, and requiring explicit source

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the two prohibited methods for a mufti (nazir and qawaid kulliyya) and apply the rule that only a clear textual reference (sarih hawala) suffices for issuing a fatwa.

Core Idea
A mufti cannot rely on similar cases or general maxims—only on explicit textual references.

In the previous lessons, we learned that a mufti must base his fatwa on transmitted evidence. This lesson deepens that principle by warning against two common shortcuts: relying on a case that appears similar (nazir) or using a general fiqh maxim (qawaid kulliyya). Both are tempting when no direct text is found, but both are strictly forbidden. The reason, as explained by later Hanafi masters, is that fiqh rulings are 'akthari' (majority-based) and not universal; subtle differences between cases exist that only the early scholars could identify. Therefore, the mufti's duty is to find a clear textual source, and if he cannot, he must pause or consult a more knowledgeable scholar.

Guided Path
1
Recognize the two prohibited methods
The passage explicitly forbids two ways of deriving a fatwa: (1) relying on a nazir (a case that resembles the current incident) and (2) relying on general legal principles (qawaid kulliyya). Identify each prohibition in the Arabic text.
Nazir is a specific analogous case; qawaid kulliyya are broad rules like 'harm must be removed'.
2
Understand the reason behind each prohibition
For nazir: scholars have written books of furuq (differences) showing that seemingly similar cases often have hidden distinctions that human intellect alone cannot grasp. For qawaid: fiqh rulings are akthari (apply to most but not all cases) and not kulli (universal), so using a general principle may lead to an incorrect exception.
The text cites Ibn Nujaym and al-Barri to establish this as settled across madhhabs.
3
Apply the correct procedure
If a mufti does not find a clear textual reference (sarih hawala), he must postpone his answer (tawaqquf) or ask a scholar who is more knowledgeable (a'lam), even if that scholar is in another city. The mufti who is not a mujtahid may only transmit the sayings of the fuqaha.
This procedure is from Fatawa Khaniyya and Fatawa Zahiriyya.
4
Identify the authority weight of this rule
Recognise that this ruling comes from later fatwa collections (fatawa mutakhkhirin) and is the mufta bihi (operative) position. It is not based on a single primary text but is a consensus of the four madhhabs as transmitted by later scholars.
The text explicitly says 'it is settled in all four madhhabs that fiqhi rulings are akthari'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
نظیر سے فتویٰ نہ دیا جائے: اور کسی نظیر پر اکتفا نہ کی جائے جو واقعہ سے ملتی جلتی ہو اس لیے کہ ممکن ہے اس واقعہ اور اس نظیر کے درمیان فرق ہو جس تک اس مفتی کی نظر نہ پہنچ سکی ہو کیونکہ بہت سے ایسے مسائل ہیں جن کے درمیان اور ان کی نظیروں کے درمیان علماء نے فرق بیان کیا ہے یہاں تک کہ علماء نے اس مقصد کے لیے فروق کی کتابیں لکھی ہیں اور اگر معاملہ ہماری عقلوں کے حوالہ کیا جاتا تو ہم ان میں کوئی فرق نہ کر پاتے ۔ قواعد کلیہ سے بھی فتوی دینا جائز نہیں: بلکہ علامہ ابن نجیم نے فوائد زینیہ میں لکھا ہے کہ قواعد کلیہ اور ضوابط عامہ سے فتویٰ دینا جائز نہیں ہے۔ مفتی کے ذمہ صریح حوالہ دینا ضروری ہے جیسا کہ علماء نے اس کی صراحت کی ہے اور علامہ ابن نجیم نے یہ بھی فرمایا ہے کہ: چاروں مذاہب میں یہ بات طے شدہ ہے کہ فقہی تو اعداکثری ہیں، کلی نہیں ہیں ۔ علامہ بیری رحمہ اللہ نے یہ بات نقل کی ہے لہذا جو مفتی صریح حوالہ نہ پائے اس پر لازم ہے کہ جواب دینے میں توقف کرے یا اعلم سے پوچھے اگر چہ وہ دوسرے شہر میں ہو جیسا کہ یہ بات اس عبارت سے معلوم ہو چکی ہے جو ہم فتاوی خانیہ کے حوالہ سے لکھ آئے ہیں۔ اور فتاویٰ ظہیر یہ میں ہے کہ اگر مفتی مجتہدین میں سے نہ ہو تو اس کے لیے فتویٰ دینا جائز نہیں ہے مگر نقل کے طور پر لہذاوہ فقہاء کے ان اقوال کو نقل کرے جو اس کو یاد ہوں۔
Fatwa should not be given from a similar case (nazir): One should not be content with a nazir that resembles the incident, because it is possible that there is a difference between this incident and its nazir that the mufti's eye did not reach. For there are many issues between which and their nazirs scholars have explained differences, to the extent that scholars have written books of furuq (differences) for this purpose; and if the matter were referred to our intellects, we would not be able to distinguish any difference. Also, giving fatwa from general principles is not permissible: Rather, Allama Ibn Nujaym wrote in al-Fawaid al-Zainiyya that giving fatwa from general principles (qawaid kulliyya) and general rules (dawabit amma) is not permissible. It is necessary for the mufti to provide a clear reference, as the scholars have clarified. And Allama Ibn Nujaym also stated: It is settled in all four madhhabs that fiqhi rulings are akthari (majority), not kulli (universal). Allama al-Barri (may Allah have mercy on him) has transmitted this. Therefore, a mufti who does not find a clear reference must pause in answering or ask someone more knowledgeable, even if he is in another city, as is understood from the statement we wrote citing Fatawa Khaniyya. And in Fatawa Zahiriyya, it is stated: If the mufti is not among the mujtahids, it is not permissible for him to give fatwa except by way of transmission. So he should transmit the sayings of the fuqaha that he remembers.
Source pages p. 91

Commentary
This passage presents two prohibitions. First, the mufti cannot rely on a nazir (a case that appears similar) because scholars have written entire books (Furuq) showing subtle differences between seemingly similar cases. Human intellect alone cannot be trusted to spot these differences. Second, even general fiqh maxims (qawaid kulliyya) cannot be used to derive a fatwa, because fiqh rulings are 'akthari' (majority, probabilistic) and not universal; there are exceptions. The text references Ibn Nujaym and al-Barri, confirming this is a settled principle across madhhabs. The only valid method for a non-mujtahid mufti is to find a clear transmitted reference (sarih hawala). If no reference is found, he must pause or ask a more knowledgeable scholar, even if far away. The authority of these rulings is from later fatwa collections (Fatawa Khaniyya, Fatawa Zahiriyya). This reinforces the earlier lesson's emphasis on the necessity of explicit textual sources.

Key Terms
نظیر (nazir): A similar case that appears analogous to the incident at hand
قواعد کلیہ (qawaid kulliyya): General legal maxims that apply to many cases
اعداکثری (akthari): Rulings that apply to the majority of cases but have exceptions, hence not universal
فروق (furuq): Books detailing nuanced differences between seemingly similar cases

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Ibn Nujaym as cited in the lesson, why is giving fatwa from general principles (qawaid kulliyya) not permissible?
A) Because the mufti is not a mujtahid.
B) Because fiqhi rulings are akthari, not kulli.
C) Because general principles are too vague.
D) Because only the Prophet gave rulings from principles.

Key Takeaway
A mufti must rely exclusively on explicit textual references; similar cases and general maxims are not valid sources for fatwa.

Restrictions on Using Precedent and General Maxims in Fatwa
Rules prohibiting fatwa based on precedent or general maxims

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify when it is impermissible to rely on precedent (nazir) or general maxims (qawaid kulliya) for fatwa, and state the mufti's duty to provide explicit references or withhold (tawaqquf).

Core Idea
A mufti must cite explicit textual rulings; precedent and general maxims alone are insufficient.

This lesson examines foundational rules from Rasm al-Mufti that govern a mufti's methodology. The passage warns against two common shortcuts: relying on a similar precedent (nazir) without verifying hidden differences, and invoking general legal maxims (qawaid kulliya) as a substitute for specific textual authority. You will learn the rationale behind these prohibitions and the proper course of action when explicit references are unavailable.

Guided Path
1
Identify the first prohibition
The passage explicitly forbids giving fatwa based solely on a precedent (nazir) that resembles the current case. Recognize that even similar cases may have hidden differences that the mufti's knowledge cannot reach.
Scholars wrote books of Furuq (differences) to document such subtle distinctions.
2
Understand the second prohibition
Fatwa based on general maxims (qawaid kulliya) or universal principles (dawabit amma) is also prohibited. Ibn Nujaym states that fiqh rulings are akthariyya (predominantly partial), not kulliyya (universal), meaning they have exceptions.
General maxims are useful for derivation but cannot be the sole basis for a fatwa.
3
Recognize the mufti's primary duty
The mufti is required to provide an explicit reference (sarih hawala) from the madhhab. If none exists, he must withhold (tawaqquf) or consult a more learned scholar (a'lam), even if in another city.
This applies to non-mujtahid muftis who act as transmitters (naqil).
4
Note the exception
The passage allows reliance on precedents in cases that are based on custom (urf) and do not contradict sacred texts. This is a limited exception to the general prohibition.
The author promises to elaborate later in the poem's commentary.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
آپ فتوی کیسے دیں؟
شروع رسمی استی [؟] نظیر سے فتویٰ نہ دیا جائے: اور کسی نظیر پر اکتفانہ کی جائے جو واقعہ سے ملتی جلتی ہو اس لیے کہ ممکن ہے اس واقعہ اور اس نظیر کے درمیان فرق ہو جس تک اس مفتی کی نظر نہ پہنچ سکی ہو کیونکہ بہت سے ایسے مسائل ہیں جن کے درمیان اور ان کی نظیروں کے درمیان علماء نے فرق بیان کیا ہے یہاں تک کہ علماء نے اس مقصد کے لیے فروق کی کتابیں لکھی ہیں اور اگر معاملہ ہماری عقلوں کے حوالہ کیا جاتا تو ہم ان میں کوئی فرق نہ کر پاتے ۔ قواعد کلیہ سے بھی فتوی دینا جائز نہیں: بلکہ علامہ ابن نجیم نے فوائد زینیہ میں لکھا ہے کہ قواعد کلیہ اور ضوابط عامہ سے فتویٰ دینا جائز نہیں ہے۔ مفتی کے ذمہ صریح حوالہ دینا ضروری ہے جیسا کہ علماء نے اس کی صراحت کی ہے اور علامہ ابن نجیم نے یہ بھی فرمایا ہے کہ: چاروں مذاہب میں یہ بات طے شدہ ہے کہ فقہی تو اعداکثری ہیں، کلی نہیں ہیں ۔ علامہ بیری رحمہ اللہ نے یہ بات نقل کی ہے لہذا جو مفتی صریح حوالہ نہ پائے اس پر لازم ہے کہ جواب دینے میں توقف کرے یا اعلم سے پوچھے اگر چہ وہ دوسرے شہر میں ہو جیسا کہ یہ بات اس عبارت سے معلوم ہو چکی ہے جو ہم فتاوی خانیہ کے حوالہ سے لکھ آئے ہیں۔ اور فتاویٰ ظہیر یہ میں ہے کہ اگر مفتی مجتہدین میں سے نہ ہو تو اس کے لیے فتویٰ دینا جائز نہیں ہے مگر نقل کے طور پر لہذاوہ فقہاء کے ان اقوال کو نقل کرے جو اس کو یاد ہوں۔
نظیر سے فتویٰ دینا کہاں جائز ہے؟ ہاں بعض مرتبہ ایسے واقعات پیش آتے ہیں جن کا عرف پر مدار ہوتا ہے جو نصوص شرعیہ کے مخالف نہیں ہوتے تو ان میں مفتی نظائر کے مطابق فتوی دے سکتا ہے جیسا کہ ہم اس کو اس نظم کے آخر میں (شعر ۶۹ کی شرح میں ) ذکر کریں گے۔
How do you give a fatwa? Beginning of Rasm al-Mufti. Fatwa should not be given based on precedent: and one should not rely on a precedent that resembles the incident because it is possible there is a difference between this incident and that precedent which the mufti's vision may not have reached, because there are many issues between which and their precedents scholars have stated differences, to the extent that for this purpose scholars have written books of differences (Furuq). And if the matter were referred to our intellects, we would not be able to differentiate between them. It is also not permissible to give fatwa based on general maxims (qawaid kulliya). Rather, Allama Ibn Nujaym wrote in Fawaid Zayniyya that it is not permissible to give fatwa based on general maxims and general principles (dawabit amma). The mufti is required to provide an explicit reference, as scholars have clarified. And Allama Ibn Nujaym also said: It is settled among all four schools that fiqh rulings are predominantly partial (akthariyya), not universal (kulliyya). Allama Birri (RA) narrated this. Therefore, a mufti who does not find an explicit reference must withhold (tawaqquf) from answering or ask a more learned person, even if that person is in another city, as is known from the passage we wrote quoting Fatawa Khaniyya. And in Fatawa Zahiriyya: if the mufti is not among the mujtahids, it is not permissible for him to give fatwa except by way of transmission (naql). So he should transmit those statements of the jurists that he remembers. Where is it permissible to give fatwa based on precedent? Yes, sometimes incidents occur that are based on custom (urf) that do not oppose the sacred texts; then the mufti can give fatwa according to precedents, as we will mention at the end of this poem (in the explanation of verse 69).
Source pages p. 91

Commentary
This passage is a set of rasm rules for the mufti. It opens by stating that a mufti should not give a fatwa merely based on a precedent (nazir) that resembles the case at hand, because even seemingly similar cases may have hidden differences that the mufti is unaware of. Scholars have compiled works on furuq (distinctions) to highlight these differences, indicating that relying on human reasoning alone would miss them. Next, the passage prohibits relying solely on general legal maxims (qawaid kulliya) or universal principles (dawabit amma) for issuing fatwas. This is a key principle in Hanafi ifta: the mufti must cite a specific explicit reference from the madhhab. Ibn Nujaym reinforces this by stating that fiqh rulings are predominantly partial (akthariyya) rather than universal (kulliyya), meaning they have exceptions and context-specific conditions. If the mufti cannot find an explicit ruling, he must halt (tawaqquf) or consult a more learned scholar, even from another city. Furthermore, a non-mujtahid mufti may only transmit the statements of the mujtahid imams; he cannot exercise independent reasoning. An exception is made for cases based on custom (urf) that do not contradict the texts, where precedents can be used. This shows the cautious methodology of Hanafi fatwa-giving: reliance on explicit textual transmission rather than analogical or universal reasoning.

Key Terms
نظیر (nazir): A precedent case from the madhhab that resembles the current incident and could be used as a basis for fatwa if no explicit ruling is found.
قواعد کلیہ (qawaid kulliya): Universal legal maxims (e.g., 'al-umur bi-maqasidiha') that are not sufficient on their own to issue a fatwa without specific supporting texts.
مفتی (mufti): One who issues fatwas; in this context, a non-mujtahid mufti who must transmit the rulings of the madhhab rather than exercise ijtihad.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the primary reason that a mufti cannot rely solely on a general maxim (qawida kulliya) for fatwa?
A) General maxims are not allowed in the Hanafi school.
B) Fiqh rulings are akthariyya (partial, not universal), so maxims have exceptions.
C) The mufti is not knowledgeable enough to apply them.
D) The Quran prohibits using general principles.

Key Takeaway
A Hanafi mufti must base fatwa on explicit textual references from the madhhab; sole reliance on precedent or general maxims is prohibited, and if no reference exists, he must withhold or consult a more learned scholar.

Hierarchical Rules for Tarjih Among Hanafi Imams
Poetic rules for preferring one Hanafi imam over another in different fiqh chapters

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the hierarchical rules of tarjih among Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad in ibadat, qada, and inheritance cases.

Core Idea
In ibadat, Abu Hanifa's saying is primary; in qada, Abu Yusuf; in dhawi al-arham, Muhammad's view is preferred.

This lesson presents a set of refined rules (rasm al-mufti) that guide the mufti in preferring the saying of one Hanafi imam over another in different chapters of fiqh. The rules are presented poetically to aid memorization. Understanding these hierarchies is essential for issuing correct fatwas within the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the fiqh chapter
First, determine whether the issue belongs to ibadat, qada (judicial matters), dhawi al-arham (inheritance), or another category.
2
Recall the tarjih rule for that chapter
For ibadat, the default is to prefer Abu Hanifa unless a narration from him is also adopted by another imam. For qada, prefer Abu Yusuf. For dhawi al-arham, prefer Muhammad.
3
Check for exceptions
Note the exception in ibadat: if Abu Hanifa's narration is adopted by another imam, the preference may shift. Also note that istihsan is generally preferred over qiyas except in a few cases.
4
Apply the textual hierarchy
When multiple texts exist, prefer the matn (core text), then shuruh (commentaries), then qadim fatawa (old fatwas), unless a clearer explicit statement overrides.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
Combine the chapter-specific rule with the textual hierarchy to arrive at the strongest position for fatwa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَهَهُنَا ضوابط محررة غَدْتُ لَدَى أَهْلِ النُّهَى مُقَرَّرَهُ فِي كُلِّ أَبْوَابِ الْعِبَادَاتِ رُجْحُ قَوْلُ الْإِمَامِ مُطْلَقًا مَالَمُ تَضِحُ عَنْهُ رِوَايَةٌ بِهَا الْغَيْرُ اَحَدُ مِثْلُ تَيَهُم لِمَنْ فَمُرًا تبد وَكُلُّ فَرُعَ بِالْقَضَا تَعَلَّقَا قَوْلُ أَبِى يُوسُفَ فِيهِ يُنقى وَفِي مَسَائِلِ ذَوِى الْأَرْحَامِ قَدْ اَفْتَوَابمَا يَقُولُهُ وَرَبَّحُوا اسْتِحْسَانَهُمْ عَلَى الْقِيَاسُ إِلَّامَسَائِلَ وَمَا فِيهَا الْبَاسُ وَظَاهِرُ الْمَرْوى لَيْسَ يُعْدَلُ عنه إلى خلافِهِ اذْيُنقَل لا ينبَغِى الْعَدُوِّلُ عَنْ دِرَايَهُ إِذَا أَتى بوفُقِهَا رَوَايَهُ وَكُلُّ قَولِ جَاءَ يَنْفِي الْكُفْرَا عَنْ مُسْلِمٍ، وَلَوْ ضَعِيفًا أخرى وَكُلُّ مَا رَجع عَنْهُ الْمُجْتَهِدُ صَارَ كَمَنُسُوحٍ فَغَيرُهُ اعْتَمَدُ وَكُلُّ قَوْلِ فِي الْمُتُونَ اثْنَا فَذَاكَ تَرْجِيحُ لَهُ ضِمْنا أتى فَرُجَحَتْ عَلَى الشُّروُح وَالشُّروْحُ عَلَى الْفَتَاوَى الْقِدَمِ مِن ذَاتِ رُجُوحٍ مَالَمْ يَكُن سِوَاهُ لَفُظا صُحَحا فا لا رُجَحُ الَّذِى به قد صرّحا
And here are some refined rules that have become established among people of intellect. In all chapters of worship, the saying of the Imam (Abu Hanifa) is given preference absolutely, as long as there is not a narration from him that someone else has adopted, like the tayammum of one who has thrown dates into water. And every branch that is related to qada (judicial matters), the saying of Abu Yusuf is preferred in it. And in issues of dhawi al-arham (kindred heirs), they gave fatwa according to what he (Muhammad) says. And they gave preference to istihsan over qiyas, except for some issues and there is no harm in them. And the apparent (zahir) of the transmitted (marwi) is not to be deviated from to its opposite, even if it is transmitted. It is not proper to deviate from draya (rational understanding) when a riwaya (narration) comes in accordance with it. And every saying that comes negating kufr from a Muslim, even if weak, is more acceptable. And every saying from which the mujtahid has retracted becomes like abrogated (mansukh), so others rely on something else. And every saying that is established in the matn (text) is considered a tarjih (preference) implicitly, then the commentaries (shuruh) are given preference over the primary texts, and the old fatawa (fatwas) over the commentaries, provided they are not overridden; otherwise, that which is explicitly stated is to be preferred.
Source pages p. 91

Commentary
This passage presents a set of hierarchical rules (rasm al-mufti) for preferring the sayings of the Hanafi imams in different areas. It begins by stating that in all chapters of ibadat (worship), the saying of Imam Abu Hanifa is given absolute preference, unless there is a narration from him that another imam has adopted (like the case of tayammum for someone who put dates in water). For masail related to qada (judicial matters), the saying of Abu Yusuf is preferred. In matters of dhawi al-arham (inheritance by kindred), Imam Muhammad's saying is given fatwa. The scholars have also given preference to istihsan over qiyas except for a few exceptions. Then a key principle: the apparent meaning of the transmitted (zahir al-marwi) should not be deviated from even if a contrary narration is also transmitted. Moreover, one should not deviate from draya (rational understanding) when it aligns with a narration—this means that if the rational understanding matches the transmitted text, it is stronger. Any statement that negates kufr (unbelief) from a Muslim is to be preferred, even if it is weak. If a mujtahid retracts his own saying, it becomes like abrogated. Finally, a hierarchy for tarjih: sayings in the matn (core texts) are given implicit preference, then commentaries (shuruh) over matn, then old fatwa collections (qadim) over commentaries, unless a clearer explicit statement overrides. This structure guides the mufti in determining the strongest position within the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
ظاہر الروایہ (zahir al-riwaya): The apparent/clear transmitted narration from the imams; it is not to be deviated from in favor of a contrary narration.
درایت (diraya): Rational understanding/derived knowledge; the text says it should not be deviated from when a narration agrees with it.
ذوی الارحام (dhawi al-arham): Kindred heirs in inheritance law; relatives who are not Ashab al-Fara'id or Asaba. In these issues, Imam Muhammad's view is preferred.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the rules in this passage, whose saying is preferred in matters related to qada (judicial issues)?
A) Imam Abu Hanifa
B) Imam Abu Yusuf
C) Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani
D) The companion of the imam

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi mufti must apply specific tarjih rules: Abu Hanifa in ibadat, Abu Yusuf in qada, Muhammad in dhawi al-arham, and follow the hierarchy of matn > shuruh > fatawa.

Rules 1-2: Dhawi al-Arham and Istihsan over Qiyas
First two rules of tarjih in fatwa

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the rules that in matters of dhawi al-arham, the opinion of Imam Muhammad is taken, and that istihsan generally outweighs qiyas in Hanafi fatwa.

Core Idea
Istihsan trumps qiyas; dhawi al-arham shares follow Imam Muhammad's qawl.

This lesson covers the first two rules from the poetic summary of tarjih. They address specific areas: the inheritance of distant kindred (dhawi al-arham) and the principle of juristic preference (istihsan). Understanding these helps a mufti know when to depart from strict analogy.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two rules
Read the two rules: (1) In dhawi al-arham matters, fatwa is given according to Imam Muhammad's qawl. (2) Istihsan is preferred over qiyas except in specific issues.
These are the first two lines of the poem.
2
Understand the first rule: Dhawi al-arham
Dhawi al-arham are distant kindred who inherit only in the absence of primary heirs. Imam Muhammad's rulings in this area are authoritative.
This is based on the Hanafi classification of heirs.
3
Understand the second rule: Istihsan over Qiyas
Istihsan is a stronger evidence than qiyas, so it prevails. The exception is 'certain issues' where qiyas may be retained.
This reflects Hanafi usul al-fiqh.
4
Apply to a scenario
Take a case: a deceased leaves a maternal uncle. The qiyas-based rule might differ from Imam Muhammad's view. Apply the rule to choose the correct fatwa.
Practice using the rule in a real fatwa context.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَفِي مَسَائِلِ ذَوِي الْأَرْحَامِ قَدْ أَفْتَوْا بِمَا يَقُولُهُ وَرَجَّحُوا اسْتِحْسَانَهُمْ عَلَى الْقِيَاسِ إِلَّا مَسَائِلَ وَمَا فِيهَا الْبَاسُ وَظَاهِرُ الْمَرْوِيِّ لَيْسَ يُعْدَلُ عَنْهُ إِلَى خِلَافِهِ إِذْ يُنْقَلُ لَا يَنْبَغِي الْعُدُولُ عَنْ دِرَايَةٍ إِذَا أَتَى بِوُفْقِهَا رِوَايَةٌ وَكُلُّ قَوْلٍ جَاءَ يَنْفِي الْكُفْرَ عَنْ مُسْلِمٍ وَلَوْ ضَعِيفًا أُخِذَ وَكُلُّ مَا رَجَعَ عَنْهُ الْمُجْتَهِدُ صَارَ كَمَنْسُوخٍ فَغَيْرُهُ اعْتُمِدَ وَكُلُّ قَوْلٍ فِي الْمُتُونِ أُثْنِي فَذَاكَ تَرْجِيحٌ لَهُ ضِمْنًا أَتَى فَرُجِّحَتِ الْمُتُونُ عَلَى الشُّرُوحِ وَالشُّرُوحُ عَلَى الْفَتَاوَى الْقُدُمِ مِنْ ذَاتِ رُجُوحٍ مَا لَمْ يَكُنْ سِوَاهُ لَفْظًا صُحِّحَا فَإِنْ لَا رُجِّحَ الَّذِي بِهِ قَدْ صُرِّحَا
And in matters of dhawi al-arham, they gave fatwa according to his saying, and they preferred their istihsan over qiyas, except for certain issues and there is no harm in that. And the apparent transmitted is not to be deviated from to its opposite when it is transmitted. It is not proper to deviate from a dirāyah when a riwāyah comes in accordance with it. And every saying that denies kufr from a Muslim, even if weak, is taken. And every saying from which the mujtahid has retracted becomes like mansukh, so other than it is relied upon. And every saying that is praised in the matun, that is an implicit tarjih for it. So the matun are given preference over the shuruh, and the shuruh over the old fatawa that have tarjih, as long as no other wording has been explicitly corrected; if not, the one that has been explicitly stated is preferred.
Source pages p. 92

Commentary
This passage presents the key rules of tarjih (preference) for a mufti. It is a poetic summary (nazm) listing nine principles: (1) In matters of dhawi al-arham (distant kindred), fatwa is given according to Imam Muhammad's qawl. (2) Istihsan is preferred over qiyas except in a few exceptions. (3) The zahir al-riwaya (well-known transmission) is not to be abandoned for a contrary narration even if it exists. (4) One should not abandon a dirāyah (principle derived through reasoning) if there is a riwāyah that supports it. (5) Any qawl that removes kufr from a Muslim is preferred even if weak. (6) A qawl from which the mujtahid retracted is like mansukh. (7) A qawl mentioned in the matun (core texts like al-Mabsut, etc.) has implicit tarjih. (8) Matun are preferred over shuruh, and shuruh over old fatawa. (9) If a qawl other than the matun has been explicitly corrected (tashih), that corrected qawl is preferred. These rules are foundational for a mufti to know the hierarchy of sources in the Hanafi madhhab.

Key Terms
ظاهر الرواية (zahir al-riwaya): The well-known transmitted opinions from the imams in the six core books.
استحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference over qiyas based on a stronger evidence or custom.
ذوي الأرحام (dhawi al-arham): Distant kindred who inherit in the absence of primary heirs in Hanafi law.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Imam Abu Hanifa
B) Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani
C) Imam Abu Yusuf
D) The later fatwa scholars

Key Takeaway
In fatwa, know when to follow Imam Muhammad's qawl and when to prefer istihsan over qiyas.

Rules 3-4: Adherence to Zahir al-Riwaya and Dirāyah
Third and fourth rules of tarjih

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the rules that the apparent transmitted opinion (zahir al-riwaya) is not to be deviated from, and that a derived principle (dirāyah) supported by a narration is to be upheld.

Core Idea
Zahir al-riwaya is binding; dirāyah backed by riwāyah is preferred.

This lesson covers two crucial rules for a mufti: never abandon the apparent transmitted opinion (zahir al-riwaya) for a contrary narration, and never abandon a derived principle (dirāyah) if a narration supports it. These rules ensure consistency and respect for the established transmitted corpus.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two rules
Rule 3: The apparent transmitted (zahir al-riwaya) is not to be deviated from to its opposite. Rule 4: It is not proper to abandon a dirāyah if a riwāyah comes in accordance with it.
These are the third and fourth rules in the poem.
2
Understand Rule 3: Zahir al-Riwaya is binding
The well-known opinions transmitted from the founders (especially Abu Hanifa) in the six core books are the primary source. A mufti cannot abandon them for a weaker or opposite transmission.
This gives stability to the madhhab.
3
Understand Rule 4: Dirāyah with riwāyah
Dirāyah refers to principles derived through reasoning (like qiyas or istihsan). If a reported narration supports that derived principle, the mufti should not discard it.
This encourages integrating reason and transmission.
4
Apply to a scenario
Consider a scenario where a mufti finds a rare transmission that contradicts the well-known zahir al-riwaya ruling. Apply Rule 3 to determine which to follow.
Similarly, if a derived ruling is confirmed by a hadith, it should be maintained.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

And in matters of dhawi al-arham, they gave fatwa according to his saying, and they preferred their istihsan over qiyas, except for certain issues and there is no harm in that. And the apparent transmitted is not to be deviated from to its opposite when it is transmitted. It is not proper to deviate from a dirāyah when a riwāyah comes in accordance with it. And every saying that denies kufr from a Muslim, even if weak, is taken. And every saying from which the mujtahid has retracted becomes like mansukh, so other than it is relied upon. And every saying that is praised in the matun, that is an implicit tarjih for it. So the matun are given preference over the shuruh, and the shuruh over the old fatawa that have tarjih, as long as no other wording has been explicitly corrected; if not, the one that has been explicitly stated is preferred.

This passage presents the key rules of tarjih (preference) for a mufti. It is a poetic summary (nazm) listing nine principles: (1) In matters of dhawi al-arham (distant kindred), fatwa is given according to Imam Muhammad's qawl. Rules 5-9: Special Cases and Source Hierarchy
Rules 5-9 of tarjih

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the rules that sayings preventing kufr are preferred even if weak, retracted opinions are like abrogated, and that matun outweigh shuruh which outweigh old fatawa.

Core Idea
Save belief, honor retraction, and prioritize matun over shuruh over old fatawa.

This lesson consolidates the remaining rules: any statement that removes the charge of kufr from a Muslim is taken even if weak; a mujtahid's retracted opinion is like mansukh; a ruling praised in the matun has implicit tarjih; and the hierarchy of sources: matun > shuruh > old fatawa, unless explicitly corrected.

Guided Path
1
List the five rules
Rules 5-9: (5) A saying that negates kufr is taken even if weak. (6) Retracted opinion is like mansukh. (7) A saying praised in matun has implicit tarjih. (8) Matun > shuruh > old fatawa. (9) The explicitly corrected wording overrides the hierarchy.
These cover various aspects of source evaluation.
2
Understand Rule 5: Kufr negation
If a saying removes the attribution of disbelief from a Muslim, it is given priority even if the saying itself is weak in transmission.
This reflects the principle of 'tahrīm al-kūfr' (avoiding takfir).
3
Understand Rules 6-7: Retraction and praise in matun
If a mujtahid retracted an earlier saying, it is treated as abrogated. A saying that is praised (athni) in the core texts (matun) carries implicit tarjih.
This gives weight to the matun literature.
4
Understand Rules 8-9: Hierarchy and correction
Matun are preferred over shuruh, and shuruh over old fatawa. However, if a different opinion has been explicitly corrected (tashih), that corrected opinion is preferred; otherwise, the explicitly stated opinion in the matun is preferred.
This is the final hierarchy for a mufti.
5
Apply to a scenario
Consider a fatwa issue where there is a weak narration that prevents takfir, a retracted opinion, and a matn ruling. Determine the order of preference.
Practice balancing these rules.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَفِي مَسَائِلِ ذَوِي الْأَرْحَامِ قَدْ أَفْتَوْا بِمَا يَقُولُهُ وَرَجَّحُوا اسْتِحْسَانَهُمْ عَلَى الْقِيَاسِ إِلَّا مَسَائِلَ وَمَا فِيهَا الْبَاسُ وَظَاهِرُ الْمَرْوِيِّ لَيْسَ يُعْدَلُ عَنْهُ إِلَى خِلَافِهِ إِذْ يُنْقَلُ لَا يَنْبَغِي الْعُدُولُ عَنْ دِرَايَةٍ إِذَا أَتَى بِوُفْقِهَا رِوَايَةٌ وَكُلُّ قَوْلٍ جَاءَ يَنْفِي الْكُفْرَ عَنْ مُسْلِمٍ وَلَوْ ضَعِيفًا أُخِذَ وَكُلُّ مَا رَجَعَ عَنْهُ الْمُجْتَهِدُ صَارَ كَمَنْسُوخٍ فَغَيْرُهُ اعْتُمِدَ وَكُلُّ قَوْلٍ فِي الْمُتُونِ أُثْنِي فَذَاكَ تَرْجِيحٌ لَهُ ضِمْنًا أَتَى فَرُجِّحَتِ الْمُتُونُ عَلَى الشُّرُوحِ وَالشُّرُوحُ عَلَى الْفَتَاوَى الْقُدُمِ مِنْ ذَاتِ رُجُوحٍ مَا لَمْ يَكُنْ سِوَاهُ لَفْظًا صُحِّحَا فَإِنْ لَا رُجِّحَ الَّذِي بِهِ قَدْ صُرِّحَا
And in matters of dhawi al-arham, they gave fatwa according to his saying, and they preferred their istihsan over qiyas, except for certain issues and there is no harm in that. And the apparent transmitted is not to be deviated from to its opposite when it is transmitted. It is not proper to deviate from a dirāyah when a riwāyah comes in accordance with it. And every saying that denies kufr from a Muslim, even if weak, is taken. And every saying from which the mujtahid has retracted becomes like mansukh, so other than it is relied upon. And every saying that is praised in the matun, that is an implicit tarjih for it. So the matun are given preference over the shuruh, and the shuruh over the old fatawa that have tarjih, as long as no other wording has been explicitly corrected; if not, the one that has been explicitly stated is preferred.
Source pages p. 92

Commentary
This passage presents the key rules of tarjih (preference) for a mufti. It is a poetic summary (nazm) listing nine principles: (1) In matters of dhawi al-arham (distant kindred), fatwa is given according to Imam Muhammad's qawl. (2) Istihsan is preferred over qiyas except in a few exceptions. (3) The zahir al-riwaya (well-known transmission) is not to be abandoned for a contrary narration even if it exists. (4) One should not abandon a dirāyah (principle derived through reasoning) if there is a riwāyah that supports it. (5) Any qawl that removes kufr from a Muslim is preferred even if weak. (6) A qawl from which the mujtahid retracted is like mansukh. (7) A qawl mentioned in the matun (core texts like al-Mabsut, etc.) has implicit tarjih. (8) Matun are preferred over shuruh, and shuruh over old fatawa. (9) If a qawl other than the matun has been explicitly corrected (tashih), that corrected qawl is preferred. These rules are foundational for a mufti to know the hierarchy of sources in the Hanafi madhhab.

Key Terms
ظاهر الرواية (zahir al-riwaya): The well-known transmitted opinions from the imams in the six core books.
متون (mutun): Core texts of the Hanafi school such as al-Mabsut and al-Jami al-Saghir.
شروح (shuruh): Commentaries on the core texts.
استحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference over qiyas based on a stronger evidence or custom.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Rule 8, which has the highest authority among these?
A) Old fatawa
B) Shuruh
C) Matun
D) They are equal

Key Takeaway
Preserve faith, respect retraction, and follow the hierarchy: matun first, then shuruh, then old fatawa, with correction overriding.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa

Preference of Imam Abu Hanifa's Qawl in Ibadat
Explanation of the first rasm al-mufti rule with exception and example

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the rule of preferring Imam Abu Hanifa's qawl in ibadat and identify the exception when a narration agreeing with the opponent exists.

Core Idea
In ibadat, Imam Abu Hanifa's qawl is mufta bihi unless a narration from him agrees with the opponent.

This lesson explains the first of nine tarjih rules collected by the author: in all acts of worship, the qawl of Imam Abu Hanifa is given priority in fatwa. However, this rule has an important exception. As Burhan al-Din al-Ta'i explains, the scholars have resolved to give fatwa according to Imam Abu Hanifa absolutely in ibadat, but only as long as no narration from him agrees with the opponent. When such a narration exists, it is followed instead. This principle is illustrated with the case of used water (ma' musta'mal). Understanding this rule is essential for any mufti to correctly apply Hanafi tarjih methodology.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Rule
Read the passage and identify the first rule of tarjih: in acts of worship (ibadat), the qawl of Imam Abu Hanifa is given preference absolutely for fatwa.
The rule is stated at the beginning: 'In acts of worship, the qawl of Imam A'zam is the one given fatwa with.'
2
Understand the Rationale
Note the praise of Imam Abu Hanifa's insight and the claim that scholars have chosen his qawl in ibadat due to its correctness.
The author quotes Burhan al-Din al-Ta'i praising Imam Abu Hanifa's fine insight and correct thought.
3
Recognize the Exception
The rule is not absolute. The exception occurs when a narration from Imam Abu Hanifa agrees with the opponent. In that case, that specific narration is followed.
The text says: 'as long as no narration is transmitted from Imam Sahib that agrees with his opponent.'
4
Examine the Example: Used Water
Study the example of ma' musta'mal (water used for wudu). In the external narration (Imam Muhammad's), it is pure but not purifying. This narration agrees with the opponent, so it is taken.
The text explains that other fuqaha mention two narrations from Imam Abu Hanifa; Imam Muhammad took the one that says it is pure but not purifying.
5
Apply to a New Scenario
Consider the case of nabidh al-tamr (date-drink) when no water is available. How would the rule apply? The same exception likely applies if a narration from Imam Abu Hanifa agrees with the opponent on its permissibility for tayammum.
The passage only lists this as another example; we can infer the mechanism is similar.
