میں نے ان اشعار میں (نو) ایسے قواعد جمع کیے ہیں جن کو علماء نے اپنی کتابوں میں متفرق طور پر ذکر کیا ہے اور ان قواعد کو علماء نے رائج اقوال کی علامت مقرر کیا ہے۔ (1) عبادات میں امام اعظم کا قول مفتیٰ بہ ہے: پہلا قاعدہ وہ ہے جس کو برہان الدین علامہ ابراہیم طائی رحمہ اللہ (۲۵) نے منیۃ المصلی کی شرح علیہ استعمالی معروف بہ کبیر بی (ص۶۶) میں فصل تیم میں بیان کیا ہے۔ وہ فرماتے ہیں کہ: امام اعظم کے کیا کہنے! کس قدر ان کی نظر باریک تھی! اور کس قدر ان کی فکر درست تھی ! اور کوئی تو وجہ تھی کہ علماء نے عبادات میں مطلقاً امام اعظم رحمہ اللہ کے قول پر فتوی دینا تجویز کیا ہے! اور جائزہ لینے سے صورت حال بھی یہیں سامنے آتی ہے۔ (کہ ہر جگہ آپ ہی کے اقوال پر فتویٰ ہوتا ہے ) جب تک امام صاحب سے آپ کے مخالف کے قول کے موافق کوئی روایت مروی نہ ہوا جیسے ماء مستعمل کی طہارت میں اور نبیذ تمر کے سوا پانی نہ ہونے متملی کے معنی ہیں مستفید کیا جاتا ہے عملی عمرہ: طویل غمر والا ہوتا اور فائدہ اٹھانا۔ ماء مستعمل کا حکم ظاہر روایت میں مذکور نہیں ہے اس وجہ سے کافی میں جو کتب ظاہر روایت کا مجموعہ ہے صرف اتنا ذکر کیا گیا ہے کہ اس سے وضو کرنا جائز نہیں اور اس کی وضاحت نہیں کی کہ وہ پاک ہے یا نا پاک فقہاء عراق نے بھی اس مسئلہ میں ہمارے ائمہ کے درمیان اختلاف ذکر نہیں کیا بس یہ کہا ہے کہ ماء مستعمل ہمارے ائمہ کے نزدیک پاک ہے مگر پاک کرنے والا نہیں ہے۔“ مگر دیگر فقہاء نے اختلاف ثابت کیا ہے وہ کہتے ہیں کہ ماء مستعمل کے سلسلہ میں امام ابو حنیفہ سے دو روایتیں ہیں امام محمد کی روایت میں وہ پاک ہے مگر پاک کرنے والا نہیں ہے۔ امام محمد نے اسی روایت کو لیا۔
I have collected in these verses nine such rules that scholars have mentioned in their books separately, and the scholars have established these rules as indicators of the prevalent opinions. (1) In acts of worship, the qawl of Imam A'zam is the one given fatwa with: The first rule is that which Burhan al-Din Allamah Ibrahim al-Ta'i (may Allah have mercy on him) explained in his commentary on Munyat al-Musalli, called 'Kabir Bay' (p.66) in the chapter of tayammum. He said: 'What can be said about Imam A'zam! How fine his insight was! How correct his thought! And there must be a reason why the scholars have resolved to give fatwa according to the qawl of Imam A'zam absolutely in acts of worship. And upon examination, the situation appears thus: that everywhere his qawls are given fatwa with, as long as no narration is transmitted from Imam Sahib that agrees with his opponent. Like in the issue of the purity of used water (ma' musta'mal) and when there is no water except date-drink (nabidh tamr). The word 'mutamalli' means 'benefiting'. 'Amali 'Umrai': means one with a long life and taking benefit. The ruling of used water is not mentioned in zahir al-riwaya; therefore, in Kafi, which is a collection of books of zahir al-riwaya, only this much is mentioned that performing wudu with it is not permissible, and it is not clarified whether it is pure or impure. The fuqaha of Iraq also did not mention the disagreement among our imams in this issue; they only said that used water is pure according to our imams but is not purifying. However, other fuqaha have established disagreement; they say that there are two narrations from Imam Abu Hanifa regarding used water. In the narration of Imam Muhammad, it is pure but not purifying. Imam Muhammad took this narration.
Source pages p. 92

Commentary
This passage explains the first rule: In all acts of worship ('ibadat), the qawl of Imam Abu Hanifa is given preference absolutely, unless there is a narration from him that agrees with the opponent. The author quotes Burhan al-Din Ibrahim al-Ta'i in his commentary on Munyat al-Musalli, who praises Imam Abu Hanifa's sharp insight and explains that the scholars have chosen his qawl in 'ibadat. The rule has an exception: when a narration from Imam Abu Hanifa agrees with the opponent, then that narration is followed. Examples are the issues of used water (ma' musta'mal) and tayammum with date-drink (nabidh tamr) when no water is available. For ma' musta'mal, the zahir al-riwaya does not explicitly state its purity; it only says wudu with it is invalid. The fuqaha of Iraq (Kufans) did not mention disagreement among the three imams; they merely said it is pure but not purifying. Other fuqaha mention two narrations from Imam Abu Hanifa: one that it is impure (not mentioned here) and one that it is pure but not purifying. Imam Muhammad took the latter narration, which agrees with the opponent (i.e., other schools). In this case, since the narration from Imam Abu Hanifa coincides with the opponent, the general rule of preferring his qawl is not applied; instead, this specific narration is followed.

Key Terms
ماء مستعمل (ma' musta'mal): Water that has been used for wudu or ghusl; its ruling on purity and purifying ability.
نبيذ التمر (nabidh al-tamr): A drink made from dates; used for tayammum when no water is available.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) When Imam Muhammad disagrees
C) When a narration from Imam Abu Hanifa agrees with the opponent
D) When the issue is about transactions

Key Takeaway
In ibadat, Imam Abu Hanifa's qawl is mufta bihi unless a narration from him agrees with the opponent.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa

Hierarchy of Textual Authorities: Matn over Sharh
Hierarchy rule for fatwa from Rasm al-Mufti

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the hierarchy of textual authorities (matn, sharh, old fatwas) to determine which ruling to prefer in a fatwa scenario.

Core Idea
Matn is preferred over sharh, and sharh over old fatwas, unless the matn's ruling is explicitly corrected.

When a mufti encounters conflicting statements in different books of the madhhab, he needs a clear hierarchy to decide which ruling to rely on. This passage from the commentary on Rasm al-Mufti lays down a fundamental rule: the matn (core text) carries implicit preference over sharh (commentaries), and sharh is preferred over older fatwa collections. However, if a statement from outside the matn has been explicitly corrected in a reliable source, that corrected statement takes precedence. This rule ensures consistency and prevents arbitrary selection.

Guided Path
1
Identify the textual levels
Recognize the three levels: matn (e.g., al-Mukhtar, Kanz al-Daqa'iq), sharh (e.g., al-'Inayah, al-Binayah), and old fatwa collections (e.g., al-Fatawa al-Hindiyya). Determine which texts you have for the issue at hand.
Matn works are condensed and represent the established Zahir al-Riwayah.
2
Apply default preference
When conflicting, give preference to matn over sharh, and sharh over old fatwas. This is the default hierarchy stated in the rule.
3
Check for explicit correction
If a statement from a source outside the matn (e.g., a sharh or fatwa) has been explicitly corrected by a reliable authority (e.g., in a later verified edition or a super-commentary), then the corrected statement is preferred over the default hierarchy.
Explicit correction must be clear and recognized; implicit preference is not enough to override the matn.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
شرح رسم المفتي
علاوہ قول معتمد ہے
(۵۰) اور ہر وہ قول جس کو متون میں لیا گیا ہے۔ تو یہ اس قول کی ضمن ترجیح ہے جو اس کو حاصل ہوگئی ہے۔
(21) پس ترجیح دی جائے گی متون کو شروح پر اور شروح کو ترجیح رکھنے والے پرانے فتاوی پر ۔ (۵۲) جب تک متون کے علاوہ قول کی مراد یہ تصحیح نہ کی گئی ہو۔ ورنہ ارجح وہ قول ہے جس کی صراحی تصحیح کی گئی ہے۔
Commentary on Rasm al-Mufti. Besides the relied-upon saying: (50) And every saying that is included in the matn (core texts) has an implicit preference that has been acquired. (21) So preference will be given to matn over sharh, and sharh over older fatwas that hold preference. (52) As long as the meaning of a saying other than the matn has not been explicitly corrected. Otherwise, the preferred saying is the one that has been explicitly corrected.
Source pages p. 93

Commentary
This passage is a methodological rule (rasm) for muftis regarding the hierarchy of textual authorities when issuing fatwas. The author explains that when there are conflicting statements, the matn (the original text of works like al-Mukhtar or al-Kanz) carries implicit preference over sharh (commentaries like al-Inayah or al-Binayah). Similarly, sharh is preferred over older fatwa collections. However, if a statement from outside the matn has been explicitly corrected (e.g., in a later verified edition), that corrected statement becomes the preferred one. This rule ensures consistency and reliability in fatwa, as the matn represents the established transmitted opinion (Zahir al-Riwayah). The numbers (50, 21, 52) likely refer to verses from the original Rasm al-Mufti poem or marginal annotations.

Key Terms
متن (matn): The core text of a fiqh work (e.g., al-Mukhtar, Kanz al-Daqa'iq) that represents the relied-upon position of the madhhab.
شرح (sharh): A commentary on a matn that explains its rulings and may include additional details or alternative opinions.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) Matn over sharh, sharh over old fatwa collections
C) Old fatwa collections over sharh, then matn

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fatwa, the default hierarchy is matn over sharh, and sharh over old fatwas, but explicit correction overrides the default.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa
intermediate
8 min
First Qaida: Imam Abu Hanifa's Opinion in Ibadat
Establishes a rasm al-mufti rule for ibadat

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the first qaida of rasm al-mufti to determine whether a fatwa in ibadat is consistent with Imam Abu Hanifa's position, using the examples of ma' musta'mal and nabidh tamr.

Core Idea
In ibadat, all fatwa ultimately traces back to Imam Abu Hanifa's opinion, even when apparently given on another Hanafi Imam.

This lesson introduces the foundational rule for muftis in the Hanafi school: in matters of worship (ibadat), the relied-upon opinion for fatwa is always that of Imam Abu Hanifa. However, later Hanafi Imams like Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani sometimes have opinions that appear different. The rule explains that these are often narrations (riwayat) from Imam Abu Hanifa himself, so following them still constitutes following his position. This ensures the madhhab's internal consistency. We will explore the rule through two classical examples: used water (ma' musta'mal) and date infusion (nabidh tamr).

Guided Path
1
Identify the qaida
State the rule: في العبادات، قول الإمام الأعظم هو المعتمد في الفتوى. Note that it applies absolutely ('ibadat), with a singular exception.
The exception is when a narration (riwaya) from Imam Abu Hanifa matches the opponent's view.
2
Understand the caveat
If a fatwa is based on another Hanafi Imam (e.g., Abu Yusuf or Muhammad), it must be verified whether that opinion is also a narration from Imam Abu Hanifa. If yes, it still falls under the rule.
The author stresses that many such opinions are indeed riwayat from Abu Hanifa.
3
Apply to ma' musta'mal
The opposed position (Imam Muhammad's view that ma' musta'mal is tahir ghair mutahhir) is a narration from Abu Hanifa. Thus, fatwa on that view conforms to the rule.
The source mentions that Imam Muhammad reported this from Abu Hanifa.
4
Apply to nabidh tamr
Imam Abu Yusuf's opinion (tayammum only) is the final position of Imam Abu Hanifa. Thus, fatwa on Abu Yusuf's view is actually fatwa on Abu Hanifa's final qawl.
The third riwaya (tayammum only) is the mufta bihi position.
5
Recognize the thamarah
The practical consequence: a mufti must check the chain of narration when encountering an opinion of a Hanafi Imam. If it traces back to Abu Hanifa, it is acceptable for fatwa in ibadat.
This rule maintains the madhhab's unity and prevents fragmentation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
میں نے ان اشعار میں (نو) ایسے قواعد جمع کیے ہیں جن کو علماء نے اپنی کتابوں میں متفرق طور پر ذکر کیا ہے اور ان قواعد کو علماء نے رائج اقوال کی علامت مقرر کیا ہے۔ (1) عبادات میں امام اعظم کا قول مفتی یہ ہے:
پہلا قاعدہ وہ ہے جس کو برہان الدین علامہ ابراہیم طبی رحمہ اللہ (۲۵) نے منیۃ المصلی کی شرت علیہ استمالی معروف به کبیر بی (ص۶۶) میں فصل تیم میں بیان کیا ہے۔ وہ فرماتے ہیں کہ: امام اعظم کے کیا کہنے! کس قدر ان کی نظر باریک تھی! اور کس قدر ان کی فکر درست تھی ! اور کوئی تو وجہ تھی کہ علما ، نے عبادات میں مطلقاً امام اعظم رحمہ اللہ کے قول پر فتوی دینا تجویز کیا ہے! اور جائزہ لینے سے صورت حال بھی یہیں سامنے آتی ہے۔ (کہ ہر جگہ آپ ہی کے اقوال پر فتویٰ ہوتا ہے ) جب تک امام صاحب سے آپ کے مخالف کے قول کے موافق کوئی روایت مروی نہ ہوا جیسے ماء مستعمل کی طہارت میں اور نبیذ تمر کے سوا پانی نہ ہونے کی صورت میں صرف تیم کرنے میں ۔"
یعنی عبادات میں اگر امام اعظم کے علاوہ کسی اور کے قول پر فتوی ہوتا ہے تو اس کی وجہ یہ ہوتی ہے کہ وہ صرف دوسرے امام کا قول نہیں ہوتا بلکہ وہ امام صاحب کی ایک روایت بھی ہوتی ہے اس لیے وہ فتوئی بھی امام صاحب ہی کے قول پر سمجھا جائے گا )

متملی کے معنی ہیں مستفید کیا جاتا ہے عملی عمرہ: طویل غمر والا ہوتا اور فائدہ اٹھانا۔ ماء مستعمل کا حکم ظاہر روایت میں مذکور نہیں ہے اس وجہ سے کافی میں جو کتب ظاہر روایت کا مجموعہ ہے صرف اتنا ذ کر کیا گیا ہے کہ اس سے وضو کرنا جائز نہیں اور اس کی وضاحت نہیں کی کہ وہ پاک ہے یا نا پاک فقباء عراق نے بھی اس مسئلہ میں ہمارے ائمہ کے درمیان اختلاف ذکر نہیں کیا بس یہ کہا ہے کہ ماء مستعمل ہمارے ائمہ کے نزدیک پاک ہے مگر پاک کرنے والا نہیں ہے۔" مگر دیگر فقہاء نے اختلاف ثابت کیا ہے وہ کہتے ہیں کہ ماء مستعمل کے سلسلہ میں امام ابو حنیفہ سے دو روایتیں ہیں امام محمد کی روایت میں وہ پاک ہے مگر پاک کرنے والا نہیں ہے۔ امام محمد نے اسی روایت کو لیا ہے۔ امام زفر نے بھی امام ابو حنیفہ سے یہی روایت نقل کی ہے جیسا کہ امام قاضی خان نے اس کو اپنی شرت میں ذکر کیا ہے اور امام ابو یوسف اور حسن بن زیاد کی روایت میں ناپاک ہے البتہ امام حسن امام صاحب سے نجاست غلیظہ روایت کرتے ہیں اور امام ابو یوسف نجاست خفیفہ اور ہر شاگرد نے وہی قول لیا ہے جو اس نے روایت کیا ہے (بحرج اص۹۴) مذکورہ بالا تفصیل سے اندازہ ہوا ہو گا کہ ماء مستعمل میں اگر امام محمد رحمہ اللہ کے قول پر فتوئی ہے تو وہ بھی حقیقت میں امام اعظم کے قول پر فتوئی ہے کیونکہ امام محمد رحمہ اللہ کا قول امام اعظم کی روایت ہے۔
نبیذ تمر میں امام اعظم رحمہ اللہ سے تین روایتیں ہیں ۔ پہلی روایت اور وہ امام صاحب کا پہلا قول ہے۔ یہ ہے کہ اس سے وضو ضروری ہے اور اس کے ساتھ تیم ملانا مستحب ہے۔ اور دوسری روایت یہ ہے کہ وضو ء اور تیم کو جمع کرنا واجب ہے جیسے گدھے کے جھوٹے کا حکم ہے اس قول کو امام محمد نے لیا ہے اور نمایة البیان میں اس کو پسند کیا ہے اور اسی کو ترجیح دی ہے اور تیسری روایت یہ ہے کہ صرف تیم کرے نبیذ سے وضو نہ کرے اور یہ امام صاحب کا آخری قول ہے۔ اس کی طرف امام اعظم نے رجوع کیا ہے اور یہی صحیح ہے اور یہی امام ابو یوسف امام شافعی امام مالک، امام احمد اور اکثر علماء کا قول ہے اور اس کو امام طحاوی نے پسند کیا ہے (بحر ج ا ص ۱۳۷)
مذکورہ بالا تفصیل سے معلوم ہوا کہ نبیذ تمر میں امام ابو یوسف کے قول پر فتوئی ہے تو وہ بھی در حقیقت امام اعظم ہی کے قول پر فتوئی ہے کیونکہ امام ابو یوسف کا جو قول ہے وہی امام صاحب کا آخری قول ہے۔
I have collected nine such rules in these poems that scholars have mentioned scattered in their books, and scholars have made these rules the sign of prevalent opinions. (1) In worship, the opinion of the Great Imam is the one for fatwa: The first rule is that which Burhan al-Din 'Allama Ibrahim al-Tabi'i (25) mentioned in the commentary on Munyat al-Musalli, known as Kabir Bay (p. 66), in the chapter on tayammum. He says: What can one say about the Great Imam! How subtle his insight was! How correct his thinking was! There must be a reason that scholars absolutely prescribed giving fatwa according to the Great Imam's opinion in worship! And upon investigation, the situation appears so (that fatwa is always given on his opinions) unless there is a narration from the Imam matching the opinion of his opponent, as in the purity of used water (ma' musta'mal) and in the case of having no water except date-infused water (nabidh tamr) and performing tayammum only. Meaning, if in worship a fatwa is given on the opinion of someone other than the Great Imam, the reason is that it is not merely the other Imam's opinion, but it is also a narration from the Great Imam, so that fatwa is also considered to be on the Great Imam's opinion. ... The details above show that in used water, if fatwa is given on Imam Muhammad's opinion, it is in reality fatwa on the Great Imam's opinion because Imam Muhammad's opinion is a narration from the Great Imam. Regarding nabidh tamr, there are three narrations from the Great Imam... From the above details it is known that in nabidh tamr, the fatwa on Imam Abu Yusuf's opinion is in reality also on the Great Imam's opinion because Imam Abu Yusuf's opinion is the final opinion of the Great Imam.
Source pages p. 93

Commentary
This passage introduces the first of nine qawaid (rules) for muftis. The rule states that in matters of 'ibadat (worship), the authoritative opinion for fatwa is that of Imam Abu Hanifa (the Great Imam). This is based on the insight and precision of Imam Abu Hanifa. The only exception is when a narration from Imam Abu Hanifa himself coincides with the opinion of his opponent (e.g., Abu Yusuf or Muhammad). The author provides two detailed examples to illustrate this principle: (1) Ma' musta'mal (water used for ablution): There are multiple narrations from Imam Abu Hanifa. Imam Muhammad's narration says it is pure but not purifying; Imam Abu Yusuf and Hasan ibn Ziyad narrate impurity. The fatwa often given on Imam Muhammad's view is actually based on a narration from Imam Abu Hanifa, so it falls under the rule. (2) Nabidh tamr (date infusion): Imam Abu Hanifa had three positions. The third and final position (tayammum only, no wudu with it) is the one chosen by Imam Abu Yusuf, and it is also the view of many other Imams. Thus, even when fatwa is given on Imam Abu Yusuf's view, it aligns with Imam Abu Hanifa's final position, maintaining the rule. The passages underline that fatwa in 'ibadat ultimately traces back to Imam Abu Hanifa's narrations, preserving the madhhab's unity.

Key Terms
قاعدة (qa'ida): A legal rule or maxim in the Hanafi school.
ماء مستعمل (ma' musta'mal): Water that has been used for wudu or ghusl; its legal status regarding purity is debated.
نبیذ تمر (nabidh tamr): Water in which dates have been soaked; used for wudu in cases of water scarcity.
روایت (riwaya): A narration or transmission of an opinion from an Imam.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is a fatwa on Imam Muhammad's opinion regarding ma' musta'mal considered consistent with the first qaida?
A) Because Imam Muhammad is a separate authority equal to Abu Hanifa
B) Because Imam Muhammad's opinion is a narration from Imam Abu Hanifa
C) Because the Quran and Sunnah directly support Imam Muhammad's view
D) Because the majority of Hanafis follow Imam Muhammad

Key Takeaway
In ibadat, all fatwa ultimately traces back to Imam Abu Hanifa through his narrations, ensuring the madhhab's internal consistency.

Second Qaida: Imam Abu Yusuf's Opinion in Qada
Establishes that Imam Abu Yusuf's opinion is preferred in judicial matters

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the second qaida of rasm al-mufti to identify which Imam's opinion is preferred in judicial matters and explain the rationale based on practical experience.

Core Idea
In judicial matters (qada), fatwa follows Imam Abu Yusuf because his experience as a judge overrides the general primacy of Imam Abu Hanifa.

The second rule of fatwa prioritization in the Hanafi school addresses judicial matters. While the first rule gives precedence to Imam Abu Hanifa in acts of worship (ibadat), this rule shifts to Imam Abu Yusuf in qada. The reason is practical: Imam Abu Yusuf served as chief judge and had hands-on experience with court procedures, evidence, and litigation, making his opinions more suitable for real-world judicial application.

Guided Path
1
Identify the rule
State the second qaida: In matters of qada, fatwa is according to Imam Abu Yusuf's opinion.
This is a specific exception to the general hierarchy.
2
Understand the scope
Distinguish qada from ibadat. Qada includes court rulings, evidence, litigation, and judicial procedures. Ibadat includes prayer, fasting, etc.
This rule applies only to qada-related questions.
3
Grasp the rationale
The reason given is that Imam Abu Yusuf had more experience (tajribat) in judicial matters. He served as a judge for many years.
Practical expertise overrides theoretical primacy.
4
Recognize the sources
The rule is cited from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq (vol. 6, p. 282) and Fatawa al-Bazzaziyya (book of qada).
Both are major Hanafi references for fatwa rules.
5
Apply the rule
When giving a fatwa on a judicial issue (e.g., testimony, court procedures), the mufti should first look for Abu Yusuf's opinion. If not found, he may refer to other Imams.
This ensures the fatwa aligns with judicial practicality.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
دوسرا قاعدہ وہ ہے جو البحر الرائق ( ج ۶، ص۲۸۲) میں فصل الحبس سے ذرا پہلے مذکور ہے
صاحب بحر فرماتے ہیں:
اور قلیہ کے باب المفتی میں ہے کہ جن امور کا تعلق قضا سے ہے ان میں فتویٰ امام ابو یوسف کے قول پر ہے کیوں کہ ان کو قضاء کے سلسلہ میں تجربات زیادہ تھے فتاوی بزازیہ کی کتاب القضا میں بھی ایسا ہی ہے۔
The second rule is that which is mentioned in al-Bahr al-Ra'iq (vol. 6, p. 282) just before the chapter on al-Habs. The author of al-Bahr says: 'And in the chapter on the mufti, it is said that in matters related to qada (judiciary), fatwa is according to the opinion of Imam Abu Yusuf, because he had more experience in matters of qada. Similarly, it is in Fatawa al-Bazzaziyya, in the book of qada.'
Source pages p. 94

Commentary
This passage presents the second qaida (rule) from the nine collected by the author. It addresses judicial matters (qada). The rule states that when a mufti is asked about rulings that pertain to court cases, judges, or litigation (masa'il al-qada), the authoritative opinion for fatwa is that of Imam Abu Yusuf, not necessarily Imam Abu Hanifa. The reasoning given is that Imam Abu Yusuf had extensive practical experience as a judge (he was the chief qadi of Baghdad). Therefore, his rulings in such matters are considered more appropriate for the realities of judicial practice. The author cites two sources: al-Bahr al-Ra'iq by Ibn Nujaym and Fatawa al-Bazzaziyya. This rule complements the first rule: in 'ibadat, preference is for Imam Abu Hanifa; in qada, preference shifts to Abu Yusuf. This reflects the Hanafi principle that the weight of opinions may vary depending on the field of fiqh due to practical considerations.

Key Terms
قضاء (qada): Judicial matters, including court rulings, evidence, and legal procedures.
امام ابو یوسف (Imam Abu Yusuf): One of the three main Hanafi Imams, known for his expertise in qada and his role as chief judge.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is Imam Abu Yusuf's opinion preferred in matters of qada?
A) Because he was a more prolific writer
B) Because he had more experience in judicial matters
C) Because he was taught by Imam Abu Hanifa
D) Because his opinions are easier to implement

Key Takeaway
In judicial matters, the Hanafi mufti should prefer Imam Abu Yusuf's opinion over others because of his practical experience as a judge.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa
intermediate

Fatwa in Judicial Matters: Preference for Imam Abu Yusuf
Establishes the rule for giving fatwa in qada matters according to Imam Abu Yusuf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule for giving fatwa in judicial matters and apply it to identify the mufta bih opinion in qada cases.

Core Idea
In judicial matters, the mufta bih is Imam Abu Yusuf's opinion, due to his practical experience.

This passage is a rasm al-mufti rule from Hanafi usul al-iftaa. It establishes a crucial hierarchy: while devotional matters (ibadat) follow Imam Abu Hanifa, judicial matters (qada) follow Imam Abu Yusuf. The reasoning is not arbitrary but based on Imam Abu Yusuf's extensive practical experience in the judiciary, which gave him superior insight into the consequences of rulings. This lesson unpacks the rule, its rationale, and how it applies to real cases.

Guided Path
1
Identify the category
Determine whether the case falls under 'ibadat' (devotional acts) or 'qada' (judicial/transactional matters). The rule applies only to qada.
Qada includes litigation, testimony, court procedures, and similar mu'amalat.
2
State the rule
For qada matters, the mufta bih (relied-upon opinion) is that of Imam Abu Yusuf, not Imam Abu Hanifa or Muhammad al-Shaybani.
This is a specific exception within the Hanafi school's hierarchy.
3
Explain the rationale
Imam Abu Yusuf had more practical experience as a judge, giving him deeper understanding of real-world implications. This mirrors Imam Abu Hanifa's own retraction of a ruling after performing Hajj himself.
The reasoning is talili (based on cause): increased experience leads to more informed rulings.
4
Apply to examples
Analyze the given examples: (a) used water – following Imam Muhammad is actually following a transmission from Abu Hanifa; (b) date infusion – Imam Abu Yusuf's opinion is Abu Hanifa's final view; (c) silent defendant – Abu Yusuf's imprisonment approach is mufta bih.
Following a student can still mean following the Imam when the student's opinion is a transmission or the Imam's final position.

شرح زنم المفتی کی صورت میں صرف تیم کرنے میں ۔
یعنی عبادات میں اگر امام اعظم کے علاوہ کسی اور کے قول پر فتوی ہوتا ہے تو اس کی وجہ یہ ہوتی ہے کہ وہ صرف دوسرے امام کا قول نہیں ہوتا بلکہ وہ امام صاحب کی ایک روایت بھی ہوتی ہے اس لیے وہ فتوئی بھی امام صاحب ہی کے قول پر سمجھا جائے گا ) (۲) قضاء کے مسائل میں امام ابو یوسف کا قول مفتی یہ ہے:
دوسرا قاعدہ وہ ہے جو البحر الرائق ( ج ۶، ص۲۸۲) میں فصل الحبس سے ذرا پہلے مذکور ہے
صاحب بحر فرماتے ہیں:

لیے ہے۔ امام زفر نے بھی امام ابو حنیفہ سے یہی روایت نقل کی ہے جیسا کہ امام قاضی خان نے اس کو اپنی شرت میں ذکر کیا ہے اور امام ابو یوسف اور حسن بن زیاد کی روایت میں ناپاک ہے البتہ امام حسن امام صاحب سے نجاست غلیظہ روایت کرتے ہیں اور امام ابو یوسف نجاست خفیفہ اور ہر شاگرد نے وہی قول لیا ہے جو اس نے روایت کیا ہے (بحرج اص۹۴) مذکورہ بالا تفصیل سے اندازہ ہوا ہو گا کہ ماء مستعمل میں اگر امام محمد رحمہ اللہ کے قول پر فتوئی ہے تو وہ بھی حقیقت میں امام اعظم کے قول پر فتوئی ہے کیونکہ امام محمد رحمہ اللہ کا قول امام اعظم کی روایت ہے۔
نبیذ تمر میں امام اعظم رحمہ اللہ سے تین روایتیں ہیں ۔ پہلی روایت اور وہ امام صاحب کا پہلا قول ہے۔ یہ ہے کہ اس سے وضو ضروری ہے اور اس کے ساتھ تیم ملانا مستحب ہے۔ اور دوسری روایت یہ ہے کہ وضو ء اور تیم کو جمع کرنا واجب ہے جیسے گدھے کے جھوٹے کا حکم ہے اس قول کو امام محمد نے لیا ہے اور نمایة البیان میں اس کو پسند کیا ہے اور اسی کو ترجیح دی ہے اور تیسری روایت یہ ہے کہ صرف تیم کرے نبیذ سے وضو نہ کرے اور یہ امام صاحب کا آخری قول ہے۔ اس کی طرف امام اعظم نے رجوع کیا ہے اور یہی صحیح ہے اور یہی امام ابو یوسف امام شافعی امام مالک، امام احمد اور اکثر علماء کا قول ہے اور اس کو امام طحاوی نے پسند کیا ہے (بحر ج ا ص ۱۳۷)
مذکورہ بالا تفصیل سے معلوم ہوا کہ نبیذ تمر میں امام ابو یوسف کے قول پر فتوئی ہے تو وہ بھی در حقیقت امام اعظم ہی کے قول پر فتوئی ہے کیونکہ امام ابو یوسف کا جو قول ہے وہی امام صاحب کا آخری قول ہے۔

شروع رسم الطعی
مع
یعنی امام ابو یوسف کو قضاء کا تجربہ ہونے کی وجہ سے زیادہ علم حاصل ہوا تھا اور اسی زیادتی علم ( اور تجربہ ) کی وجہ سے امام ابو حنیفہ نے اپنے اس قول سے کہ صدقہ نفل حج سے افضل ہے۔ اس وقت رجوع فرما لیا جب آپ نے خود حج کیا اور حج کی مشقتیں علم میں آئیں۔ اور الاشباہ کی شرح میں علامہ بیری رحمہ اللہ نے یہ اضافہ کیا ہے کہ شہادتوں کے سلسلہ میں بھی فتوئی امام ابو یوسف کے قول پر ہے میں ( علامہ شامی ) کہتا ہوں کہ اس اضافہ کی ضرورت نہیں ہے کیونکہ شہادت قضاء کے متعلقات میں سے ہے۔
اور البحر الرائق ( ج ۷، ص۲۰۳) کتاب الدعوی میں ہے کہ اگر مدعی علیہ خاموشی اختیار کرے ( یعنی مدعی کے دعوئی کے بارے میں نہ اقرار کرے نہ انکار کرے) تو طرفین کے نزدیک اس کو منکر قرار دیا جائے گا اور مقدمہ کی کارروائی آگے بڑھائی جائے گی مگر امام ابی یوسف کے نزدیک اس کو جبس میں رکھا جائے گا تا آنکہ وہ کوئی جواب دے یہ یہ بات امام سرخی نے بیان فرمائی ہے اور فتویٰ ان امور میں جن کا تعلق قضاء سے ہے امام ابو یوسف کے قول پر ہے جیسا کہ قبیہ اور بزازیہ میں ہے اور اسی وجہ سے میں نے (علامہ ابن نجیم نے فتویٰ دیا ہے کہ اس کو جبس میں رکھا جائے تا آنکہ وہ کوئی جواب دے۔
Explanation of Rasm al-Mufti: In the case of only doing tayammum... That is, in worship, if a fatwa is given according to someone other than Imam Azam, the reason is that it is not just another Imam's opinion but also a transmission from Imam Sahib, so that fatwa is also considered on Imam Sahib's opinion. (2) In matters of qada, the opinion of Imam Abu Yusuf is the mufta bih. This is the second rule mentioned in al-Bahr al-Raiq (vol. 6, p. 282) just before Fasl al-Habs. The author of al-Bahr says: And in Qadiyya's Bab al-Mufti, it says that in matters pertaining to qada, fatwa is on the opinion of Imam Abu Yusuf because he had more experience in the field of qada. The same is in Fatawa Bazaziyya's Kitab al-Qada. ... Imam Zufar also transmitted this from Imam Abu Hanifa, as Imam Qadi Khan mentioned in his sharh. And in the transmission of Imam Abu Yusuf and Hasan b. Ziyad, there is impurity; rather, Imam Hasan transmits from Imam Sahib about heavy impurity, and Imam Abu Yusuf about light impurity, and each student took the opinion they transmitted. From the above detail, one can estimate that regarding used water, if fatwa is on Imam Muhammad's opinion, it is actually on Imam Azam's opinion because Imam Muhammad's opinion is a transmission from Imam Azam. Regarding nabidh al-tamr, there are three transmissions from Imam Azam. The first transmission, and it is his first opinion, is that wudu with it is necessary and doing tayammum with it is mustahab. The second transmission says combining wudu and tayammum is wajib, like the ruling of a donkey's saliva; Imam Muhammad took this opinion and preferred it in Nihayat al-Bayan. The third transmission is to only do tayammum and not wudu with nabidh; this is Imam Sahib's final opinion to which he returned, and it is sahih, and it is the opinion of Imam Abu Yusuf, Imam Shafi'i, Imam Malik, Imam Ahmad, and most scholars, and Imam Tahawi preferred it. From the above detail, it is known that in nabidh al-tamr, fatwa is on Imam Abu Yusuf's opinion, which is actually on Imam Azam's opinion because Imam Abu Yusuf's opinion is his final opinion. ... That is, due to his experience in qada, Imam Abu Yusuf acquired more knowledge, and due to this excess knowledge (and experience), Imam Abu Hanifa retracted his statement that nafl sadaqah is better than hajj when he himself performed hajj and learned its hardships. In Sharh al-Ashbah, Allama Biri added that in matters of testimony, fatwa is also on Imam Abu Yusuf's opinion. I (Allama Shami) say this addition is unnecessary because testimony is among the matters related to qada. In al-Bahr al-Raiq (vol. 7, p. 203), Kitab al-Da'wa, it says: If the defendant remains silent (i.e., neither admits nor denies the claim), according to the two (Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Muhammad) he is considered a denier and the case proceeds, but according to Imam Abu Yusuf, he will be placed in prison until he gives an answer. This was stated by Imam Sarkhasi. Fatwa in matters pertaining to qada is on Imam Abu Yusuf's opinion, as in Qadiyya and Bazaziyya, and for this reason I (Ibn Nujaym) gave fatwa that he be placed in prison until he answers.
Source pages p. 94

Commentary
This passage is a rasm al-mufti rule from a Hanafi usul al-iftaa work. It establishes the hierarchy of opinions in judicial matters. The author explains that in purely devotional matters (ibadat), fatwa is generally on the opinion of Imam Abu Hanifa. However, in matters of qada (judicial rulings), the mufta bih (relied-upon) opinion is that of Imam Abu Yusuf. The reasoning given is that Imam Abu Yusuf had extensive practical experience in the judiciary, which gave him superior insight into the practical implications of rulings. To support this, the author provides examples: first, using the case of used water (ma' musta'mal) where Imam Muhammad's opinion is sometimes followed, but that opinion is actually a transmission from Imam Abu Hanifa, so it is still within the Imam's framework. Second, the case of nabidh al-tamr (date infusion) is detailed: Imam Abu Hanifa had three successive opinions; the final one—that only tayammum is performed—is the one Imam Abu Yusuf adopted, so following Imam Abu Yusuf here means following Imam Abu Hanifa's final view. The author also notes that Imam Abu Hanifa himself retracted a prior ruling on the superiority of voluntary charity over hajj after gaining personal experience of hajj. Additionally, the author clarifies that matters of testimony are included under qada, so the rule applies there too. A practical example is given: a silent defendant is treated differently—according to the majority (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) he is a denier and the case proceeds, but according to Abu Yusuf he is imprisoned until he responds, and because the rule prefers Abu Yusuf in qada matters, the fatwa is to imprison him. The overall message is that the mufti must be aware of these hierarchies and that following a student can still mean following the Imam when the student's opinion is himself a transmission from the Imam.

Key Terms
قضاء (qada): Judicial matters, including litigation, testimony, and court proceedings.
مفتیٰ (mufta): The opinion upon which fatwa is given; the relied-upon position in a given category.
روایت (riwayah): A transmission of Imam Abu Hanifa's opinion by his students.
بحر الرائق (al-Bahr al-Raiq): A major Hanafi fiqh work by Zayn al-Din Ibn Nujaym, referenced in the passage as the source for the rule.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is fatwa given on Imam Abu Yusuf's opinion in matters of qada?
A) Because he was the most knowledgeable among the Hanafi scholars
B) Because he had extensive experience in judicial matters
C) Because Imam Abu Hanifa explicitly commanded it
D) Because he lived in a different era

Key Takeaway
In judicial matters, the mufta bih is Imam Abu Yusuf's opinion, grounded in his practical experience and often representing the final position of Imam Abu Hanifa.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa
beginner
6 min
The Mufta Bih in Dhawi al-Arham Inheritance
Establishes the rule for giving fatwa in inheritance of distant relatives according to Imam Muhammad

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the mufta bih opinion for dhawi al-arham inheritance and explain why Imam Muhammad's view is the well-known transmission (mashhur riwayah) from Imam Abu Hanifa.

Core Idea
In dhawi al-arham inheritance, the mufta bih is Imam Muhammad's opinion, which is the mashhur riwayah from Abu Hanifa.

In the Hanafi madhhab, the mufti must know which opinion to give fatwa on in each area of fiqh. This lesson presents a specific rasm al-mufti rule: the division of inheritance among distant relatives (dhawi al-arham) follows the opinion of Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani. This ruling is not an arbitrary preference but reflects the well-known transmission from Imam Abu Hanifa himself.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling as a Rasm al-Mufti Rule
Recognize that this passage is not a fiqh ruling about inheritance itself, but a meta-rule instructing the mufti which Hanafi opinion to rely on for fatwa.
Rasm al-mufti rules are procedural: they tell the mufti what to say, not directly what the law is.
2
Pinpoint the Subject: Dhawi al-Arham
Understand that dhawi al-arham are non-agnate relatives (e.g., maternal aunts, maternal cousins) who were controversial in inheritance law.
The Hanafi school had multiple views on whether they inherit at all.
3
State the Mufta Bih: Imam Muhammad's Opinion
The passage explicitly says 'biqawli Muhammad yufta' — fatwa is given on Imam Muhammad's opinion in all matters of dhawi al-arham inheritance.
This includes both the eligibility to inherit and the method of distribution.
4
Understand the Reasoning: It is the Mashhur Riwayah
The passage explains that Imam Muhammad's opinion is the well-known transmission (mashhur riwayah) from Imam Abu Hanifa, meaning it is the more reliably transmitted and practiced view.
In Hanafi usul, the mashhur riwayah is preferred for fatwa over other transmissions.
5
Note the Consensus Among Hanafi Authorities
The passage cites multiple sources (Muntaqa al-Bahr, Sakb al-Anhar, Sajawandi's commentary, al-Kafi) all confirming this rule, showing it is established and uncontested within the school.
This consistency reinforces the mufti's confidence in applying the rule.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۳) مسائل ذوی الارحام میں امام محمد کا قول مفتی یہ ہے:
تیسرا قاعدہ وہ ہے جو فقہ کے متن منتقی الا بحر ( ج ۲ ص ۳۵۱) میں اور اس کے علاوہ دیگر کتابوں میں اس مسئلہ کے ذیل میں ہے کہ ذوی الارحام پر تر کہ کس طرح تقسیم کیا جائے گا؟ سب حضرات فرماتے ہیں کہ وبقول محمد یفتی ( اور امام محمد کے قول پر فتوی دیا جائے گا ) اور علامہ علاء الدین علی بن محمد طرابلسی رحمہ اللہ ( ۱۵۰ فر۱۰۳ھ) نے منتقی الا بحر کی کتاب الفرائض کی شرح سکب الانہر میں فرمایا ہے کہ ذوی الارحام کو وارث بنانے کے تمام مسائل میں امام محمد کے قول پر فتوئی ہے اور ذوی الارحام کی توریث امام ابو حنیفہ کی دو روایتوں میں سے مشہور روایت ہے اور اسی پر فتوی دیا گیا ہے۔ شیخ سراج الدین محمد بن عبد الرشید سجاوندی رحمہ اللہ نے بھی اپنے فرائض کی شرح میں یہی فرمایا ہے اور کافی میں ہے کہ:
..
اور امام محمد کا قول امام ابو حنیفہ کی دو روایتوں میں سے مشہور روایت ہے، تمام
یہ مضمون سراجی ص ۴۴ میں ہے خود مصنف نے سراجی کی کوئی شرح نہیں لکھی
(3) In matters of dhawi al-arham, the opinion of Imam Muhammad is the mufta bih: This is the third rule found in the fiqh matn Muntaqa al-Bahr (vol. 2, p. 351) and other books under the issue of how to divide the estate among dhawi al-arham. All scholars say: 'Wa biqawli Muhammad yufta' (fatwa is given on Imam Muhammad's opinion). Allama Ala al-Din Ali b. Muhammad Trabulsi (d. 150/103?) said in his Sharh Sakb al-Anhar on Muntaqa al-Bahr's Kitab al-Faraid that in all matters of making dhawi al-arham heirs, fatwa is on Imam Muhammad's opinion, and making dhawi al-arham heirs is the well-known transmission of Imam Abu Hanifa from two transmissions, and fatwa has been given on it. Shaykh Siraj al-Din Muhammad b. Abd al-Rashid al-Sajawandi also said this in his commentary on faraid. In al-Kafi, it says: And Imam Muhammad's opinion is the well-known transmission among the two transmissions from Imam Abu Hanifa. All. This content is in Siraji, p. 44. The author did not write any commentary on Siraji.
Source pages p. 95

Commentary
This passage presents the third rasm al-mufti rule: in inheritance matters involving dhawi al-arham (non-agnate relatives, i.e., those related through females or other distant ties), the relied-upon opinion for fatwa is that of Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani. The rule is recorded in the matn Muntaqa al-Bahr and other works. The author notes that this rule applies to all questions of how to distribute inheritance among dhawi al-arham. He further explains that making dhawi al-arham eligible to inherit is itself a position attributed to Imam Abu Hanifa, and among two transmissions from him, the one allowing inheritance (adopted by Imam Muhammad) is the well-known and fatwa-worthy position. The author cites multiple authorities: Allama Alauddin al-Tarabusi in his commentary Sakb al-Anhar, Shaykh Siraj al-Din al-Sajawandi in his commentary on Faraid, and the book al-Kafi. The passage ends with a clarifying note that the actual author of the Siraji (a matn on faraid) did not write a commentary himself, but the reference is to the text. The key point is that in this specific area of fiqh (inheritance by distant relatives), the mufti should follow Imam Muhammad, not because he is superior in general, but because his opinion is the most consistent with the school's established practice and represents the well-known transmission from the founding Imam.

Key Terms
ذوی الارحام (dhawi al-arham): Distant relatives who are not agnate (asabah), such as maternal aunts, maternal cousins, etc.
مشہور روایت (mashhur riwayah): The well-known transmission from Imam Abu Hanifa; the position favored for fatwa.
مفتیٰ (mufta bih): The opinion upon which fatwa is based in a given category.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In inheritance matters for dhawi al-arham, which Hanafi scholar's opinion is given fatwa according to this passage?
A) Imam Abu Hanifa
B) Imam Abu Yusuf
C) Imam Muhammad
D) Imam Zufar

Key Takeaway
In dhawi al-arham inheritance, the mufti must follow Imam Muhammad's opinion because it is the well-known transmission from Imam Abu Hanifa and the established mufta bih.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa
intermediate

Fatwa on Dhawi al-Arham: Imam Muhammad's Saying is the Relied Position
Rasm al-mufti rule: mufta bih for dhawi al-arham

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the mufta bih position in dhawi al-arham inheritance and explain why Imam Muhammad's saying is preferred over the other riwaya of Abu Hanifa.

Core Idea
In dhawi al-arham cases, the mufta bih is Imam Muhammad's saying — the mashhur riwaya of Abu Hanifa.

This lesson presents a foundational rule in Hanafi mufti methodology: when dealing with inheritance of dhawi al-arham — kindred relatives who are neither Quranic heirs nor asaba — the position upon which fatwa is given is that of Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani. This is not a random choice; it is the well-known (mashhur) transmission from Imam Abu Hanifa himself. Understanding this rule helps you identify which authority to rely on when issuing fatwas in inheritance cases.

Guided Path
1
Identify the rule and its scope
Recognize that the rule applies specifically to dhawi al-arham inheritance, not to all inheritance cases.
Dhawi al-arham are those relatives not entitled as fard or asabah.
2
Recognize the mufta bih position
Note that Imam Muhammad's saying is the basis for fatwa, as stated in the sources: 'wa bi qawl Muhammad yufata'.
This is the operative ruling for fatwa.
3
Understand why Imam Muhammad's saying is preferred
It is the mashhur (well-known) riwaya from Imam Abu Hanifa, confirmed by later scholars like al-Tarabulsi, al-Sajawandi, and al-Kafi.
The other riwaya is less-known and not relied upon.
4
Apply the rule in practice
When a mufti encounters a dhawi al-arham case, they must use Imam Muhammad's method for ranking and distributing shares.
Ignoring this rule leads to an incorrect fatwa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۳) مسائل ذوی الارحام میں امام محمد کا قول مفتی یہ ہے:
تیسرا قاعدہ وہ ہے جو فقہ کے متن منتقی الا بحر ( ج ۲ ص ۳۵۱) میں اور اس کے علاوہ دیگر کتابوں میں اس مسئلہ کے ذیل میں ہے کہ ذوی الارحام پر تر کہ کس طرح تقسیم کیا جائے گا؟ سب حضرات فرماتے ہیں کہ وبقول محمد یفتی ( اور امام محمد کے قول پر فتوی دیا جائے گا ) اور علامہ علاء الدین علی بن محمد طرابلسی رحمہ اللہ ( ۱۵۰ فر۱۰۳ھ) نے منتقی الا بحر کی کتاب الفرائض کی شرح سکب الانہر میں فرمایا ہے کہ ذوی الارحام کو وارث بنانے کے تمام مسائل میں امام محمد کے قول پر فتوئی ہے اور ذوی الارحام کی توریث امام ابو حنیفہ کی دو روایتوں میں سے مشہور روایت ہے اور اسی پر فتوی دیا گیا ہے۔ شیخ سراج الدین محمد بن عبد الرشید سجاوندی رحمہ اللہ نے بھی اپنے فرائض کی شرح میں یہی فرمایا ہے اور کافی میں ہے کہ: اور امام محمد کا قول امام ابو حنیفہ کی دو روایتوں میں سے مشہور روایت ہے، تمام ذوی الارحام کے سلسلہ میں اور اسی پر فتوئی ہے۔
یہ مضمون سراجی ص ۴۴ میں ہے خود مصنف نے سراجی کی کوئی شرح نہیں لکھی ۱۲
(3) Issues of dhawi al-arham: The saying of Imam Muhammad is the one on which fatwa is given. The third rule is what is found in the text of al-Muntaqa al-Abhur (vol. 2, p. 351) and other books under this issue: how will the inheritance be distributed among dhawi al-arham? All (scholars) state: wa bi qawl Muhammad yufata (and on Imam Muhammad's saying fatwa is given). And Allamah Ala al-Din Ali bin Muhammad al-Tarabulsi (d. 103? H) said in his commentary on the book of faraid of al-Muntaqa al-Abhur, Saka al-Anhur, that in all issues of making dhawi al-arham heirs, fatwa is on Imam Muhammad's saying. And the tawrith of dhawi al-arham is the mashhur riwaya from two riwayas of Imam Abu Hanifa, and fatwa is given upon it. Sheikh Siraj al-Din Muhammad bin Abd al-Rashid al-Sajawandi also said the same in his commentary on faraid, and in al-Kafi it states: And Imam Muhammad's saying is the mashhur riwaya from two riwayas of Imam Abu Hanifa, in all matters of dhawi al-arham, and on it fatwa is given. This content is in Siraji, p. 44; the author himself did not write any commentary of Siraji.
Source pages p. 95

Commentary
This passage presents the third rule of mufti methodology, specifically regarding the inheritance of dhawi al-arham (kindred relatives who are not primary heirs). The text establishes that in all such matters, the relied-upon position for fatwa is that of Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani. The commentators explain that this is the mashhur (well-known) riwaya from Imam Abu Hanifa, and thus it is the preferred view. The passage cites multiple authorities: al-Muntaqa al-Abhur, al-Tarabulsi, al-Sajawandi, and al-Kafi, all confirming that Imam Muhammad's saying is the basis for fatwa. The note at the end clarifies that the author of this sharh did not write a commentary on Siraji.

Key Terms
ذوی الارحام (dhawi al-arham): Those kindred relatives who are not primary heirs (ashab al-faraid) and are not asaba; they inherit in the absence of primary heirs according to certain rules.
قول مفتیٰ بہ (qawl mufta bih): The saying (of an imam) upon which fatwa is given; the relied-upon position in the madhhab.
روایت مشہور (riwaya mashhur): The well-known transmission from the imam, distinguished from a rare or less-known riwaya.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) Imam al-Shafi'i

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fatwa methodology, for dhawi al-arham inheritance, the mufta bih is Imam Muhammad's saying as the mashhur riwaya of Abu Hanifa.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa
intermediate
8 min
The Fourth Rule of Fatwa: Istihsan Precedes Qiyas (With Exceptions)
Establishes the rule that istihsan takes precedence over qiyas, with exceptions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the fiqh maxim that istihsan takes precedence over qiyas, identify its exceptions, and apply the correct meaning of tarjih in fatwa practice.

Core Idea
Istihsan is given precedence over qiyas, but with known exceptions — a mufti must know both the rule and its limits.

The passage presents the fourth rule of fatwa-giving, a foundational principle in the Hanafi school: when qiyas and istihsan conflict, istihsan is preferred. The author notes that there are exceptions, and also touches on a subtle difference in how 'precedence' (tarjih) is understood. This lesson unpacks the rule, its exceptions, and the scholarly discussion on the meaning of tarjih.

Guided Path
1
State the maxim
Clearly articulate the rule: Istihsan is given precedence over qiyas when both are present in a case.
This is a general rule (qa'ida kulliya) applied across fiqh chapters.
2
Identify the scope
Understand that the rule applies to all matters where qiyas and istihsan conflict, not limited to specific chapters.
It is a universal guide for the mufti's reasoning.
3
List the exceptions
Acknowledge that there are specific cases (11 or 22, as mentioned) where qiyas overrides istihsan. These must be known by the mufti.
Exceptions are listed in works like Natafi's Ajnas and Ibn Najim's commentary.
4
Analyze the meaning of tarjih
Distinguish the majority view that tarjih means exclusive preference (only istihsan is acted upon) from Bazdawi's view that it means mere preference (qiyas remains permissible).
This affects the mufti's flexibility in applying the rule.
5
Apply the rule in fatwa
When issuing a fatwa, check if the case falls under the general rule or an exception, and be aware of the school's adopted interpretation of tarjih.
The operative (mufta bihi) position follows the majority view.

Source Text

چوتھا قاعدہ وہ ہے جو اکثر کتابوں میں مذکور ہے کہ جب کسی مسئلہ میں قیاس اور استحسان جمع ہوں تو استحسان کو قیاس پر ترجیح دی جائے گی البتہ چند مسائل مستقیٰ ہیں اور وہ گیارہ ہیں جیسا کہ ناطفی کی اجناس میں ہے اور ان کو علامہ ابن نجیم نے بھی منار کی شرح میں ذکر کیا ہے۔ پھر ذکر کیا ہے کہ نجم الدین نسفی نے ان کی تعداد بائیس تک پہنچائی ہے اور ابن نجیم نے اس سے پہلے تلویح کے حوالہ سے ذکر کیا ہے کہ رجحان کا صحیح مطلب یہاں راج (استحسان) کے مطابق عمل کا متعین ہونا اور مرجوح (قیاس) پر عمل نہ کرنا ہے۔ اور فخر الاسلام بزدوی رحمہ اللہ کے کلام سے بظاہر یہ معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ رجحان کے معنی اولیت کے ہیں یہاں تک کہ مرجوح (قیاس) پر بھی عمل جائز ہوگا۔
The fourth rule is what is mentioned in most books: When qiyas and istihsan are combined in a matter, precedence will be given to istihsan over qiyas. However, a few matters are excepted, and they are eleven, as in Natafi's Ajnas, and Allamah Ibn Najim also mentioned them in his commentary on al-Manar. Then he mentioned that Najm al-Din al-Nasafi increased their number to twenty-two. And Ibn Najim earlier, quoting al-Talwih, mentioned that the correct meaning of tarjih here is that action is determined according to the preponderant (istihsan) and not acting on the preponderated (qiyas). And from the statement of Fakhr al-Islam al-Bazdawi, may Allah have mercy on him, it outwardly appears that tarjih means preference, such that acting on the preponderated (qiyas) would also be permissible.
Source pages p. 96

Commentary
This passage presents the fourth rule of fatwa-giving, which is a foundational principle in the Hanafi school: when there is a conflict between qiyas (analogical reasoning) and istihsan (juristic preference), istihsan takes precedence. The author clarifies that this rule has exceptions; there are specific cases where qiyas is followed instead. The text then discusses a scholarly difference regarding the meaning of tarjih (preponderance): according to some, it means that only the preponderant view is valid for action, while according to Fakhr al-Islam al-Bazdawi, it may mean that the preponderated view is also permissible but less preferred. The rule is essential for muftis to understand how to weigh conflicting evidence.

Key Terms
رجحان (tarjih): The process of giving precedence to one evidence over another; here it means that action is determined according to the preponderant (istihsan)
استحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference; a method of reasoning that departs from strict analogy (qiyas) in favor of a more equitable outcome.
قیاس (qiyas): Analogical reasoning; deriving a ruling for a new case based on an original case with a shared effective cause (illa).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the fourth rule, what happens when qiyas and istihsan conflict in a matter?
A) Qiyas is always given precedence.
B) Istihsan is given precedence, but there are exceptions.
C) Both are equally valid and the mufti may choose.
D) The earlier ruling is followed regardless.

Key Takeaway
The fourth rule is that istihsan is given precedence over qiyas, but with specific exceptions; a mufti must know both the rule and the exceptions to issue correct fatwas.

The Obligation to Base Fatwa on Zahir al-Riwayah
Rule stating the obligation to base fatwa on Zahir al-Riwayah with exceptions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the fifth rule of rasm al-mufti to determine whether a given narration qualifies as the basis for fatwa, and identify the two exceptions to the rule.

Core Idea
Fatwa must be on Zahir al-Riwayah; rare narrations are valid only if jurists explicitly endorse them.

This lesson establishes a foundational principle of Hanafi fatwa practice: the mufti and judge are bound by the well-known narrated positions (Zahir al-Riwayah) of the school. The rule protects the integrity of the madhhab by excluding retracted or rare statements, except when later jurists make an explicit exception. Understanding this hierarchy is essential for issuing sound fatwa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the primary source for fatwa
Recognise that Zahir al-Riwayah — the six core books of Imam Muhammad — is the default authority for all fatwa and judicial decisions in the Hanafi school.
The rule cites al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, Book of Qada.
2
Understand the consequence of being outside Zahir al-Riwayah
Statements that fall outside Zahir al-Riwayah are considered marju‘ ‘anhu (retracted) and lose their authority. A muqallid cannot act upon them.
3
Recognise the default prohibition of rare narrations
A judge (qadi) may only decide according to Zahir al-Riwayah. A rare narration (riwayah shadhdhah) cannot be used unless explicitly authorised.
4
Identify the two exceptions
First, if later jurists explicitly state that the fatwa is upon a rare narration, it becomes operative. Second, if a matter is not mentioned in Zahir al-Riwayah at all, then other narrations may be consulted.
Both exceptions are grounded in necessity and the practice of later scholars.
5
Apply the rule to a scenario
Given a scenario, determine which narration the mufti must follow, and check whether any exception applies.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
پانچواں قاعدہ وہ ہے جو البحر الرائق کی کتاب القضاء ( ج۶ ص۲۷۰) میں ہے کہ جو اقوال ظاہر روایت سے خارج ہیں وہ مرجوع عنہ ہیں اور مرجوع عنہ قول مجتہد کا قول باقی نہیں رہتا علماء نے ایسا ہی ذکر کیا ہے۔ اور ہم پہلے انفع الوسائل کے حوالہ سے بیان کر آئے ہیں کہ مقلد قاضی ظاہر روایت کے مطابق ہی فیصلہ کر سکتا ہے۔ روایت شاذہ کے مطابق فیصلہ نہیں کر سکتا۔ الا یہ کہ فقہاء تصریح کریں کہ فتویٰ روایت شاذہ پر ہے۔ اور البحر کے باب قضاء الفوائت ( ج ۲ ص ۸۲) میں ہے کہ جب کوئی مسئلہ ظاہر روایت میں مذکور نہ ہو اور دوسری روایت میں ثابت ہو تو اس کی طرف رجوع کرنا متعین.
The fifth rule is what is in al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, Book of Qada (vol. 6, p. 270): the statements that are outside Zahir al-Riwayah are those from which the mujtahid has retracted, and the retracted statement of the mujtahid no longer remains. The scholars have mentioned this. And we have earlier stated with reference to Anfa' al-Wasa'il that a muqallid judge can only decide according to Zahir al-Riwayah. He cannot decide according to a rare narration (riwayah shadhdhah), unless the jurists explicitly state that the fatwa is upon the rare narration. And in al-Bahr, chapter of Qada' al-Fawa'it (vol. 2, p. 82), it is stated: when a matter is not mentioned in Zahir al-Riwayah but is established in another narration, then referring to that is necessary.
Source pages p. 96

Commentary
This passage lays down the fifth rule: the mufti and judge must base their fatwa and judgment on the well-known narrations (Zahir al-Riwayah) of the Hanafi school. The rule has two aspects: first, statements outside Zahir al-Riwayah are considered retracted and not valid for action; second, if a matter is not found in Zahir al-Riwayah, then other narrations may be used. An exception is made if the later jurists explicitly state that the fatwa is on a rare narration. This rule clarifies the hierarchy of narrations in the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
ظاہر روایت (Zahir al-Riwayah): The well-known and authoritative narrations from the Hanafi imams, forming the core of the madhhab

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the fifth rule, when may a judge use a rare narration (riwayah shadhdhah) for a verdict?
A) Never; only Zahir al-Riwayah is allowed.
B) When the rare narration is stronger in evidence.
C) Only if the jurists explicitly state that the fatwa is on that rare narration.
D) When it is the only available narration.

Key Takeaway
The mufti's default source is Zahir al-Riwayah; rare narrations are only usable when explicitly endorsed or when the core is silent.

Sixth Rule: Drayah (Evidence) When Narrations Differ
When narrations conflict, the evidence (drayah) is considered for choosing the stronger view.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the rule of preferring narrations based on drayah (evidence) when conflicting Hanafi riwayat exist, and identify the stronger narration by examining the underlying evidence.

Core Idea
When Hanafi narrations conflict, the mufti must prefer the one backed by stronger evidence (drayah), not mere transmission frequency.

This lesson introduces a vital principle for muftis: when we have conflicting reports from Imam Abu Hanifa on the same issue, we cannot simply count narrations. Instead, we must weigh the underlying evidence (drayah) to determine which narration is stronger. The source passage explains this rule using the example of tuma'ninah in prayer and clarifies that 'drayah' means 'dalil' (evidence), synonymous with 'hujja'.

Guided Path
1
Identify the rule and its scope
The rule states that when narrations from Imam Abu Hanifa differ, consideration is given to drayah (evidence). Its scope covers any matter where multiple riwayat exist on the same ruling.
2
Understand the key term 'drayah'
Drayah here means evidence (dalil), not mere rational opinion. It is synonymous with 'hujja' as shown in al-Hawi al-Qudsi.
This is a technical usage specific to Hanafi rasm al-mufti.
3
Examine the example given
Tuma'ninah in qiyam and jalsah: narrations differ whether it is sunnah or wajib. The drayah (evidence) indicates obligation, so the narration that says wajib is preferred.
The evidence likely comes from the Prophet's (s) practice and the principle that actions in prayer are wajib unless proven otherwise.
4
Apply the rule to a new scenario
Consider another matter with conflicting narrations. Identify the key evidence for each position and prefer the narration that is consistent with stronger evidence.
For example, the issue of tasmiyah aloud in prayer.
5
Note the relationship to other qawaid
This rule is a sub-maxim (sughra) and parallels the maxim 'al-dirayah muqaddamah ala al-riwayah' (evidence is given precedence over transmission).
It is part of a larger set of rules for a mufti in cases of ikhtilaf.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۲) اختلاف روایات کے وقت درایت (دلیل) کا لحاظ چھٹا قاعدہ وہ ہے جو سدید الدین کا شعری رحمہ اللہ کی منیۃ المصلی کی شرح کبیری (ص ۲۹۵) [؟] نہیں تعدیل ارکان کی بحث میں ذکر کیا گیا ہے۔ شارح نے طمانیت قومہ اور جلسہ کے بارے میں امام اعظم کی مختلف روایتیں ذکر کرنے کے بعد کہ وہ سنت ہیں یا واجب فرمایا ہے کہ: اور آپ جان چکے ہیں کہ دلیل کا مقتضی وجوب ہے شیخ کمال الدین ابن الہمام نے ایسا ہی فرمایا ہے اور جب درایت کے موافق روایت بھی ہو تو اس سے عدول مناسب نہیں ہے۔" اور لفظ درایت ( بے نقطہ دال سے ) بمعنی دلیل استعمال کیا جاتا ہے جیسا کہ حافظ الد نسفی کی المستصفی میں ہے اور اس کی تائید اس عبارت سے بھی ہوتی ہے جو الحاوی القدی کے آخر میں ہے کہ جب کسی مسئلہ میں امام ابو حنیفہ سے روایتیں مختلف ہوں تو ان میں سے جو دلیل کے اعتبار سے قوی ہو اس کو لینا بہتر ہے ( اس عبارت میں درایت کی جگہ حجت استعمال کیا گیا ہے معلوم ہوا دونوں ایک ہیں )
(2) Consideration of drayah (evidence) when narrations differ: the sixth rule is what is mentioned in Sadid al-Din al-Sha'ari's commentary al-Kabir on Munyat al-Musalli (p. 295) [؟] not in the discussion of ta'dil al-arkan. The commentator, after mentioning the different narrations from Imam A'zam regarding tuma'ninah in qiyam and jalsah, that they are sunnah or wajib, said: 'And you already know that the requirement of the evidence is obligation. Sheikh Kamal al-Din Ibn al-Humam said likewise. And when the narration also agrees with the drayah, then deviating from it is not appropriate.' And the word drayah (with unpointed dal) is used in the meaning of evidence, as in al-Mustasfa of Hafiz al-Din al-Nasafi. And this is supported by the statement at the end of al-Hawi al-Qudsi: 'When narrations from Imam Abu Hanifa differ on a matter, then whichever is stronger in terms of evidence, it is better to adopt it' (in that statement, instead of drayah, 'hujja' is used; so it is clear that both are the same).
Source pages p. 96

Commentary
This passage presents the sixth rule: when there are conflicting narrations from Imam Abu Hanifa, the mufti must consider the underlying evidence (drayah) to determine which narration is stronger. The text gives a specific example: regarding tuma'ninah (tranquility) in standing and sitting during prayer, there were different narrations about whether it is sunnah or wajib. The commentator relies on the evidence that the obligation is indicated, preferring the narration that aligns with that. The term 'drayah' is explained to mean 'dalil' (evidence), and it is synonymous with 'hujja'. This rule ensures that the mufti does not blindly follow conflicting narrations but applies reason and evidence to choose the correct one.

Key Terms
درایت (drayah): Evidence (dalil) used to prefer one narration over another when narrations conflict.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) Follow the earliest narration.
D) Avoid giving a fatwa until consensus is reached.

Key Takeaway
When Hanafi narrations conflict, the narration supported by stronger evidence (drayah) must be preferred.

Seventh Rule: Caution in Kufr Fatwa
Mandates extreme caution before issuing a fatwa of kufr against a Muslim.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle of caution in takfir to a given scenario and determine when a fatwa of kufr should be withheld.

Core Idea
Never issue a fatwa of kufr if any possibility, even a weak narration, can preserve the Muslim's iman.

This lesson introduces the seventh rule from the Hanafi tradition on takfir. The source passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq and Ibn Najim establishes that a mufti must exhaust all means to avoid declaring a Muslim a disbeliever. Even a weak narration that negates kufr is sufficient to withhold takfir. This reflects the Hanafi school's emphasis on preserving the benefit of the doubt for Muslims.

Guided Path
1
Identify the rule
Read the rule: caution is necessary in issuing a fatwa of kufr. Recognize that takfir is an extremely grave matter.
2
Recognize the threshold
Note that the threshold for avoiding takfir is low: any narration that negates kufr, even if weak, prevents the fatwa. Even the possibility of a good interpretation (ta'wil) suffices.
This is more lenient than requiring strong evidence.
3
Recall the scholarly support
The rule is attributed to Sadr al-Shahid Ibn Maza and endorsed by Ibn Najim. Both emphasize extreme caution.
Ibn Najim explicitly includes weak narrations.
4
Apply the rule
In practice, when a mufti encounters a statement that may be kufr, he must actively search for any interpretation or reported opinion that negates kufr. If found, he withholds the fatwa of kufr.
This applies even if the majority of evidence points to kufr.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ساتواں قاعدہ وہ ہے جو البحر الرائق ( ج ۵ ص ۱۲۴) باب المرتد میں صدر شہید ابن مازه کے فتاویٰ صغریٰ سے منقول ہے کہ: کفر نہایت سنگین بات ہے اس لیے میں کسی مومن کو کافر نہیں قرار دیتا جب مجھے کوئی ایسی روایت مل جاتی ہے جس سے اس کے کفر کی نفی ہوتی ہو۔" پھر ابن نجیم نے ( ج ۵ ص ۱۲۵ میں ) فرمایا ہے: اور وہ بات جو مصلح ہو چکی ہے وہ یہ ہے کہ کسی ایسے مسلمان کی تکفیر کا فتویٰ نہیں دیا جائے گا جس کے کلام کو اچھے محل پر محمول کیا جا سکتا ہو یا جس کلام کے کفر ہونے میں روایتیں مختلف ہوں، اگر چہ اختلاف پیدا کرنے والی روایت ضعیف ہو۔
The seventh rule is what is quoted from the Fatawa al-Sughra of Sadr al-Shahid Ibn Maza in al-Bahr al-Ra'iq (vol. 5, p. 124), chapter of the apostate: 'Kufr is an extremely grave matter. Therefore, I do not declare a believer to be a disbeliever as long as I find any narration that negates his kufr.' Then Ibn Najim said (vol. 5, p. 125): 'What has been agreed upon is that a fatwa of takfir will not be given for a Muslim whose speech can be interpreted in a good light, or concerning whose speech there are conflicting narrations regarding whether it constitutes kufr, even if the narration causing the doubt is weak.'
Source pages p. 97

Commentary
This passage presents the seventh rule, which is a principle of extreme caution in matters of takfir (declaring someone a disbeliever). The mufti must exhaust all possibilities to avoid issuing a fatwa of kufr. The rule cites Sadr al-Shahid: he will not declare a believer a kafir if any narration exists that negates his kufr. Ibn Najim adds that even if there is a weak narration that suggests the speech might not be kufr, or if the speech can be interpreted favorably, takfir is avoided. This reflects the Hanafi school's general reluctance to takfir.

Key Terms
کفر (kufr): Disbelief; the opposite of iman; a legal status with severe consequences.
تکفیر (takfir): The act of declaring someone a disbeliever.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) He should still issue a fatwa of kufr if the statement seems clear.
B) He should not declare the Muslim a kafir.
C) He should only rely on strong narrations.
D) He should refer the matter to a higher authority.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi rule mandates maximum caution in takfir: even a weak doubt preserves the Muslim's faith.

Eighth Rule: Retracted Opinion is Like Abrogated
Explaining the Hanafi rule on retracted opinions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the rule that a retracted opinion is like an abrogated ruling by determining when a mujtahid's earlier opinion becomes invalid for fatwa.

Core Idea
A mujtahid's retracted opinion loses all authority, like an abrogated ruling.

In the Hanafi tradition, a mujtahid may change his mind on a legal issue. This rule clarifies what happens to his earlier opinion: it ceases to be part of his madhhab and becomes akin to a mansukh (abrogated) ruling. A mufti must instead adopt the opinion to which the mujtahid retracted. This principle ensures that fatwas are based on the final, confirmed position of the mujtahid.

Guided Path
1
Identify the retracted opinion
Find the earlier statement of the mujtahid from which he later retracted. This is the 'marju' 'anhu'.
Retraction may be explicit or known through later works.
2
Determine the retracted-to opinion
Search for the final opinion to which the mujtahid retracted. This is the mu'tamad (reliable) position.
Often found in later commentaries or the mujtahid's own revised works.
3
Apply the rule: treat the first as mansukh
Understand that the retracted opinion is like an abrogated ruling: it has no legal force and cannot be used for fatwa.
This is analogous to naskh (abrogation) in usul al-fiqh.
4
Confirm the fatwa position
Issue fatwa based on the final, retracted-to opinion. The earlier opinion is abandoned.
In Hanafi fatwa, the mufta bihi is always the most recent position of the mujtahid.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
آٹھواں قاعدہ وہ ہے جو البحر الرائق میں ہے اور اس کو ہم قریب ہی (پانچویں قاعدہ میں بیان کر آئے ہیں کہ جس قول سے رجوع کر لیا گیا وہ مجتہد کا مذہب باقی نہیں رہا پس اس قول کو تلاش کرنا ضروری ہے جس کی طرف مجتہد نے رجوع کیا ہے اور اس پر عمل کیا جائے گا کیونکہ پہلا قول منسوخ حکم جیسا ہو گیا ہے اور بحر ہی میں شیخ سراج الدین ہندی رحمہ اللہ کی ہدایہ کی شرح التوشیح کے حوالہ سے لکھا ہے کہ: " جس قول سے مجتہد نے رجوع کر لیا ہے اس کو لینا جائز نہیں " اور التحریر کی شرح التقریر والتخمیر ( ج ۳ ص ۳۳۴) میں مذکور ہے کہ:
The eighth rule is what is in al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, and we have mentioned it just now (in the fifth rule): the statement from which retraction has been made does not remain the madhhab of the mujtahid. So it is necessary to search for the statement to which the mujtahid has retracted, and action will be taken according to it, because the first statement has become like an abrogated ruling. And in al-Bahr itself, quoting from al-Tawshih, a commentary on al-Hidayah by Sheikh Siraj al-Din al-Hindi, may Allah have mercy on him, it is written: 'The statement from which the mujtahid has retracted is not permissible to adopt.' And in al-Taqrir wa al-Tahbir, a commentary on al-Tahrir (vol. 3, p. 334), it is mentioned:
Source pages p. 97

Commentary
This passage presents the eighth rule: when a mujtahid retracts an earlier opinion, that opinion is no longer considered part of his madhhab and is akin to an abrogated (mansukh) ruling. The mufti must instead adopt the opinion to which the mujtahid retracted. The rule emphasizes that it is not permissible to follow a retracted opinion. This is closely related to the fifth rule about Zahir al-Riwayah, as retracted opinions are generally those outside the well-known narrations.

Key Terms
مرجوع عنہ (marju' 'anhu): The opinion from which the mujtahid has retracted; it becomes invalid for fatwa.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the eighth rule, what is the status of an opinion from which the mujtahid has retracted?
A) It remains valid but is less preferred.
B) It becomes like an abrogated ruling and cannot be followed.
C) It can still be used if it is based on strong evidence.
D) It is considered a separate madhhab.

Key Takeaway
A retracted opinion loses all legal effect and cannot be used for fatwa; only the final, unretracted opinion is authoritative.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa

8 min
The Seventh Principle of Fatwa: Caution in Takfir
Sets a rule requiring caution before declaring a Muslim a disbeliever

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that a fatwa of takfīr is not issued if the person's speech can be favorably interpreted or if narrations differ on its being kufr, even if the dissenting narration is weak.

Core Idea
A mufti must not declare a Muslim a disbeliever if any favorable interpretation or weak contrary narration exists.

Takfīr — declaring a Muslim to be a disbeliever — is among the gravest acts in Islamic law, carrying immense consequences in this world and the next. The Hanafi school, known for its caution, has established a clear principle: a mufti must exhaust every possible avenue to avoid takfīr. This lesson unpacks the seventh principle (qāʿidah) from the Hanafi tradition, as recorded in al-Bahr al-Rā'iq and the Fatāwā al-Ṣughrā of Ṣadr al-Shahīd. Understanding and applying this rule is essential for any mufti entrusted with the weighty responsibility of issuing fatwas on apostasy.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Rule and Its Source
Locate the rule in the passage: it is the seventh principle in the list, narrated from Ṣadr al-Shahīd in al-Bahr al-Rā'iq (chapter of apostasy). Recognize that the rule has two parts: the statement of Ṣadr al-Shahīd ("I do not declare any believer a disbeliever as long as I find any narration that negates his disbelief") and the refinement by Ibn Nujaym ("A fatwa of takfir shall not be given if the speech can be interpreted favorably, or if narrations differ, even if the conflicting narration is weak").
2
Understand the Two Conditions
The rule specifies two independent grounds to avoid takfīr: (1) if the person's speech can be given a good interpretation (tahmīl ʿalā maḥmal ḥasan), i.e., a possible non-kufr meaning; (2) if there are differing narrations (riwāyāt) within the madhhab about whether such a statement constitutes disbelief. Either condition suffices.
Condition (2) highlights the importance of internal madhhab disagreement. Even a weak narration (riwāyah ḍaʿīfah) that opposes takfīr is enough to prevent the fatwa.
3
Appreciate the Weight of the Rule
Note that the rule is a manifestation of the Hanafi commitment to preserving the status of a Muslim (al-aṣl baqāʾ mā kāna ʿalā mā kāna). It reflects the principle that doubt (shakk) in a matter as serious as takfīr must be resolved in favor of the accused. The mufti must actively seek out any possible interpretation or narration that avoids takfīr.
This is not a concession but an obligation: the mufti must search for such interpretations, not passively wait for them to be presented.
4
Apply the Rule to a Hypothetical Scenario
Consider a person who says, "I do not believe in any religion." At first glance, this appears to be kufr. However, examine whether the speech can be interpreted favorably: perhaps the person means they reject only religions they perceive as corrupted, or they are in a state of extreme anger. If any such interpretation is plausible, takfīr is avoided. Additionally, check whether there are any narrations from Hanafi imams about similar statements that did not lead to takfīr. Even a weak narration in this direction would block the fatwa.
In practice, the mufti should consult the madhhab's literature and consider all possible ta'wīl before issuing a ruling.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۷) کفر کے فتویٰ میں احتیاط لازم ہے۔ ساتواں قاعدہ وہ ہے جو البحر الرائق ( ج ۵ ص ۱۲۴) باب المرتد میں صدر شہید ابن مازه (۶۸) کے فتاوی صغریٰ سے منقول ہے کہ: کفر نہایت سنگین بات ہے اس لیے میں کسی مومن کو کا فرنہیں قرار دیتا جب مجھے کوئی ایسی روایت مل جاتی ہے جس سے اس کے کفر کی نفی ہوتی ہو۔" پھر ابن نجیم نے ( ج ۵ ص ۱۲۵ میں ) فرمایا ہے: اور وہ بات جو مصلح ہو چکی ہے وہ یہ ہے کہ کسی ایسے مسلمان کی تکفیر کا فتویٰ نہیں دیا جائے گا جس کے کلام کو اچھے محل پر محمول کیا جا سکتا ہو یا جس کلام کے کفر ہونے میں روایتیں مختلف ہوں، اگر چہ اختلاف پیدا کرنے والی روایت ضعیف ہو۔
(7) Caution in issuing a fatwa of disbelief is necessary. The seventh principle is that which is narrated from the Fatawa Sughra of Sadr al-Shahid Ibn Maza (68) in al-Bahr al-Ra'iq (vol. 5, p. 124), chapter of apostasy: 'Disbelief is an extremely grave matter, therefore I do not declare any believer a disbeliever as long as I find any narration that negates his disbelief.' Then Ibn Nujaym said (vol. 5, p. 125): 'And the matter that has been rectified is that a fatwa of takfir shall not be given for a Muslim whose speech can be interpreted in a good manner, or regarding whose speech there are differing narrations concerning its being disbelief, even if the narration causing the difference is weak.'
Source pages p. 97

Commentary
This passage presents the seventh rule (qāʿidah) of iftā' from the Hanafi tradition, emphasizing extreme caution in takfīr. The rule is drawn from al-Bahr al-Rā'iq and the Fatāwā al-Ṣughrā of Ṣadr al-Shahīd. The core principle: a mufti must not rush to declare a Muslim a disbeliever. Even if a statement appears to be kufr, the mufti must seek any possible interpretation (ta'wīl) that preserves the person's Islam. If there exists even a weak narration that suggests the statement is not kufr, that narration is to be given weight. Ibn Nujaym reinforces this: takfīr is avoided if the speech can be given a good interpretation, or if the narrations about its kufr are conflicting. This reflects the Hanafi commitment to preserving the status of a Muslim and the gravity of removing someone from the fold of Islam.

Key Terms
تکفیر (takfīr): Declaring a Muslim to be a disbeliever (kāfir).
روایت (riwāyah): A transmitted report or narration from a mujtahid Imam regarding a ruling.
فتویٰ (fatwā): A non-binding legal opinion issued by a mufti.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the seventh rule (qāʿidah) from al-Bahr al-Rā'iq, when should a mufti avoid issuing a fatwa of takfīr?
A) Only if there is a clear proof of the person's Islam.
B) Only if the person recants his statement.
C) If there exists any narration that negates the disbelief, even if weak.
D) Only if the majority of scholars say the statement is not kufr.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi rule mandates that a mufti must not issue takfīr if any favorable interpretation or any contradictory narration—even weak—exists, preserving the person's status as a Muslim.
