8 min
Retracted Ruling of a Mujtahid is Not Followed
Rule on mujtahid's retracted ruling

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the rule that a mujtahid's retracted ruling is like an abrogated ruling, and determine which ruling is the mufta bihi based on whether the later ruling is known.

Core Idea
A mujtahid's later ruling abrogates his earlier; the mufti must follow the later.

This lesson introduces the eighth qāʿidah in Rasm al-Mufti: when a mujtahid retracts an earlier ruling, it becomes like an abrogated ruling (mansūkh) and cannot be used for fatwa. The mufti must identify the later ruling and act upon it. However, if the later ruling is unknown, both rulings are transmitted without deciding, indicating that the later ruling is not confirmed.

Guided Path
1
Identify the rule and its source
The passage states the eighth qāʿidah from al-Bahr al-Rā'iq: the retracted statement of a mujtahid becomes like an abrogated ruling.
This rule is part of the mufti's methodology (rasm al-mufti).
2
Understand the consequence of retraction
Once a mujtahid retracts, the earlier ruling is no longer his madhhab. The mufti must search for and follow the later ruling.
Retraction (rujūʿ) is a deliberate change of opinion.
3
Apply the condition about knowledge of the later ruling
If the later ruling is known, it is the madhhab and the earlier is abrogated. If not known, both rulings are transmitted without choosing.
This nuance comes from al-Taqrīr wa al-Takhmīr.
4
Practice with a real example
Consider Imam Abu Hanifa's two rulings on wudu by touch. His later ruling (no wudu required) is the madhhab; the earlier is abrogated.
The mufti must know the chronological order.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۸) مرجوع عند قول منسوخ قول ہے: آٹھواں قاعدہ وہ ہے جو البحر الرائق میں ہے اور اس کو ہم قریب ہی (پانچویں قاعدہ میں بیان کر آئے ہیں کہ جس قول سے رجوع کر لیا گیا وہ مجتہد کا مذہب باقی نہیں رہا پس اس . قول کو تلاش کرنا ضروری ہے جس کی طرف مجتہد نے رجوع کیا ہے اور اس پر عمل کیا جائے گا کیونکہ پہلا قول منسوخ حکم جیسا ہو گیا ہے اور بحر ہی میں شیخ سراج الدین ہندی رحمہ اللہ (۹۷) کی ہدایہ کی شرح التوشیح کے حوالہ سے لکھا ہے کہ: " جس قول سے مجتہد نے رجوع کر لیا ہے اس کو لینا جائز نہیں اور التحریر کی شرح التقریر والتخمیر ( ج ۳ ص ۳۳۴) میں مذکور ہے کہ: اگر بعد کا قول معلوم ہو تو وہ مجتہد کا مذہب ہوگا اور پہلا قول منسوخ ہو گا ورنہ مجتہد کے دونوں قول ان میں سے کسی کے بارے میں رجوع کا فیصلہ کیے بغیر نقل کیے جائیں گے۔"
(8) A retracted statement is an abrogated statement. The eighth principle is that which is in al-Bahr al-Rā'iq, and we have just explained it (in the fifth principle) that a statement from which one has retracted is no longer the madhhab of the mujtahid. Therefore, it is necessary to search for the statement to which the mujtahid has retracted and to act upon it, because the first statement has become like an abrogated ruling. And in al-Bahr itself, quoting from Shaykh Sirāj al-Dīn al-Hindī's (97) commentary on al-Hidāyah, al-Tawshīh, it is written: 'It is not permissible to adopt a statement from which the mujtahid has retracted.' And in al-Taqrīr wa al-Takhmīr, the commentary on al-Tahrīr (vol. 3, p. 334), it is mentioned: 'If the later statement is known, then that is the madhhab of the mujtahid, and the first statement becomes abrogated; otherwise, both statements of the mujtahid will be transmitted without deciding regarding which of them he retracted.'
Source pages p. 98

Commentary
This eighth rule (qāʿidah) addresses the situation where a mujtahid (here specifically an Imam of the madhhab) has two rulings on the same issue, one earlier and one later, and he has retracted (rajūʿ) from the earlier one. The rule states: once a mujtahid retracts, the earlier ruling ceases to be part of his madhhab; it is like an abrogated (mansūkh) ruling. The mufti must identify the later ruling and give fatwa accordingly. Shaykh Sirāj al-Dīn al-Hindī explicitly forbids using the retracted ruling. Furthermore, the commentary on al-Tahrīr adds a condition: if the later ruling is known, it is the madhhab; if not, both rulings are transmitted without deciding, indicating that the later ruling is not confirmed. This rule is crucial for muftis who must navigate the chronological development of a mujtahid's positions.

Key Terms
مرجوع (marjūʿ): A statement from which the mujtahid has retracted, i.e., he later adopted a different ruling.
منسوخ (mansūkh): Abrogated; here used analogically for a mujtahid's retracted ruling, which is abrogated by his later ruling.
مجتہد (mujtahid): A jurist qualified to derive rulings directly from the sources; here specifically referring to the founding Imams of the madhhab (e.g., Abu Hanifa).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When a mujtahid retracts an earlier ruling and adopts a later one, what is the status of the earlier ruling according to the eighth qāʿidah?
A) It remains part of the madhhab but is weaker.
B) It is like an abrogated ruling and is no longer followed.
C) It can still be used if no other ruling exists.
D) It is considered an error and discarded entirely.

Key Takeaway
When a mujtahid's later ruling is known, it is the madhhab; the earlier is abrogated and not to be followed.

Priority of Explicit Correction Over Mutūn
Principles for weighing rulings in fatwa

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the rule that explicit correction (taṣḥīḥ ṣarīḥ) overrides the implicit correction (taṣḥīḥ iltizāmī) of the mutūn when determining the muftā bihī position in the Hanafi madhhab.

Core Idea
Explicit correction overrides the implicit authority of the mutūn.

In the Hanafi madhhab, the mutūn (standard authoritative texts) carry great weight because their authors committed to including only correct rulings. However, this commitment creates only an implicit correction – not an absolute guarantee. Later scholars may explicitly correct a ruling found in the mutūn, and when they do, that explicit correction takes precedence. This lesson unpacks this ninth qā‘idah from Rasm al-Muftī and illustrates it with the case of a blind person’s testimony.

Guided Path
1
Understand the two types of taṣḥīḥ
Distinguish between implicit correction (taṣḥīḥ iltizāmī) – inferred from a ruling’s inclusion in the mutūn – and explicit correction (taṣḥīḥ ṣarīḥ) – a later scholar’s definitive statement that a particular ruling is the correct one.
Implicit correction is based on the author’s commitment; explicit correction is a deliberate, later declaration.
2
Grasp the hierarchy
Recognise that the qā‘idah establishes: explicit correction > implicit correction. A ruling outside the mutūn, once explicitly corrected, trumps the ruling found in the mutūn.
The opposite rule (mutūn always prevail) is a common misconception.
3
Apply the rule to a concrete fur‘
Consider the example from the source: the mutūn rule that a blind person’s testimony is invalid. If later scholars explicitly correct this to say it is valid, the explicit correction becomes the muftā bihī position.
The fur‘ here is from Kitāb al-Shahādāt.
4
Identify the underlying rationale
Allāmah Ibn ‘Ābidīn explains that the mutūn authors committed to correct rulings, but that commitment is not infallible. Explicit taṣḥīḥ supersedes because it is a direct, purposeful correction.
This reasoning (ta‘līl) is essential for applying the qā‘idah in new cases.
5
Integrate into fatwa practice
When a muftī encounters a ruling in the mutūn and a later explicit correction, he must weigh the authority. The rule tells him to prefer the explicitly corrected ruling after verification.
This is a key principle in Rasm al-Muftī for resolving conflicts within the madhhab.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(1) کسی قول کا متون میں ہوتا اس کی نعمتی تصیح ہے نواں قاعدہ وہ ہے جو علامہ قاسم رحمہ اللہ نے اپنی کتاب صحیح القدوری میں ذکر کیا ہے کہ جو اقوال متون میں میں وہ التزامی طور پر تی شدہ ہیں اور صریح نصیح التزامی تصیح پر مقدم ہے۔ میں ( علامہ شامی) کہتا ہوں کہ علامہ قاسم رحمہ اللہ کے قول کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ متون کے مصنفین نے اپنی کتابوں میں صحیح اقوال کو لینے کا التزام کیا ہے لہذا جو اقوال متون سے باہر ہیں جب تک ان کی صراحی تصیح نہ کی جائے وہ صحیح کے مقابل ہوں گے اور صریح تصحیح کے بعد ان کو متون کے اقوال پر مقدم کیا جائے گا کیونکہ جب ان کی صراحی تصحیح کی گئی تو اب وہ التزامی تصیح پر مقدم ہوں گے۔ ہے کہ: اور فتاوی خیریہ کی کتاب الشہادات ( ج ۲ ص ۳۳) میں ایک سوال کے جواب میں صحیح مفتی بہ مذہب جس کو متون والوں نے لیا ہے۔ جو مذہب کی صحیح روایات یعنی ظاہر روایت کو نقل کرنے کے لیے تصنیف کئے گئے ہیں۔ یہ ہے کہ اندھے کی گواہی درست نہیں ہے ۔
(1) A statement being in the mutūn is its implicit (iltizāmī) correction. The ninth principle is that which Allāmah Qāsim (may Allah have mercy on him) mentioned in his book Ṣaḥīḥ al-Qudūrī: 'Statements that are in the mutūn are implicitly (iltizāmī) corrected, and explicit (ṣarīḥ) correction takes precedence over implicit correction.' I (Allāmah Shāmī) say that the gist of Allāmah Qāsim's statement is that the authors of the mutūn have committed themselves to including only correct statements in their books. Therefore, statements that are outside the mutūn are considered not correct unless they are explicitly corrected; and after explicit correction, they are given precedence over the statements of the mutūn, because when they are explicitly corrected, they take precedence over implicit correction. And in Fatāwā al-Khayriyyah, the chapter on testimonies (vol. 2, p. 33), in answer to a question: 'The correct muftā bihī madhhab is that which the authors of the mutūn have adopted, since they compiled [the mutūn] to transmit the correct narrations of the madhhab, i.e., ẓāhir al-riwāyah. That is: the testimony of a blind person is not valid.'
Source pages p. 98

Commentary
This ninth rule (qāʿidah) clarifies the relative authority of rulings found in the standard works (mutūn) versus rulings found elsewhere. Allāmah Qāsim (the author of Ṣaḥīḥ al-Qudūrī) states that rulings included in the mutūn are implicitly considered correct because the authors committed to including only correct positions. However, if a ruling outside the mutūn is explicitly declared correct (taṣḥīḥ ṣarīḥ) by later scholars, that explicit correction trumps the implicit correctness of the mutūn. Allāmah Ibn ʿĀbidīn (Shāmī) explains the rationale. An example from Fatāwā al-Khayriyyah: the correct madhhab according to the mutūn is that the testimony of a blind person is invalid. This illustrates that the mutūn's implicit correction is authoritative but can be overridden by explicit taṣḥīḥ.

Key Terms
متون (mutūn): The standard authoritative texts of the Hanafi madhhab, such as al-Qudūrī, al-Mukhtār, al-Kanz, etc.
تصحیح (taṣḥīḥ): Correction; indicating a particular ruling as the correct one within the madhhab.
التزامی (iltizāmī): Implicit; here meaning that the correctness of a ruling is implied by its inclusion in the mutūn, due to the author's commitment to include only correct positions.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When does an explicitly corrected ruling outside the mutūn take precedence over a ruling found in the mutūn?
A) Always, because explicit correction is more reliable.
B) Only if the ruling in the mutūn is weak.
C) After the explicit correction, because it overrides the implicit correction of the mutūn.
D) Never; mutūn are always authoritative.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fatwa methodology, explicit correction (taṣḥīḥ ṣarīḥ) overrides the implicit correction (taṣḥīḥ iltizāmī) of the mutūn.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa

6 min
Hierarchy of Hanafi Legal Sources: Mutun, Shuruh, Fatawa
Establishes precedence hierarchy for Hanafi legal texts

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the hierarchy of Hanafi legal texts (mutun, shuruh, fatawa) to resolve conflicts between sources when issuing a fatwa.

Core Idea
Mutun prevail over shuruh, and shuruh prevail over fatawa — this hierarchy ensures fatwa consistency.

A mufti often encounters apparent contradictions between different Hanafi texts. This lesson establishes a clear rule: the core texts (mutun) are the most authoritative, followed by commentaries (shuruh), and finally fatwa collections. When they conflict, the higher-ranking source governs. This principle, drawn from Fatāwā al-Khayriyyah and al-Bahr al-Rā’iq, is essential for reliable fatwa-giving.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three layers
Recognize the three categories: mutun (core authoritative texts like al-Qudūrī), shurūḥ (commentaries like al-Hidāyah), and fatāwā (collections of fatwas like Fatāwā al-Hindiyyah).
Mutun are the most concise and authoritative.
2
Memorize the hierarchy
When there is conflict, mutun take precedence over shurūḥ, and shurūḥ take precedence over fatāwā.
This order is absolute — never invert.
3
Apply to a conflict scenario
Given a rule in a fatwa collection that contradicts a commentary, you must adopt the commentary's ruling.
If the commentary's ruling also appears in a matn, the matn governs.
4
Recognize authority weight
Understand that mutun represent the most reliable transmission (zahir al-riwayah), while shurūḥ and fatāwā may include later ijtihād or weak narrations.
This hierarchy protects the madhhab's core positions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
متون شروح اور فتاوی کی درجہ بندی: پھر آگے (فتاوی خیریہ میں ) لکھا ہے کہ جب یہ بات معلوم ہو گئی کہ معتبر قول حقیقت میں وہ ہے جس پر متون متفق ہوں تو وہی قول معتمد علیہ اور معمول یہ ہوگا کیونکہ علماء نے تصریح کی ہے کہ جب متون اور فتاویٰ کی باتوں میں تعارض ہو جائے تو قابل اعتماد وہ باتیں ہیں جو متون میں ہیں اسی طرح جو باتیں شروح میں ہیں ان کو فتاوی کے مضامین پر مقدم رکھا جائے گا اھ اور البحر الرائق کی فصل الحبس ( ج ۶، ص ۲۸۵ ) میں ہے: ” اور عمل ان باتوں پر ہے جو متون میں ہیں اس لیے کہ جب متون اور فتاوی کی باتوں میں تعارض ہو جائے تو قابل اعتماد وہ باتیں ہیں جومتون میں ہیں جیسا کہ
Classification of mutūn, shurūḥ, and fatāwā: Then further (in Fatāwā al-Khayriyyah) it is written that when it becomes known that the reliable statement in reality is that upon which the mutūn agree, then that same statement is the one relied upon and acted upon, because the scholars have explicitly stated that when there is conflict between the statements of the mutūn and the fatāwā, the trustworthy statements are those found in the mutūn. Similarly, statements found in the shurūḥ are given precedence over the contents of fatāwā. End. And in al-Bahr al-Rā'iq, chapter on ḥabs (vol. 6, p. 285), it is stated: 'And action is upon those statements that are in the mutūn, because when there is conflict between the statements of the mutūn and the fatāwā, the trustworthy statements are those found in the mutūn, just as...'
Source pages p. 98

Commentary
This passage establishes a clear hierarchy among the standard sources used for fatwa in the Hanafi madhhab. The most authoritative are the mutūn (core authoritative texts). Next come the shurūḥ (commentaries on the mutūn). Last are the fatāwā (collections of fatwas). In case of conflict, the mutūn take precedence over the fatāwā, and the shurūḥ take precedence over the fatāwā. This rule is cited from Fatāwā al-Khayriyyah and supported by al-Bahr al-Rā'iq. The text is incomplete, ending with 'just as...', but the principle is clear. This hierarchy guides muftis in resolving apparent contradictions between the different layers of Hanafi legal literature.

Key Terms
متون (mutūn): The core authoritative texts of the Hanafi madhhab (e.g., al-Qudūrī, al-Mukhtār).
شروح (shurūḥ): Commentaries on the mutūn, which explain and sometimes expand on the rulings.
فتاوی (fatāwā): Collections of fatwas issued by later Hanafi jurists.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the hierarchy of texts in the Hanafi madhhab, which source takes precedence when there is a conflict between a ruling in a fatwa collection and a ruling in a commentary (sharḥ)?
A) The fatwa collection, because it is more recent.
B) The commentary, because it explains the mutūn and the passage explicitly says shurūḥ are given precedence over fatāwā.
C) The mutūn, not the commentary or fatwa.
D) Neither; all are given equal weight.

Key Takeaway
When issuing a fatwa, always defer to the highest authoritative layer: mutūn first, then shurūḥ, then fatāwā.
